库尔特·约翰内森作序

FOREWORD BY KURT JOHANNESSON

哈你将成为一名熟练的扬声器？历史上人们一直在思考这个问题。毕竟，语言是我们传递知识、创建社区以及引导人们的思想、情感和行动的最重要手段。

Hfrom which you become a skilledspeaker?People have pondered this throughout history.After all, language is the most important means we have for conveying knowledge, creating community, and guiding people's thoughts, feelings, and actions.

这一问题在古代尤为突出。当时，公开审判是解决社会纠纷不可或缺的途径。现代审判在很大程度上遵循了希腊和罗马法庭首先发展起来的模式。当时，重大政治问题都是通过希腊议会或罗马元老院的辩论来决定的。然后，人们举行聚会，在聚会上发言者解释仪式或节日的含义。人们不断注意到某些演讲者如何吸引人们倾听，以及他们如何似乎对人们施加一种奇怪的力量。该如何解释这一点呢？演讲是否可能是一门特殊的艺术，有其自身的规则和秘密，只有少数人掌握？

The issue was particularly burning in antiquity.At that time, public trials were an indispensable way to resolve disputes within society.Modern trials largely follow the patterns first developed in the courts of the Greeks and Romans.At that time, major political issues were decided through debates in the Greek assemblies or the Roman Senate.Then, parties were held where speakers would interpret the meaning of the rite or festival.And one constantly noticed how certain speakers made people listen and how they seemed to exercise a strange power over them.How would one explain this?Was speaking possibly a special art, with its own rules and secrets that only a few mastered?

是的，就是这样，有人说。他们还给这种艺术起了个名字，叫“修辞术”。从公元前五世纪开始。出现了特殊学校，人们可以在老师的严格监督下练习发表不同类型的演讲。这是一种艰苦但有效的教学，可以持续很多年。在那里，人们还学到了如何准备和发表精彩演讲的各种规则，这些规则总结了无数演讲者的经验和见解。有时，老师或学生可以将这些规则收集到一本专门的修辞教科书中。

Yes, that's how it is, some said.They also had a name for this art, “rhetoric.”From the 5th century BC.special schools emerged where people could practice giving different kinds of speeches under the critical scrutiny of teachers.It was a tough but also effective teaching that could last for many years.There, one also learned various rules for how to prepare and deliver a good speech, rules that summarized the experiences and insights of countless speakers.Sometimes a teacher or student could collect such rules into a special textbook on rhetoric.

通过这种方式，古代的演说学校积累了大量的专业知识——在我们这个时代几乎没有类似的东西。授课的修辞学家意识到其重要性，并经常批评彼此的理论和方法。但在一点上他们很谦虚：他们一次又一次地打断教学，说没有人能够仅通过学校的练习或类似的规则来获得真正的演讲艺术。它必须通过学习和模仿现实生活中的专业演讲者来学习。因此，人们必须去法院、政治议会和其他有经验和重要公民聚集的地方，了解这个严酷无情的世界对演讲者的要求。

In this way, an immense amount of professional expertise was gathered in the oratory schools of antiquity – there is hardly anything similar in our time.The rhetors who taught were aware of their importance and often criticized each other's theories and methods.But on one point they were humble: time and again they interrupted their teaching and said that no one could reach the true art of oratory just through exercises in a school or such rules.It must be learned by studying and imitating professional speakers in real life.Therefore, one had to go to the courts, to the political assemblies, and other places where experienced and important citizens gathered, to learn the demands placed on speakers in this harsh and merciless world.

一些古代修辞学教科书至今仍保存完好。例如，亚里士多德的修辞他试图以敏锐的分析力将修辞学与辩证法区分开来，并将其塑造成他自己的语言、人和社会理论。这是西塞罗的演说家们，《关于演说家》，一些具有深厚政治经验的人称赞雄辩是一切社会生活、一切文化和人类的基础。这是昆体良的演讲学院，《教授演讲的艺术》，这位著名的修辞学家在十二本书中总结了他的渊博知识。

Some of the ancient textbooks on rhetoric have survived to this day.For example, Aristotle'sRhetoricwhere he tries with analytical acuity to delimit rhetoric from dialectics and shape it into his own theory of language, man and society.It is Cicero'sThe orators,"About the Speaker", where some men with deep experience in politics praise eloquence as the foundation of all social life and all culture and humanity.It is Quintilian'sOratory Institute,"Teaching the Art of Oration", where this famous rhetorician summarizes his vast knowledge in twelve books.

但也有一本小书通常被称为宣告赫伦尼姆，因为它是写给某个叫赫伦尼乌斯的人的。它可能写于公元前 86-82 年。我们不知道它在古代是否具有任何意义。但后来基督教教父们推荐了它。因此，它在中世纪学校教授修辞学时经常被使用，同时还有西塞罗的一部年轻作品，发明或关于论点的“发明”。数百份手稿被保存了下来，当然还有更多的手稿丢失了。文艺复兴时期，人文主义者建立了一种新型的学校，在那里，学生们每天都会进行修辞练习。并且仍在使用宣告赫伦尼姆作为教材或编写新演讲教材时的范本。

But there is also a small book that is usually calledAd Herennium,because it is addressed to a certain Herennius.It was probably written in 86-82 BC.We do not know whether it had any significance in antiquity.But it was then recommended by the Christian church fathers.Therefore, it was constantly used when teaching rhetoric in medieval schools, along with a youthful work by Cicero,The inventionor about the “invention” of arguments.Several hundred manuscripts have been preserved, and of course many more have been lost.During the Renaissance, humanists built a new type of schools, where days were filled with rhetorical exercises.And still usedAd Herenniumas a textbook or as a model when writing new textbooks in public speaking.

当时人们认为这部作品是西塞罗创作的。这当然增加了它的权威。西塞罗被认为是罗马有史以来最伟大的演说家。直到 19 世纪，他的演讲、信件和其他著作在所有西方学校中都被阅读，并在演讲和写作练习中不断被模仿。历史上没有一个人对西方雄辩术产生过如此重大的影响。但现在学者们怀疑西塞罗是否真的写过公元前 50 年。

At this time it was assumed that Cicero wrote the work.That, of course, increased its authority.Cicero was considered the greatest orator the Romans ever had.His speeches, letters and other writings were read in all Western schools until the 19th century and were constantly imitated in speaking and writing exercises.No single man has had such a significant impact on Western eloquence throughout history.But now scholars doubt that Cicero really wroteAd Herennium.

很多事情与他的写作不同。这项发明。西塞罗和不知名的罗马人写了宣告赫伦尼姆他们似乎生活在同一时代，甚至可能上过同一所演讲学校，读过同样的教科书——但两部作品却反映出不同的气质。

A lot of things differ from his writing.The invention.Cicero and the unknown Roman who wroteAd Herenniumapparently lived at the same time, they may even have attended the same oratorical school or read the same textbooks – but different temperaments are reflected in the two works.

但宣告赫伦尼姆各有各的优点。它相对较短。它也很清晰、有教育意义，有时还非常个性化。此外，它还涉及修辞学的各个部分，不同于这项发明。这也许可以解释为什么宣告赫伦尼姆成为西方历史上最重要的教科书之一。而如果你想快速掌握古典修辞学的概况，它仍然是必不可少的。

ButAd Herenniumhas its own merits.It is relatively short.It is also clear, educational and at times very personal.In addition, it deals with all the parts of rhetoric, unlikeThe invention.This perhaps explains whyAd Herenniumbecame one of the most important textbooks in Western history.And it is still indispensable if you want to quickly gain an overview of classical rhetoric.

作者在引言中说，言语有三种类型。他像往常一样给他们打电话。genus iudiciale, 属审议和示范性别。在第一种言论中，你指责或辩护某人或某事；在第二种言论中，你建议或反对某事；在第三种言论中，你赞扬或责备某人或某事。审判中的演讲属于第一种类型，因此在本译本中被称为“法律”演讲或“审判演讲”。有关社会问题和辩论的演讲属于第二种类型，因此被称为“政治”演讲。第三种类型在这里被称为“颂词”演讲。这是在庄严的场合向一大群人用希腊语发表的悼词。颂，或者当人们想以另一种方式来描述一个神、一个人、一个民族、一座城市、一个国家等时。

There are three types of speech, the author says in his introduction.He calls them as usualgenus iudiciale, genus deliberativeanddemonstrative gender.In the first type of speech, you accuse or defend someone or something, in the second you advise or advise against something, and in the third you praise or blame someone or something.The speeches given at a trial belonged to the first genre, which is why they are called “legal” speeches or “trial speeches” in this translation.The speeches given on social issues and debates belonged to the second genre, and they will therefore be called “political” speeches.The third type is called here “panegyric” speeches.It is a eulogy given on a solemn occasion before a large gathering of people, in Greek.panegyric,or when one wanted to characterize a god, a person, a people, a city, a country, etc. in another way.

前两本书完全致力于法律体裁——法庭演讲。这是古典修辞学的典型特征。如上所述，审判在古代公共生活中发挥着重要作用。当时许多伟大的演说家正是通过出现在法庭上而获得了声誉——年轻的西塞罗就是一个著名的例子。在公共演讲学校，人们不断练习在复杂、耸人听闻、看似毫无希望的“案例”中演讲。

The first two books are devoted entirely to the legal genre, court speeches.This is typical of classical rhetoric.As mentioned, trials played a major role in ancient public life.Many of the great orators of the time gained their reputation precisely by appearing in the courts – the young Cicero is a famous example.In public speaking schools, people constantly practiced speaking in complicated, sensational and seemingly hopeless “cases”.

本文首先讨论如何组织此类法庭演讲才能尽可能有效地说服法官和观众。这在修辞学上被称为性格。必须学会通过各种方式进行适当的介绍来引起听众的兴趣和好感，然后介绍背景或进行现代审判中所说的“事实陈述”，然后再进行证据和反驳。此外，重要的是确定法律纠纷的真正内容，地位正如他们常说的那样宣告赫伦尼姆作者选择了不同的术语，宪法。古典修辞学试图发展一种理论，关于在不同类型的法律案件中应该如何辩论。这地位-这一原则成为律师快速有效地找到诉讼程序关键点的重要手段，所有论证都应集中于此。这在现代进程中与两千年前同样重要，而古代地位原则即使对于今天的律师来说，也显然有很大的益处。这两本书还讨论了如何以不同的方式发展、支持和修饰你的论点，以及如何总结和结束你的演讲。

This article first discusses how such court speeches should be structured to convince judges and audiences as effectively as possible.This is called in rhetoricdisposition.One must learn to gain the audience's interest and goodwill with a suitable introduction using various means, then to draw a background or make a "statement of facts" as it is called in modern trials, and then move on to evidence and rebuttal.In addition, it is important to determine what the legal dispute is actually about, itsstatusas they used to say – inAd Herenniumthe author chooses a different term,constitution.Classical rhetoric attempted to develop a theory of how one should argue in different types of legal cases.Thisstatus-The doctrine became an important means for lawyers to quickly and effectively find the crux of a process, the one against which all argumentation should be concentrated.This is as important in the modern process as it was two thousand years ago, and the ancientstatus doctrinecan demonstrably be of great benefit even to today's lawyers.These two books also discuss how to develop, support and embellish your arguments in different ways and how to summarize and conclude your speech.

该演示可能看起来过于技术性和详细。但任何有过审判和法庭经验的人都可以在这里找到许多精确的观察结果，这些观察决定了审判过程的结果，无论是在辩论方面，还是在激发法官和观众情绪的方式方面。在古典修辞学中，双方在法官面前的决斗也被视为所有演讲的原型。因此，人们在演说学校里经常练习辩论各种法律案件。

The presentation may seem overly technical and detailed.But anyone with any experience of trials and courts can find here many precise observations of what determines the outcome of a process, both in terms of the argumentation and the way in which the emotions of the judges and the audience are aroused.Within classical rhetoric, the duel between the parties before the judges was also seen as the prototype of all oratory.Therefore, people always practiced arguing in various legal cases in the oratorical schools.

第三本书首先讨论审议属，“政治”演讲。您必须使用其他类型的论点，主要是那些与效用和荣誉相关的论点。然后，作者展示了当想要赞扬或责备某人时应该使用哪些论点，例如在颂词中。

The third book first deals withgenus delibemtivum,the “political” speeches.There you have to use other types of arguments, mainly those relating to utility and honor.The author then shows which arguments one should use when wanting to praise or blame someone, for example in panegyric speeches.

古典修辞学认为演讲的艺术分为五个部分。在前两本书中，作者主要关注第一部分，即拉丁语部分发明，论证的“发现”或“发明”，但也涉及第二部分或性格。在第三本书中，他现在经历了处置更加系统地。然后他对待行动或通常是第五部分的表演。教科书中经常省略它，因此这些页面特别有趣。它们生动地描绘了古代演讲者如何根据演讲的不同部分以及他们想要表达和激发听众的情感来改变他们的声音和肢体语言。

In classical rhetoric, it is said that the art of speech has five parts.In the first two books, the author focuses mostly on the first part, the one called in Latininvention,the “finding” or “invention” of arguments, but also concerns the second part ordisposition.In the third book he now goes throughdispositionmore systematically.Then he treatsactionor the performance which is usually the fifth part.It is often omitted in textbooks and therefore these pages are particularly interesting.They provide a very vivid picture of how ancient speakers varied their voice and body language according to the different parts of the speech and the emotions they wanted to express and arouse in their listeners.

接下来是该作品最原始的部分之一。这里作者讨论了被称为记忆。这是现存最古老的古代记忆术或记忆术的代表。在那里，演讲的不同部分被想象成“地点”或房间，并且在每个地点或房间中都放置了特别挑选的“图片”。这样，演讲时就不会受稿件的束缚，即使很长的演讲也能记住。

Then follows one of the most original parts of the work.Here the author addresses the part of rhetoric that was calledmemory.This is the oldest preserved representation of the ancient mnemonics or art of memory.There, the different parts of a speech were imagined as “places” or rooms, and in each of these, specially selected “pictures” were placed.In this way, one could speak without being bound by any manuscript and memorize even very long speeches.

因此，第四本书全部致力于修辞学的这一部分，称为演说。这是关于说话者应该如何设计语言本身。这本书无疑是宣告赫伦尼姆，也是最具历史意义的。在引言中，作者提出了一个问题：在教授公开演讲时应该使用自己的例子还是他人的例子？他本人坚定地声称，修辞学家必须自己创造所有例子，以证明他真正掌握了修辞艺术。因此，人们也可以相信接下来的例子确实是作者自己的。但持怀疑态度的学者们表明，他从其他人那里借鉴了很多思想，包括他以居高临下的态度谈论的希腊修辞学家。

The entire fourth book is thus devoted to the part of rhetoric calledelocution.This is about how a speaker should design the language itself.This book is undoubtedly the most original and personal inAd Herennium,and also the one that has gained the greatest historical significance.In the introduction, the author raises a question: should one use one's own or others' examples when teaching public speaking?He himself firmly claims that a rhetorician must create all the examples himself, to prove that he truly masters his art.Therefore, one could also believe that the examples that follow are truly the author's own.But skeptical scholars have shown that he borrowed many from others, including from the Greek rhetoricians whom he otherwise speaks so condescendingly of.

在介绍之后，作者讨论了不同层次的风格，并给出了高级风格、中级风格和低级风格的非常具有说明性的例子。然后，他谈到了是什么让风格变得多样化和富有表现力，即修辞手法和思想手法。这里的演示变得流畅丰富且富有启发性，作者用具有启发性和娱乐性的例子描述了 64 个这样的人物，并讨论了如何以及在何处使用它们。这个特定的部分宣告赫伦尼姆它在学校里受到热烈的阅读，许多未来的诗人、作家、传教士和政治演说家可能在这里第一次发现了这种语言所蕴含的无限可能性和财富。其他修辞学家将这个数字目录视为一种挑战，并试图创建更大、更复杂的数字系统——这在文艺复兴时期尤为常见。

After this introduction, the author discusses different levels of style and gives very illustrative examples of high style, middle style, and low style.He then touches on what makes the style varied and expressive, namely the figures of speech and thought.Here the presentation becomes flowingly rich and inspired, here the author describes 64 such figures with instructive and entertaining examples and discusses how and where they can be used.This particular part ofAd Herenniumcame to be read with great enthusiasm in schools, and many future poets, writers, preachers and political orators probably discovered here for the first time the immeasurable possibilities and riches that the language holds.Other rhetoricians saw this catalog of figures as a challenge and attempted to create even larger and more elaborate systems of figures – this became especially common during the Renaissance.

正是在第四本书中，修辞学史上的一个永恒问题被揭示出来。人们相信希腊人创造了这种艺术。但现在作者说至他不想使用希腊术语，例如数字。他试图在拉丁语中找到与它们对应的词。然后其他罗马修辞学家也会这样做，有时他们选择的术语与我们的作者不同。这在修辞术语上造成了一种巴比伦式的困惑。在那里你可以找到表示同一事物的几个希腊语和拉丁语术语。

It is precisely in the fourth book that an eternal problem in the history of rhetoric is brought to light.It was believed that the Greeks created this art.But now the author says toAd Herennium tohe does not want to use the Greek terms, for example for the figures.He has tried to find equivalents for them in Latin.Then other Roman rhetoricians would do the same, and sometimes they chose different terms than our author.This has created a kind of Babylonian bewilderment in rhetorical terminology.There you can find several Greek and Latin terms for the same thing.

那么应该使用哪个术语？在这个翻译中，我们试图从实际的角度看待这个问题：重要的不是术语本身，而是我们能够尽可能简单、准确地描述语言现象。因此，我们选择了传统中影响最大的术语，无论是希腊语还是拉丁语。有时我们也会选择一个纯粹的瑞典语术语，因为它可以完全涵盖古代概念的含义。所有这些都在注释中进行了详细的评论。书的后面还有一个索引，其中包括拉丁原文的技术术语。例如，如果您对隐喻感兴趣，您可以在主题索引中找到对特定部分的引用。宣告赫伦尼姆同时看到作者用拉丁词翻译了这个希腊词翻译。

Which term should be used then?In this translation we have tried to look at the problem practically: what is important is not the terms as such, but that we can describe linguistic phenomena as simply and accurately as possible.Therefore, we have chosen the term that has had the most impact in the tradition, whether it is Greek or Latin.Sometimes we have also chosen a purely Swedish term when it fully covers the meaning of the ancient concept.All of this is commented on in detail in the notes.At the back of the book there is also an index that includes the technical terms of the Latin original.For example, if you are interested in metaphors, you can find a reference to a specific section in the subject index.Ad Herenniumand at the same time see that the author translated this Greek term with the Latin wordtranslation.

如今，人们谈论欧洲的话题很多。是什么创建了欧洲共同体？当然，这其中有贸易、交通、宗教、神话和历史记忆，但还有一个事实，那就是几个世纪以来，所有欧洲国家的学校都使用相同的教科书。宣告赫伦尼姆属于他们。无数的男学生和中学生都曾为此奋斗过。但与此同时，无论他们生活在波兰、瑞典、英国还是意大利，他们都以同样的方式学习说和写拉丁语。拉丁语将欧洲统一起来。当人们用白话说话或写作时，他们常常试图按照在拉丁语雄辩中所学到的模式和理念来塑造词语和句子。这在所有欧洲语言中都留下了明显的痕迹。这也许可以解释为什么我们发现与欧洲人交流比与其他文化的人交流更容易。我们都是最终以拉丁语和古典修辞为基础的语言社区的一部分。

There is a lot of talk about Europe today.What created the European Community?Certainly there is trade, transportation, religion, myths and historical memories – but also the fact that for many centuries and in all European countries the same textbooks have been used in schools.Ad Herenniumbelongs to them.Countless schoolboys and students had to struggle with it.But at the same time, they learned to speak and write Latin in the same way, whether they lived in Poland, Sweden, England or Italy.Latin held Europe together.And when people then spoke or wrote in the vernacular, they often tried to shape the words and sentences according to the patterns and ideals learned in Latin eloquence.This has left unmistakable traces in all European languages.And this may explain why we find it easier to communicate with Europeans than with people from other cultures.We are all part of a linguistic community that ultimately rests on Latin and classical rhetoric.

所以听着宣告赫伦尼姆欧洲文学中最受欢迎的书籍。它从未被翻译成瑞典语。以前没有必要；直到 19 世纪，受过教育的瑞典人阅读拉丁文就和阅读英文一样自由。但我们并不像我们的父辈那样精通拉丁语，因此我们可能需要这种翻译。在这里，我们发现了两千年来整个欧洲文化所特有的语言观点。这与我们的文化根源有关。但在这里，我们也发现了大量关于如何使用语言说服他人的深刻见解——这一直是修辞艺术的核心。这种艺术在今天和在古代同样重要。

So listenAd Herenniumto the most read books in European literature.It has never been translated into Swedish.It wasn't necessary before; up until the 19th century, educated Swedes read Latin about as freely as we read something in English.But we are not as proficient in Latin as our fathers and therefore we may need this translation.Here we find the view of language that has characterized the entire European culture for two thousand years.It's about our cultural roots.But here we also find a wealth of insightful observations about how to use language to persuade people – this has always been the core of the art of rhetoric.And that art is as important today as it was in antiquity.

库尔特·约翰内森

Kurt Johannesson

译者序

TRANSLATOR'S FOREWORD

岛拉丁原文的翻译（其标题不详，但被认为是依据 racené dicendi ad C。 赫伦尼姆，《致盖乌斯·赫伦尼乌斯论演说理论》一书基于对多个版本的比较，即哈利·卡普兰 (Harry Caplan) 于 1954 年在洛布古典图书馆出版的版本、温弗里德·特里利奇 (Winfried Trillitzsch) 于 1964 年在托伊布纳图书馆出版的根据弗里德里希·马克思 (Friedrich Marx) 1923 年改编的版本，以及盖伊·阿查德 (Guillaume Budé) 于 1989 年在法国大学收藏馆出版的版本。然后根据 Anton Hafner 的修辞学和修辞学的基本原理（欧洲 Hochschulschriften，Reihe XV，Band 45，1989）。阿查德对马克思提出了一些批评（他对整个文本的看法得到了卡普兰和特里利奇的赞同），但哈夫纳在对同年出版的手稿传统的研究中走得更远，其中部分内容很难分析。他的工作为资料评估奠定了新的、稳定的基础。如果我的翻译在上述版本中没有对应的版本，那主要是因为我吸收了哈夫纳的文本批判结果，然而，应该补充的是，这对文本内容的影响很小。哈夫纳在很多地方都指出了所有手稿中常见的原型错误，并指出了中世纪对文本改进的尝试，尽管他自己无法重建原始措辞。在这些情况下，翻译是基于中世纪的阅读，但在评论中对此事进行了说明。在少数情况下，与哈夫纳不同，我认为中世纪的修订是正确的，因此我将其用作翻译的基础，而没有发表评论。有几次，我自己发现自己被迫背离手稿中给出的文本，这些文本已被以前的出版商接受，但哈夫纳没有对其进行评论。

ISLANDthe translation of the Latin original (whose title is unknown but has been assumed to beOn the ratione dicendi ad C. Herennium,“To Gaius Herennius on the Theory of Oratory”) is based on a comparison between several editions, namely Harry Caplan's edition in The Loeb Classical Library from 1954, the adaptation of Friedrich Marx's edition from 1923 published by Winfried Trillitzsch in 1964 in the Bibliotheca Teubneriana, and Guy Achard's edition from 1989 in the Collection des universités de France publiée sous le patronage de l'Association Guillaume Budé.The result has then been reviewed against Anton Hafner'sUntersuchungen zur Ueberlieferungsgeschichte der Rhetorik ad Herennium(European Hochschulschriften, Reihe XV, Band 45, 1989).Achard directs some criticism at Marx (whose view of the text as a whole is echoed by both Caplan and Trillitzsch), but Hafner goes considerably further in his investigation of the manuscript tradition, which is in part very difficult to analyze, published the same year.His work lays a new and stable foundation for the evaluation of sources.When my translation has no equivalent in the aforementioned editions, it is also essentially due to the fact that I have incorporated Hafner's text-critical results, which, however – it should be added – only marginally affects the content of the text.There are a number of places where Hafner both points out errors in the archetype common to all manuscripts and identifies medieval attempts at textual improvement, although without being able to reconstruct the original wording himself.In those cases, the translation is based on the medieval reading, but with a note about the matter in the commentary.In a few cases, where, unlike Hafner, I believe that the medieval emendation is correct, I have used it as the basis for the translation without comment.On a few occasions, I myself have found myself compelled to depart from a text given in the manuscripts, accepted by previous publishers and uncommented by Hafner.

至于第四本书中各种修辞手法和思想手法的名称，我们的匿名作者指出（IV：10），他自己编造了与希腊技术术语相对应的拉丁语词。但在瑞典文体传统中，主要使用的不是拉丁语名称，而是希腊语名称；我们说寓言、强调、隐喻等等。我部分地适应了这一传统，并且经常更喜欢使用希腊术语，但有几个次为了清楚起见，我创造了瑞典语术语或使用了拉丁语借词。关于修辞术语的更多信息可以在现代修辞文献中找到，例如托尔莫德·艾德斯修辞词汇（1990）和库尔特·约翰内森的修辞或说服的艺术（2003 [1990]）；这两部作品中都有 b.ö。丰富地引用了其他相关文献。通过查阅书末的索引，读者可以轻松确定拉丁原文中与特殊修辞表达（包括文体和其他方面）对应的词语。它还提供了拉丁语修辞文献中出现的其他技术术语的一些定义和信息。

As for the designations of the various figures of speech and thought in the fourth book, our anonymous author points out (IV:10) that he himself has fabricated Latin equivalents for the Greek technical terms.But in Swedish stylistic tradition, it is not Latin but Greek terms that have primarily been used; we say allegory, emphasis, metaphor, etc.I have partly adapted to that tradition and often preferred the Greek technical terms, but severaltimesFor the sake of clarity, I have coined Swedish terms or used Latin loanwords.Further information on rhetorical terminology can be found in modern rhetorical literature such asTormod EidesRhetorical lexicon(1990) and Kurt Johannesson'sRhetoric or the art of persuasion(2003 [1990]); in both of these works there is B.E.rich in references to other relevant literature.The reader can easily determine what equivalents the Latin original has for special rhetorical expressions, both stylistic and otherwise, by consulting the index at the end of the book.It also provides some definitions and information about other technical terms that appear in Latin-language rhetorical literature.

赫伦尼乌斯的修辞风格有时有些生硬，与罗马这一流派的杰出作家西塞罗相比，他显然是无法相比的。特别是在个别书籍的介绍和结尾，呈现方式有时变得几乎是做作的，并且不乏纯粹的重新整理。另一方面，第四本书中的许多例子都以自由且文学有效的方式设计，并且在同一本书中，作者展现了对风格细微差别的良好听觉。我的翻译也旨在反映拉丁原文的风格变化。

The style of Herennius' rhetoric is sometimes somewhat heavy-handed, and the author certainly does not bear comparison with Cicero, Rome's foremost writer in the genre.Especially in the introductions and endings of the individual books, the presentation sometimes becomes almost contrived, and there is no shortage of pure rehash.On the other hand, many of the examples in the fourth book are designed in a free and literary effective way, and in the same book the author reveals a good ear for stylistic nuances.My translation aims to also reflect the stylistic shifts in the original Latin text.

我要向担任我国唯一修辞学教授的库尔特·约翰内森 (Kurt Johannesson) 表示感谢，感谢他在翻译和评论中所做的大量改进和补充。我的前任学生、已故普通法教授托尔·斯特伦伯格 (Tore Strömberg) 审阅了前三本书，并在其中调整了多处法律词汇，以便现代瑞典法律从业者也能识别。我很遗憾，我无法再向他表达我对他所给予的出色帮助的谢意。名誉教授。北欧语言学家 Gösta Holm 对第四本书提出了宝贵的评论。对于前三本书的许多改进，我也要感谢我的兄弟 b。议员 Gunnar Bergh。

To Professor Kurt Johannesson, holder of the country's only chair in rhetoric, my thanks go out for a large number of improvements and additions, both in the translation and in the comments.My exstudent, the late professor of general law Tore Strömberg, has reviewed the first three books and in doing so has adjusted the legal vocabulary in a number of places so that it should also be recognizable to a modern Swedish practitioner.I regret that my thanks for his excellent help can no longer reach him.Professor Emeritus.in Nordic languages ​​Gösta Holm has made valuable comments on the fourth book.For a number of improvements in the first three books, I am also indebted to my brother, b.Councillor Gunnar Bergh.

Birger Bergh，隆德 1993

Birger Bergh, Lund 1993

In the second edition, some corrections have been made to the text, while the notes have undergone a re-editing.

第一卷

第一书

BOOK I

LIBER PRIMUS

公元一世纪：1-27年

AD HERENNIUM I:1-27

1由于个人事务繁忙，我几乎没有足够的时间进行学术研究，而我习惯将有限的空闲时间主要用于哲学研究。以免您认为我对您关心的问题缺乏兴趣，或者我逃避努力本身，但我仍然同意您的愿望，盖乌斯·赫伦尼乌斯，写一本关于修辞理论的著作。我以更大的热情对待这项任务，因为我很清楚你想要获得修辞知识的理由很充分。如果一个人拥有丰富多样、自由的自我表达方式，那么他将获得不少好处，但前提是这种能力符合真正的洞察力和严格的自我反省的要求。1这也是为什么我避免以不必要的假设来讨论希腊作家所提出的主题的原因。因为他们担心自己看起来缺乏洞察力，所以他们把注意力集中在与主题毫无关系的问题上，只是为了让演讲的艺术看起来更难掌握。另一方面，我只处理我认为属于修辞理论的事情。与其他人不同，我拿起笔来并不是因为对金钱的渴望，也不是因为野心，而是为了通过无私的牺牲为你们谋福利。但为了避免冗长，我现在就开始我的演讲。在此之前，我只想提醒大家一件事，那就是没有不断练习口语的理论知识是没有用的。我这样说是为了让您意识到我在这里提供的理论教学必须辅以实际应用。

1Busy as I am with personal matters, I barely have enough time for scholarly studies, and the modest free time that is available to me, as is my habit, I devote primarily to philosophy.Lest you think that I lack interest in a matter that is close to your heart or that I shun the effort itself, I have nevertheless agreed to your wish, Gaius Herennius, to write a work on the theory of rhetoric.I tackled this task with all the greater enthusiasm, as I was well aware that you had good reasons for wanting to acquire knowledge of rhetoric.There are no insignificant advantages that follow if one possesses a richly varied and free way of expressing oneself, provided, however, that this ability conforms to the requirements of true insight and strict self-reflection.1Herein also lies the reason why I have refrained from treating subjects which Greek writers have brought up for discussion with unwarranted presumption.For in their fear of appearing less insightful, they have drawn attention to issues that lack any relevance to the subject, just so that the art of speaking may appear more difficult to acquire.I, on the other hand, have only dealt with things that, in my view, belong to the theory of rhetoric.Unlike what is the case with others, it is neither the desire for money nor ambition that has made me take up the pen, but my intention is to do you good through selfless sacrifice.But to avoid verbosity, I will now begin my presentation.Before that, let me just remind you of one thing, namely that theoretical knowledge without constant practice in speaking is of little use.This is said so that you will realize that the theoretical teaching I provide here must be supplemented with practical application.

2演讲者的任务是能够就根据习俗和法律属于公开辩论的话题进行演讲，并以此争取尽可能多的听众的认可。演讲者应该承担三类案件：颂言语[指示类]，政治的演讲[审议性言论]以及合法的演讲[司法属]。2颂词是指对某个人的赞扬或责备。政治演讲是关于建议的，目的是劝告或劝阻。法律演讲源于诉讼，涉及指控、提出法律主张或为某人或某事辩护。现在我将阐明演讲者必须掌握哪些个别要素，然后说明如何处理上述情况。

2The speaker's task is to be able to speak on topics that, according to custom and law, belong in public debate, and he shall thereby seek to win as much approval as possible among his audience.There are three types of cases that the speaker should undertake:panegyricspeech [genus demonstrative],politicalspeech [genus deliberativum] as well aslegalspeech [judiciale genus].2Panegyric speeches refer to the praise or blame of a particular person.Political speeches are about advice and are intended to advise or discourage.Legal speeches have their roots in litigation and involve accusing, making legal claims, or defending someone or something.I will now clarify which individual elements the speaker must master and then show how the aforementioned cases should be handled.

3因此，演讲者必须能够查找参数[inventio]，赋予演讲正确的含义处置[处置] 和语言设计[雄辩] 和记住[备忘录]和履行它[动作/发音]。3寻找论据意味着思考真实或可能的事情，以使事情变得可信。处置是对材料的安排和分配；它提供了有关演讲各个部分应放在哪里的说明。语言设计的目的是找到适合论点的适当的单词和句子。记忆涉及对内容、语言和结构的牢固记忆。表演需要用令人愉悦的方式运用声音、面部表情和手势。

3The speaker must therefore be able tofind arguments[inventio], give the speech the right meaningdisposition[disposition] andlinguistic design[eloquence] andmemorize[memorandum] andperformit [action/pronunciation].3Finding arguments means thinking up true or probable things that are intended to make the matter credible.Outline is the arrangement and distribution of the material; it provides instructions on where each individual part of the speech should be placed.The linguistic design aims to find appropriate words and sentences adapted to the argument.Memorization involves the firm retention in memory of content, language, and structure.The performance requires a pleasant way of using voice, facial expressions and gestures.

有三条路可以掌握这一切：理论[年]，模仿[模仿] 和锻炼[锻炼]。理论是指提供特定系统的说话方法的一套规则。模仿，基于深思熟虑的方法，使我们能够效仿某些榜样。练习就是不断练习说话​​，养成说话的习惯。

Three paths lead to mastery of all this:theory[year],imitation[imitation] andexercise[exercise].Theory refers to the set of rules that provide a specific systematic method of speaking.Imitation, based on a well-thought-out method, enables us to emulate certain role models.Practice is the constant practice and habit of speaking.

因此，我澄清了哪些情况演讲者必须处理哪些部分以及他必须具备哪些能力，因此，现在我解释一下演讲者应该如何以有条不紊的正确方式履行他的职责似乎是合适的。

Thus I have clarified which casesthe speakerhas to deal with and in which parts he must possess competence, and it therefore seems appropriate that I now explain how the speaker should proceed to fulfill his duties in a methodically correct manner.

4形成论点的工作涉及演讲的所有六个部分，即：介绍[序言]，事实陈述[旁白]，澄清立场[分配]，证据[确认]，反驳[反驳] 和终止[结论]。引言是演讲的开始，它吸引听众倾听。事实陈述说明了已经发生或可以假定已经发生的事件。澄清立场意味着我们澄清什么是同意的，什么是不同意的，并且我们传达后续陈述的要点。在证据中，我们提出我们的论点并断言其正确性。反驳意味着驳斥对手的论点。结论是演讲的最后部分，按照修辞规则设计。

4The work of shaping the argument touches on all six parts of which a speech consists, i.e.introduction[exordium],statement of fact[narration],clarification of position[division],evidence[confirmation],refutation[confutation] andtermination[conclusion].Introduction is the beginning of the speech, which gets the audience to listen.The factual statement accounts for events that have occurred or can be assumed to have occurred.Clarifying our position means that we clarify what is agreed upon and what is not agreed upon, and that we communicate the main points for the subsequent presentation.In the evidence, we present our arguments and assert their correctness.Refutation means tearing apart your opponent's arguments.The conclusion is the last part of the speech, designed in accordance with the rules of rhetoric.

为了使主题更容易理解，我在解释演讲者的要求时提到了演讲的各个部分及其在论证清单中的作用。因此，首先讨论演讲的开场白可能是合适的。

In order to make the subject easier to understand, I mentioned the parts of the speech and their role in the argument inventory in connection with the explanation of what is required of the speaker.It may therefore be appropriate to begin by discussing the opening of the speech.

5当案件本身确定后，为了做出最好的介绍[开场白]，应该考虑案件的性质。案件类型有四种：可敬[genus causae honestum]，即可耻[属 causae turpe]，即不清楚[属 causae dubium] 以及琐碎的[属卑微原因]。我们要么捍卫每个人认为值得捍卫的东西，要么攻击每个人认为应该攻击的东西，这种情况被认为是值得尊敬的，例如保卫英雄或攻击叛徒。不光彩指的是攻击值得尊敬的事物或维护不光彩的事物的情况。不清楚的情况一方面值得尊敬，另一方面又不光彩。琐碎案件是指提出一些不重要的问题供审议的案件。

5When the case itself is established, in order to make the best possible introduction [exordium], one should consider its character.There are four types of cases:respectable[genus causae honestum], thatdisgraceful[genus causae turpe], thatunclear[genus causae dubium] and thattrivial[genus causae humile].The kind of case in which we either defend what everyone thinks deserves to be defended or attack what everyone thinks should be attacked is considered respectable, e.g.defense of a hero or attack on a traitor.By dishonor is meant the case where something respectable is attacked or something dishonorable is defended.Unclear is a case that is partly respectable, partly dishonorable.A trivial case is one in which some insignificant issue is brought up for consideration.

6鉴于此，引言的格式应根据案件的性质进行调整。有两种类型的介绍：直接开始[principium]，在希腊语中称为晋升，并且谨慎的态度[insinuatio]，所谓的以弗得。直接的开头意味着您试图让听众毫不犹豫地倾向于倾听。目标是能够依靠听众细心、善于教导和仁慈。如果案例类型不明确，则引言应侧重于创建仁4，这样案件中不光彩的部分就不会给我们带来任何问题。但如果案件是琐碎的，就应该集中精力吸引注意力。然而，如果案件属于不光彩的类别，则应采取谨慎的态度，我将在后面讨论。5例外情况是，当我们想出某种办法来攻击对方并由此获得善意时。最后，如果情况值得尊敬，那么直接开始也无妨。对于前一种选择，我们应该要么说明为什么这个案例是值得尊敬的，要么简要说明我们打算讨论的内容。但如果选择不直接开场，那么演讲开始时就应该引用一些法律、一些文件或一些支持我们事业的论点。

6In light of this, the format of the introduction should be adapted to the nature of the case.There are then two types of introduction: thedirect beginning[principium], which in Greek is calledpromotion,and thatcautious approach[insinuatio], the so-calledephod.A direct beginning means that you try to make the listener inclined to listen without hesitation.The aim is to be able to count on listeners who areattentive, teachableandbenevolent.If the case is of the unclear type, the introduction should focus on creatingbenevolence4, so that the parts of the case that are dishonorable will not have to cause us any problems.But if the case is of the trivial kind, one should focus on attracting attention.If, however, the case falls into the dishonorable category, the cautious approach should be applied, which I will discuss later.5An exception is when we have come up with something that makes it possible for us to attack the other party and thereby achieve goodwill.If, finally, the case is of the respectable kind, one can just as well use a direct beginning as not to.In the former option, one should either show why the case is respectable, or briefly state what we intend to discuss.But if one chooses to refrain from starting directly, one should begin the speech by quoting some law, citing some document, or some argument that supports our cause.

7由于我们的目标是让听众可教[温顺]，仁慈[仁慈] 和细心[adtentus]，我现在将逐点揭示如何实现这一目标。如果我们对案例进行简要概述并成功吸引他们的注意力，我们就能获得可教的听众：因为愿意认真倾听的人是可教的。如果我们承诺讨论重要、新颖、不寻常的事情，或者对社会、听众本身或对不朽神灵的崇拜很重要的事情，我们就会引起他们的注意；如果我们要求他们认真倾听，并列出我们打算讨论的要点，那么效果会更好。

7Since our aim is for the listener to beteachable[docile],benevolent[benevolent] andattentive[adtentus], I will now reveal point by point how this can be achieved.We can get a teachable audience if we give a brief summary of the case and succeed in capturing their attention: for he is teachable who is willing to listen attentively.We gain their attention if we promise to discuss important, new, and unusual matters, or those that are of importance to society, to the listeners themselves, or to the worship of the immortal gods; further, if we ask them to listen attentively and if we list the points we intend to treat.

8我们可以通过四种方式获得愿意听的听众：我们自己，从交易对手方，从观众或来自他们自己这个问题。

8We can gain a willing audience in four ways: by starting fromourselves,fromthe counterparty,fromthe audienceor from themselvesthe issue.

（1）从自身出发，不带傲慢地强调自己的责任感，阐明自己对国家、亲属、朋友或听众的行为，并提及<…>6但前提是所有这些都与当前的问题有一定关联；进一步说，如果我们讲述我们的逆境、我们的贫穷、我们的孤独和不幸，如果我们乞求听众的帮助，同时强调我们不想把希望寄托在他们以外的任何人身上。

(1) Starting from our own person, we assure ourselves of goodwill if we emphasize without arrogance our sense of duty and clarify how we have acted towards the state, our relatives, our friends or the audience themselves, and if we refer to<…>6, provided, however, that all of this has some relevance to the issue at hand; furthermore, if we tell of our adversities, our poverty, our loneliness and misfortune, and if we beg for the help of the audience, while emphasizing that we have not wanted to place our hope in anyone other than them.

（2）从我们的对手开始，如果我们成功地激起对他们的仇恨、厌恶或蔑视，我们就获得了善意。如果我们指出他们犯下的任何卑鄙、傲慢、不忠诚、残忍、傲慢、恶意或犯罪行为，我们就会让他们陷入仇恨之中。如果我们指出对手的暴力行为、权力地位、阴谋、财富、放荡、贵族出身和客户，就会引起对手的怨恨。7、宾客友谊关系、友谊和婚姻关系，如果我们由此表明他们更依赖这些而不是真相。如果我们强调对手的懒惰、懦弱、缺乏主动性和奢侈的生活方式，我们就会让他们遭受蔑视。

(2) Starting from the person of our opponents, we achieve goodwill if we succeed in evoking hatred, dislike, or contempt for them.We expose them to hatred if we point out any low-minded, arrogant, faithless, cruel, insolent, malicious or criminal act they have committed.We arouse resentment towards our opponents if we point out their violent behavior, their position of power, intrigues, wealth, licentiousness, noble birth, their clients.7, guest-friendship relationships, friendship and marriage ties, and if we thereby reveal that they rely more on such than on the truth.We create contempt for our opponents if we highlight their laziness, cowardice, lack of initiative, and lavish lifestyle.

（3）从听众本人出发，回忆他们在以往的决策中表现出来的勇气、智慧、人性和宽宏大量，揭示他们享有的声誉和人们对他们的决定的期待，就能激起他们的善意。

(3) Starting from the person of the audience, goodwill is aroused if we recall the courage, wisdom, humanity and magnanimity they have shown in previous decisions, as well as if we reveal the reputation they enjoy and the interest with which their decision is awaited.

（4）从实际问题出发，用赞扬的言辞陈述自己的观点，用轻蔑和贬低的言辞谈论对方的观点，就能使听者产生善意。

(4) Starting from the actual issue, we will make the listener benevolent if we present our own case in praiseworthy terms but speak contemptuously and disparagingly of the other party's.

9接下来，我们将讨论谨慎的方法。有三种情况不能适用直接开头，需要仔细考虑。部分原因是因为我们的情况属于这种情况不光彩的战斗，IE。当实际问题使听众与我们疏远时，或者当听众似乎变得确信那些先前为对方发言的人，最后当听众变得疲劳的听取前面发言者的发言。

9Next, the cautious approach will be discussed.There are three situations where one cannot apply the direct beginning, and they deserve careful consideration.This is partly because our case belongs to itdishonorable battle,i.e.when the actual issue distances the listener from us, and partly when the listener appears to have becomeconvincedof those who have previously spoken for the opposing side, and finally when the listener has becometiredfrom listening to the previous speakers.

（1）如果案件不光彩，我们可以按照如下思路进行引言。我们强调，应该关注的是人而不是行为，我们自己与对方认为已经发生的行为保持距离，并认为这些行为是不值得的或可耻的。经过长时间的阐述这个主题之后，我们将证明我们不能责怪任何此类事情。8或者我们回想一下其他人对类似案件的评估，无论它是完全相似还是范围较小或较大，以便逐步接近我们自己的案件并确定相似性。如果我们宣称无意讨论另一方或任何特定问题，但却以隐晦的方式进行讨论，也会取得同样的结果。

(1) If the case is dishonorable, we can formulate the introduction along the following lines.We emphasize that it is the person and not the action that should be the focus, that we ourselves distance ourselves from the actions that the opposing side believes have been committed and that these are unworthy or shameful.After having developed this theme for a long time, we shall show that nothing of the kind can be blamed on us.8Or we recall the assessment that some have made of a similar case, whether it was completely similar or of smaller or larger scope, in order to step by step approach our own case and establish the similarity.We achieve the same result if we declare that we have no intention of discussing either the other party or any particular issue but nevertheless do so in veiled terms.

10（2）如果听者已经被说服，即如果对方通过演讲赢得了听众的信任——我们可以很容易地确定这一点，因为我们并非不知道信任通常是如何产生的——如果我们因此期望信任已经得到激发，那么我们应该以以下方式谨慎处理此案。我们承诺首先解决对方认为最有力的支持点。我们从对方的陈述开始，最好是刚刚做出的陈述，然后假装犹豫不决，不知道我们应该说什么或者应该首先解决哪一点。

10(2) If the listener has been convinced, i.e.If the opposing party has gained the audience's trust through his speech - which we can easily ascertain, since we are not unaware of how trust is normally created - if we therefore expect that trust has been aroused, we should cautiously approach the case in the following way.We promise to address the point that the opposing party considers to be its strongest support first.We start from a statement by the opposing side, preferably something that has just been made, but then pretend to be indecisive and wondering what we should say or which point we should address first.

(3) 如果听众听腻了，可以讲一些能引人发笑的内容，比如一个寓言、一个可信的故事、一个恶搞的戏仿、一些讽刺或模棱两可的陈述、一个典故、一个嘲弄或一些愚蠢的表述、一种夸张、一种重复、一种文字游戏——一些出乎意料的事情、一个比喻、一个惊喜、一个历史故事、一首诗，或者向听众中的某个人走去，或者朝另一个方向微笑表示同意。或者，我们可以说，我们打算发表一次与计划不同的演讲，并且不会像其他人通常那样表达我们的话。然后我们可以简要解释其他发言者通常做什么以及我们自己打算做什么。

(3) If the audience has grown weary of listening, one begins with something that can provoke laughter, a fable, a credible story, a wicked parody, some ironic or ambiguous statement, an allusion, a mockery or some foolish formulation, an exaggeration, a repetition, a play on words – something that defies all expectation, a comparison, a surprise, a story from history, a verse, or one goes out to someone in the audience or smiles in agreement in some other direction.Alternatively, we can say that we intend to give a different speech than we planned and not put our words in the same way as others usually do.We can then briefly explain what other speakers usually do and what we ourselves intend to do.

11谨慎的方法和直接开始之间存在以下区别。直接的开始应该是我们毫不犹豫地尝试并公开使用我给出指示的方法，使听众变得仁慈、细心或可教，而谨慎的方法应该是我们使用伪装的词语和伪装来达到同样的目的。我们的想法是，这样我们就能够像第一种情况一样轻松地继续演讲。上述三个目标，即：在整个演讲过程中，听众向我们展示持续的关注、学习和善意当然是应该追求的目标，但在演讲开始时尤其应该牢记这一点。

11There is the following difference between the cautious approach and a direct start.The direct beginning should be such that we try, without hesitation and with open use of the methods I have given instructions, to make the listener either benevolent or attentive or teachable, while the cautious approach should be such that we use disguised words and pretense for the same purpose.The idea is that we should then be able to continue the speech as easily as in the first case.The three aforementioned objectives, viz.The aim of the listener showing us constant attention, learning, and goodwill should certainly be pursued throughout the speech, but they should be especially kept in mind at the beginning of the speech.

为了避免我们犯错误设计引言的风险，我现在将解释必须避免哪些错误。在介绍时，必须保证语言平静，用词符合常用用法，使演讲给人一种没有准备的印象。可以用于几种情况的介绍不正确；据说这是平庸的。同样不正确的是对方可以同样有利地使用的介绍；这被称为日常。对方可能用来对付你的引言也是不正确的，这种引言太过复杂或太长，看起来并非源于实际问题，与事实的陈述没有自然联系，最终无法让听众感到友善、有启发或专心。介绍就到这里吧。现在让我们来回顾一下事实。

So that we do not run the risk of ever designing the introduction incorrectly, I will now explain which mistakes must be avoided.During the introduction, you must ensure that the language is calm and that the choice of words follows common usage, so that the speech gives the impression of being unprepared.The introduction that can be used in several cases is incorrect; it is said to be banal.Likewise, the introduction that could be used with equal advantage by the opposing party is incorrect; it is called commonplace.Also incorrect is the introduction that the other party may use against you, one that is too elaborate or too long, one that does not appear to have arisen from the actual issue in such a way that it has a natural connection with the presentation of the facts, and finally one that is unable to make the listener either benevolent, instructive, or attentive.That's enough about the introduction.Let us now turn to the presentation of the facts.

12有三种不同类型的叙述。一是当我们叙述一系列事件时，我们试图利用每一个细节来为自己谋利，以期取得胜利；此类型包括以判决方式裁决的案件。第二种是我们有时在演讲中插入一些话来增加我们的可信度，或者引起对方的怀疑，或者使对方离题，或者做一些准备。第三种类型虽然不属于诉讼范围，但却提供了一个练习的机会，旨在提高我们在实际法律案件中运用上述类型的陈述的能力。

12There are three different types of narrative.One is when, in our account of a course of events, we try to exploit every detail to our advantage with the aim of emerging victorious; this type includes cases that are decided by verdict.The second type is the one we sometimes insert into a speech to increase our credibility, to make the other party suspicious, to make a digression, or to prepare something.The third type, although it falls outside the scope of litigation, nevertheless provides an opportunity for exercises designed to improve our ability to apply the above-mentioned types of presentation in real legal cases.

十三这种事实陈述有两种类型：一种涉及事件另一个人们。

13There are two types of this type of factual presentation: one concernseventsand the otherpeople.

（1）适用于事件叙述的类型分为三类：寓言[寓言]，历史[历史] 和故事[争论]。寓言讲述的事情既不真实也不太可能发生，例如悲剧情节。历史指的是在我们这个时代之前很久就已经发生过的事情。故事讲述了一些可能发生的事情，例如喜剧的情节。

(1) The type that applies to the account of events breaks down into three types:fable[fable],history[history] andstory[argument].The fable tells about things that are neither true nor probable, e.g.the plot of tragedies.History refers to something that has actually occurred, but long before our time.The story recounts something invented that could have happened, e.g.the plot of comedies.

（2）描写人物的，要写得生动活泼，表现人物的严肃与温柔、希望与恐惧、怀疑与憧憬、伪装与怜悯等不同的情绪，以及人生的沧桑、变幻莫测的厄运、突如其来的喜事、圆满的结局等各种境遇。但这些事情应该以练习的形式来对待。现在我将解释如何在实际案例中进行事实陈述。

(2) The kind of representation that concerns people should be distinguished by liveliness in style and describe different moods such as severity and gentleness, hope and fear, distrust and longing, pretense and pity, and all the vicissitudes of life such as vicissitudes of fate, an unexpected misfortune, a sudden joyful event or a happy outcome.But these things should be treated in the form of exercises.I will now explain how a factual presentation should be carried out in real cases.

14事实陈述必须满足三个要求：它必须简短、清晰和可能。既然我们知道了这些是必须实现的目标，那么就有必要学习实际的方法。

14The factual statement must meet three requirements: it must beshort, clearandlikely.Now that we know that these are the goals that must be achieved, it is necessary to learn the actual method.

（1）如果我们从讲述必要内容开始，如果我们不试图从头开始描述某件事，如果我们概括地而不是详细地介绍问题，如果我们不描述某件事的最终结果而只满足于必要内容，如果我们不离题并且不偏离我们已经开始的论述，如果我们以这样一种方式呈现事件过程的结果，即人们也可以推断出之前发生的事情，即使我们没有明确地这么说。那么，我们可以简洁地陈述事实。例如，如果我说我从外省回来，其实我也去过外省。总的来说，最好不仅忽略那些可能对事业有害的事情，而且忽略那些既无害也无益的事情。我们还应该注意不要重复说同一句话。次尤其是立即重复我们刚才说过的话，例如：

(1) We can make the presentation of the facts brief if we begin by telling what is necessary, if we refrain from trying to describe something from the very beginning, if we present the matter in broad outlines and not in detail, if we refrain from describing something to its ultimate end but are content with what is necessary, if we refrain from digressions and do not stray from the exposition we have begun, and if we present the result of a course of events in such a way that one can also infer what happened before, even though we have not explicitly said so.If I, for example,says that I have returned from the province, one must realize that I have also traveled to the province.In general, it is better to ignore not only what may be detrimental to the cause, but also what neither harms nor benefits it.We should also be careful not to say the same thing two or more times.timesand especially to immediately repeat something we have just said, according to the example:

一天傍晚，西蒙从雅典抵达麦加拉。

One evening Simo arrived in Megara from Athens.

随后，他在麦加拉设下埋伏，准备袭击一名女孩。

In Megara he then laid an ambush for a girl.

但他设下埋伏后，强行将她带至那里。9

But after he had laid an ambush, he took her there by force.9

15（2）如果我们从最先发生的事情开始，并观察事情实际发生或看似发生的顺序，我们对事实的陈述就会很清楚。我们必须确保我们的陈述不会变得混乱、复杂或含糊，我们不会改变主题，我们不会从头开始或走得太远，而且我们也不会忽略与问题相关的任何内容。如果我们遵循关于简洁性的指示，这也有利于清晰度，因为事实的呈现越简短，就越清晰，越容易理解。

15(2) Our presentation of the facts will be clear if we begin with what happened first and observe the order in which things actually have or seem to have happened.We must ensure here that our presentation does not become confused, complicated or obscure, that we do not change the subject, that we do not start from the very beginning or go too far ahead, but also that we do not overlook anything that is relevant to the matter.It is also beneficial for clarity if we follow the instructions given regarding brevity, for the shorter the presentation of facts, the clearer and easier it will be to understand.

16（3）如果我们的陈述方式考虑到常见、预期和自然的情况，并且如果我们提供的有关所花费的时间、涉案人员的位置、动机和犯罪现场的性质的信息是一致的，则事实陈述将显得可能性很大，这是为了防止基于时间太短、没有动机、地点不合适或涉案人员本人不可能实施或遭受这种或那种行为等事实的反驳证据。即使一方掌握了真理，在陈述事实时仍必须考虑到所有这些方面，因为通常只有通过这种程序才能让人相信真理。但如果我们处理的仅仅是想象的事件进程，就必须更加仔细地考虑这些规则。当我们伪造此类事件时，必须谨慎，因为官方文件或某人的权威声明可能发挥了作用。到目前为止，我相信我所表达的观点与这门科学的其他作者的观点相同，除了我制定的关于谨慎方法的新规则之外；与其他人不同，我独自区分了这种引入的三种不同场合，目的是就引入的艺术而言，创造一种完全安全的方法和清晰的理论。以下内容现在适用于其余部分。由于有必要讨论如何找到论据，这对演讲者的技巧提出了特殊的要求，我的目标是表明我确实为这项任务付出了与该主题的重要性相称的努力。不过，我首先想就立场澄清发表几点意见。

16(3) The statement of facts will appear probable if we speak in a way that takes into account what is common, expected and natural, and if the information we provide about the time spent, the position of those involved, the motive and the nature of the crime scene are consistent, this is to guard against rebuttal evidence based on the fact that the time was too short, that there was no motive, that the place was unsuitable or that the people involved themselves could not have carried out or been subjected to this or that act.Even if one has the truth on one's side, all these aspects must still be taken into account during the presentation of the facts, because often the truth can only be believed through this type of procedure.But if we are dealing with a merely imagined course of events, these rules must be considered much more carefully.Caution is necessary when we fake such events, where official documents or an authoritative statement by someone may turn out to have played a role.In what I have said so far, I believe I hold the same views as other writers in this science, except for the new rules I have developed regarding the cautious approach; unlike the others, I alone have distinguished three different occasions for this kind of introduction, with the intention of creating a perfectly safe method and clear theory, as far as the art of introduction is concerned.The following now applies to the remainder.Since it is necessary to discuss how to find arguments, which places particular demands on the speaker's skill, it is my ambition to show that I have really put as much effort into this task as the importance of the subject justifies.However, I would first like to make a few remarks regarding clarification of position.

17立场澄清[divisio]包括两个要素。在陈述完事实之后，我们首先要明确我们和对方在哪些方面达成了一致——前提是我们在对我们有利的事情上达成了一致——以及在哪些方面还存在分歧，例如：“我和对方都同意，奥瑞斯忒斯杀死了他的母亲。他这样做是否正确、恰当，这是一个争议。”同样以类似的方式：“他们承认克吕泰涅斯特拉杀死了阿伽门农。“即便如此，他们还是声称我不应该为我父亲报仇。”10在此之后，我们应该提出一个点划分[分配11]。它由两部分组成，枚举[枚举] 和总结[博览会]。当我们想要指出我们想要涵盖的点数时，我们会采用枚举的方法。不建议超过三个。否则，我们提出的观点可能会多或少，听众会怀疑演讲的准备和预谋，这有损演讲的可信度。在摘要中，我们对想要讨论的要点进行了简要而分类的总结。

17The clarification of position [divisio] includes two elements.After the presentation of the facts, we should first clarify what we and the other party agree on – provided that we agree on things that are beneficial to us – and what there is still disagreement about, as follows: “The other party and I agree that Orestes killed his mother.Whether it was right and proper for him to do so, that is the dispute.” Likewise in a similar way: “They admit that Clytemnestra killed Agamemnon."Even so, they claim that I should not have avenged my father."10After this point, we should then present apoint division[distribution11].It consists of two parts,enumeration[enumeration] andsummation[exposition].We resort to enumeration when we want to indicate the number of points we intend to cover.It is not advisable for these to be more than three.Otherwise, the risk is that we will then present more or fewer points and the audience will suspect preparation and premeditation, which is detrimental to the credibility of the speech.In the summary, we provide a brief and categorical summary of the points we intend to discuss.

18现在让我们转向证明[confirmatio]和反驳[confutatio]。我们希望取得胜利，就像说服技巧一样，完全基于证明和反驳的要素，因为当我们提出支持我们观点的依据并反驳反对意见时，我们无疑就完成了作为演讲者的任务。我们能够解决这两个任务的先决条件是我们知道问题12在这种情况下。虽然其他人计算出四种不同的问题，但我的老师却认为只有三种，这并不是因为他想质疑其他人得出的结论，而是因为他想证明他们已经将一个问题分为两种不同的类型，而他们应该将这两种类型视为一个单一的、连贯的问题。问题在于辩护律师的主要反对意见以及检察官的责任主张。正如我刚才所说，问题有三个，它们涉及事实核查、法律分类各自法律评估。

18Let us now turn to proof [confirmatio] and refutation [confutatio].Our hopes of emerging victorious, like the very technique of persuasion, are based entirely on the elements of proof and refutation, for when we have presented what supports our case and refuted the objections, then we have undoubtedly fulfilled our task as speakers.A prerequisite for us to be able to solve both of these tasks is that we knowthe question12in the case.While others count four different questions, my teacher was of the opinion that there are only three, not because he wanted to question anything that others had come to, but because he wanted to demonstrate that they had divided a question into two different types, which they should have treated as a single, coherent one.The issue consists of the defense attorney's main objection in conjunction with the prosecutor's claim of liability.As I just said, the questions are three in number, and they concernfact-checking, legal classificationrespectivelegal assessment.

（1）当争议涉及某事是否发生时，就存在事实审查，如下例：

(1) A factual examination exists when the dispute concerns whether something has happened, as in the following example:

当阿贾克斯意识到自己在疯狂爆发时所做的一切时，他持剑跳入森林。奥德修斯出现了，他注意到了死者并从他的身体里拔出了血淋淋的武器。现在 Teuker 出现了，他看到了自己死去的兄弟，以及手持血淋淋的剑的敌人。他指控后者犯有谋杀罪。十三

After Ajax realized what he had done during his outburst of madness, he threw himself into the forest on his sword.Odysseus appears, notices the dead man and pulls the bloody weapon from his body.Now Teuker appears, seeing his dead brother and his enemy with a bloody sword.He accuses the latter of murder.13

在这种情况下，真相是通过事实调查来确定的，即争议的焦点在于某一行动是否已经发生。因此，该问题被称为事实调查问题。

In this case, the truth is determined through fact-finding, i.e.The dispute will concern whether a certain action has taken place.Hence the name fact-finding question.

19（2）当一份书面文件直接或间接地引起某种形式的分歧时，该问题涉及法律分类。这个问题分为六种不同的类型：措辞和含义[脚本和观点]，冲突的法律[相反的法律]，歧义[模糊的]，定义[定义]，程序性异议[翻译]和类比推理[推理]。

19(2) The issue concerns legal classification, when a written document directly or indirectly gives rise to some form of disagreement.This question is divided into six different types:wording and meaning[script and opinion],conflicting laws[contrariae leges],ambiguity[ambiguous],definition[definition],procedural objection[translation] andanalogical reasoning[ratiocinatio].

(a) 当作者的意图与所写内容不符时，​​就会产生措辞和含义上的争议，如下例所示。假设有一条法律规定，在暴风雨中弃船的人将失去对船只的所有权利，而船只（包括其货物）如果得救，则属于留在船上的人。被猛烈的风暴吓坏了，现在每个人都离开了船，进入了救生艇——除了一个人，一个病人，由于身体不适，无法离开船逃生。纯属偶然，这艘船漂流到了港口，现在已成为病人的财产，而它的前主人则声称拥有它。这个法律分类问题涉及措辞和含义。

(a) A dispute over wording and meaning arises when the author's intention does not seem to match what is written, as in the following example.Let us assume that there is a law that states that those who abandon a ship in a storm shall lose all rights to it, and that the ship, including its cargo, if saved, shall belong to those who remained on board.Terrified by a violent storm, everyone has now left their ship and entered the lifeboat – all except one, a sick man who, due to his illness, was prevented from leaving the ship and escaping.By pure chance, the ship has drifted into a harbor and has now become the property of the sick man, while its former owner claims it.This question of legal classification concerns wording and meaning.

20（b）当一条法律规定或允许某事而另一条法律禁止该事时，就会存在法律冲突，如下所示。法律禁止任何被判犯有敲诈勒索罪的人在人民议会上发言。另一支球队强加占卜官在人民议会前提名在已故占卜官之后竞选该职位的人选14。一名因敲诈勒索而被定罪的占卜师现在提名一名候选人来填补一名已故占卜师的职位；他正在被罚款。这一法律分类问题是基于冲突的法律。

20(b) A conflict of laws exists when one law mandates or permits something while another prohibits it, as follows.A law prohibits anyone convicted of extortion from speaking before the people's assembly.Another teamimposesan augur to nominate before the people's assembly the person who will run for the position after a deceased augur14An augur convicted of extortion has now nominated a candidate for the position of a deceased augur; he is being fined.This issue of legal classification is based on conflicting laws.

（c）当一段文本可以有两种或两种以上的方式解释时，歧义性就是争议的基础，如下所示。当一个家庭的父亲指定他的儿子为继承人时，他会将银器遗赠给他的妻子：“我的继承人将给我的妻子她自己选择的重30磅的银器。”男人死后，女人便继承了一些珍贵的凿刻器皿。儿子声称欠她 30 英镑他的自由选择。这里的分类问题源于模糊性。

(c) Ambiguity is the basis for dispute when a text can be interpreted in two or more ways, as follows.When a father of a family appointed his son as heir, he bequeathed silver vessels to his wife: “My heir shall give to my wife silver vessels weighing 30 pounds of her own free choice.” After the husband’s death, the woman lays claim to some precious chiseled vessels.The son claims to owe her 30 pounds afterhisfree choice.The issue of classification here has its origin in ambiguity.

21（d）定义类案件，涉及对某一行为应如何称呼的争议。下面是一个例子。当卢修斯·萨图尔尼努斯15正准备提出以五分之六驴为单位的粮食价格法案时，当时的城市财务官昆图斯·卡皮奥向参议院解释说，国库无法承担如此大的开支。参议院决定，如果萨图尔尼努斯将该法案提交给人民，将被视为违背国家利益。萨图尔尼努斯立即采取行动，不顾同事的否决，安排了投票。当卡皮奥看到萨图尔尼努斯不顾同事的否决，提出与国家利益相悖的建议时，他在一些保守派的帮助下攻击了萨图尔尼努斯，拆毁了投票桥梁16，推翻了投票箱并阻止了对该提案的进一步审议。卡皮奥被指控犯有叛国罪。这里的分类问题从定义开始，因为当我们试图确定叛国罪的含义时，我们也定义了这个概念本身。

21(d) A case about definition concerns the dispute over how a certain action should be called.An example is the following.When Lucius Saturninus15was about to present the bill on the grain price at five-sixths of an ass, the then city quaestor Quintus Caepio explained to the senate that the treasury could not bear such a large expenditure.The Senate decided that Saturninus would be considered acting against the interests of the state if he presented the bill to the people.Saturninus sprang into action, and despite his colleagues' veto, he arranged for a vote.When Caepio saw that Saturninus, despite the veto of his colleagues, was presenting his proposal contrary to the interests of the state, he attacked him, assisted by some conservatives, tore down the voting bridges16, overturned the ballot boxes and prevented further consideration of the proposal.Caepio was charged with high treason.The question of classification here starts from definition, because when we try to determine the meaning of high treason, we also define the concept itself.

22(e) 争议基于程序性异议，即被告要求推迟审判或更换检察官或法官。希腊人通常在审判期间提出此类问题，而我们通常在初步调查期间提出此类问题。尽管如此，它在我们的法庭诉讼过程中会发挥一些作用，例如如下。如果有人被指控贪污，罪名是从某个地方移走属于国家的银器，那么在明确了盗窃和贪污之后，他可以辩称，指控应该与盗窃有关，而不是贪污。由于以下原因，这种分类问题很少在法庭诉讼中出现。在裁判官面前的争议中，裁判官可以接受反对意见，如果原告缺乏正式理由继续追究此事，则他失去起诉的权利；在公开案件中，法律确保提前决定是否允许检察官提起诉讼，前提是这样做不会对嫌疑人造成妨碍。

22(e) A dispute is based on a procedural objection, when the accused demands either that the trial be postponed or that the prosecutor or judge be replaced.This type of question occurs among the Greeks during the trial itself, while among us it is usually raised during the preliminary investigation.Nevertheless, it will come to some use during our court proceedings, for example as follows.If someone is accused of embezzlement with reference to having removed silver vessels belonging to the state from a particular location, he can, after having defined both theft and embezzlement, argue that the charge should relate to theft and not embezzlement.For the following reasons, this type of classification issue rarely comes up in court proceedings.In a dispute before the praetor, he may accept objections, and the plaintiff loses the right to sue if he lacks formal grounds to pursue the matter; in public cases, the laws provide for a decision to be made in advance as to whether the prosecutor should be allowed to bring charges or not, if this can be done without hindrance to the suspect.

23（f）当某件事成为判决的主题时，争议基于类比推理，尽管该事本身缺乏可适用的法律框架，但由于可能存在相似性，仍需在其他法律中寻求解决。以下是一个例子。法律规定：“如果一个人失去理智，他的人身和财产应由他的后代和亲属监护。”另一条法律规定：“任何被判犯有弑父罪的人都应被捆绑起来，装进皮袋，扔进河里。”还有一条法律：“一家之主在遗嘱中关于家庭和财产的决定应成为法律。”另一条法律规定：“如果父亲去世时没有留下遗嘱，他的家庭和财产将归他的后代和亲戚所有。”马尔莱奥勒斯因谋杀母亲而被判有罪。宣判后，他的头立即被套上狼皮袋，双脚被戴上木镣，关进监狱。他的辩护人带着写字板来到监狱，当着他的面写下了他的遗嘱；证人也按规定顺序到场。马莱奥勒斯被处死，遗嘱中指定的继承人接管了遗产。但在审判期间站在对立面的马莱奥勒斯的弟弟现在却声称要根据后代法来继承他的遗产。这里没有引用具体的个别法律条文，但是却引用了许多法律条文，这些条文构成了类比推理的基础，目的是表明 Malleolus 是否有权立遗嘱。因此，这是一个基于类比推理的法律分类问题。17

23(f) A dispute is based on analogical reasoning when something becomes the subject of a judgment that, although lacking its own applicable legal framework, is nevertheless sought in other laws due to the similarity that may exist.The following is an example.One law says: “If a man loses his mind, he shall be placed under the guardianship of his descendants and relatives regarding his person and property.” Another law says: “Anyone convicted of parricide shall be bound, put in a leather bag and thrown into a stream of water.” Yet another law: “What a father of a family has determined in his will regarding his household and property shall be law.” Yet another law: “If a father of a family dies without having made a will, his household and property shall go to his descendants and relatives.” Malleolus was convicted of murdering his mother.Immediately after the verdict, his head was wrapped in a wolfskin sack, wooden shackles were pulled over his feet, and he was taken to prison.His defenders brought writing tablets to the prison and wrote down his will in his presence; witnesses were also present in the prescribed order.Malleolus was executed, and the heirs named in the will took over the inheritance.But Malleolus' younger brother, who was on the opposing side during the trial, now claims to inherit him by virtue of the law of descendants.No specific individual legal provision is cited here, but nevertheless many legal provisions are cited that form the basis for an analogical reasoning with the aim of showing whether Malleolus had or did not have the right to make a will.It is therefore a question of legal classification based on analogical reasoning.17

我现在已经表明了法律分类分解成哪些部分。现在我来讨论一下法律评估。

I have now shown the parts into which the legal classification breaks down.Let me now discuss the legal assessment.

24（3）当对行为本身达成一致，但问题在于有关人员的行为是否正确时，法律评估才是相关的。这个问题有两种不同的类型，其中一种叫做分类[绝对部分] 另一个是间接的[双引号]。

24(3) The legal assessment is relevant when there is agreement regarding the action itself but the question is whether the person concerned acted rightly or wrongly.This question appears in two different types, one of which is called thecategorical[pars absolute] and the other thecircumstantial[pairs adsumptiva].

（a）当我们断言某个行为本身就是真实行为（不参考间接证据）时，就出现了范畴类型。例如：一位哑剧演员在舞台上向诗人阿修斯发表演讲18按名字。阿修斯以侮辱罪起诉他。这位演员除了表示可以提及以该剧名义在舞台上演出的演员的名字之外，没有为自己做出任何辩护。

(a) The categorical type is present when we assert, without reference to circumstantial evidence, that an action in itself was a true action.Example: A mime actor addressed the poet Accius from the stage18by name.Accius prosecuted him for insult.The actor offered nothing in his defense other than that it was permissible to mention by name the person in whose name the play was performed on stage.

（b）当一种本质上较弱的防御通过引用某些生物学情况而得到加强时，就会出现与情况相关的类型。与环境相关的类型有四种不同的形式：同意[让步]19，否认责任[消除犯罪]，责任转移[犯罪翻译]和比较[比较]。

(b) The circumstance-related type exists when an inherently weak defense is strengthened by citing some biological circumstance.The circumstance-related type occurs in four different forms:consent[concession]19,denial of responsibility[removal of crime],transfer of responsibility[translatio crimeni] andcomparison[comparatio].

（1）同意是指被告人索要贿赂的情况，分为免责[炼狱]和道歉[弃用]。免责意味着被告否认其行为是故意的，并陷入无知[轻率]，事故[福图纳] 和必要性[必要性]。卡皮奥事件中的事故20他在人民保民官面前就其军队损失一事提出申辩；无知，就像一个男人因为谋杀主人而处决了一个奴隶，而主人是这个男人的兄弟——他在违背兄弟的遗嘱之前就这么做了，根据遗嘱，奴隶已经被释放了21；必要性，例如由于道路被洪水淹没，士兵休假后没有按时报到的情况。

(1) Consent refers to the situation where the accused asks for a bribe, and is divided intoexculpation[purgatory] andapology[deprecation].Exculpation means that the accused denies that he acted with intent and disintegrates intoignorance[imprudence],accident[fortuna] andnecessity[necessity].Accident as in the Caepio case20in his plea before the tribunes concerning the loss of his army; ignorance as in the case of the man who had a slave executed for murdering his master, who was the man's brother - he did this before breaking the brother's will, according to which the slave had been freed21; necessity as in the case of the soldier who did not report on time after leave because the roads were flooded.

当被告承认罪行和犯罪意图但仍请求宽恕时，就会提出认罪请求。实际上，这种情况在普通审判中很少发生，而在我们为那些因许多善行而声名鹊起的人说话的情况下。这里我们可以用一些标准的论点来详细阐述整件事，例如：“但如果他确实犯了罪，那么考虑到他以前的善行，对他从轻处理仍然是合适的。但他本人并没有要求任何额外的钱。”因此，此类案件不会发生在法庭上，而是发生在参议院、众议院或委员会听证会上。

A plea of ​​guilty is applied when the accused admits both the crime and criminal intent but still asks for mercy.In practice, this hardly occurs in a regular trial, but rather in contexts where we speak for someone who has made a name for themselves for their many good deeds.Here we can elaborate on the whole thing with some standard arguments, e.g.: “But if he had been guilty of this, it would still be appropriate to show him leniency in view of his previous good deeds.But he himself does not ask for a bribe.” Such a case therefore does not occur in a court of law but rather in the Senate, or before a general or in a committee hearing.

二十五（2）当我们不否认某一行为，但声称是他人的罪行迫使我们实施这一行为时，案件就实现了责任的转移，例如奥瑞斯忒斯22通过将责任推卸给母亲来为自己辩护。

25(2) A case actualizes the transfer of responsibility, when we do not deny the act but claim that the crimes of others forced us to perform it, as when Orestes22defends himself by shifting the blame onto his mother.

（3）否认责任发生在我们否认罪行本身而不是否认犯罪行为本身的情况下，我们要么将罪行转嫁给另一个人，要么将其归咎于某种情况。例如：如果承认谋杀了普布利乌斯·苏尔皮西乌斯的人被起诉，但为自己辩护时援引了执政官的命令，那么责任就转移到了别人身上23并同时声称他们不仅下令谋杀，而且还说明了为什么这一行为是合法的。责任是归咎于某种情况，例如某人被公共决议禁止履行遗嘱中要求其做的事项。

(3) Denial of responsibility occurs in a case where we deny not the criminal act itself but the guilt itself, which we either shift to another individual or attribute to some circumstance.So for example:The blame is shifted to another, if the person who confesses to having murdered Publius Sulpicius is prosecuted but in his defense invokes an order from the consuls23and at the same time claim that they not only ordered the murder but also stated why this act was legal.The blame is to attribute a circumstance, if e.g.someone is prohibited by a public decision from carrying out what he has been ordered to do in a will.

（4）比较发生在我们声称必须执行两个动作中的一个，并且我们选择的那个动作更好的时候。以下可以说明这种情况。当盖乌斯·波皮利乌斯被高卢人俘虏且无路可逃时，他与敌方领导人进行谈判，并最终获得允许率领军队撤离，条件是他投降。他觉得失去绳索比失去军队还好，所以他率领军队出去，留下了绳索。他被指控犯有叛国罪。24

(4) Comparison occurs in a case where we claim that it was necessary to perform one of two actions and that the one we chose was the better one.The following may illustrate such a case.When Gaius Popilius was held captive by the Gauls and had no means of escape, he entered into negotiations with the enemy leaders and as a result obtained permission to lead the army out on condition that he surrendered.He considered it better to lose the rope than the army, so he led the army out and left the rope.He was charged with high treason.24

因此，我认为我已经展示了各种问题及其细分。现在将讨论它们的正确使用方式和方法。但首先，我想明确一下各方在过程中必须共同追求的目标，这个目标将决定演讲的整个结构。

I therefore consider myself to have shown the various issues, as well as their subdivisions.The proper way and method of their use is now to be discussed.But first, I want to clarify what the parties in a process must jointly aim for, the goal that will then determine the entire structure of the speech.

二十六在发现相关问题之后，必须立即寻找免除责任的依据。它对于案件具有决定性作用，并包括辩护，根据以下示例，现在为了澄清起见坚持这个具体案例：奥瑞斯忒斯承认他杀死了他的母亲，但如果他不提供不为其行为负责的基础，那么他就无法为自己辩护。所以他带领了一场，没有这场就不会有进球。他说：“她杀了我的父亲。”因此，所谓的释放理由就是辩护理由，正如我刚才所表明的，如果没有这个理由，就不会对定罪产生丝毫怀疑。

26Immediately after having thus found the relevant issue, one must search for a basis for discharge from liability.It is decisive for the case and includes the defense, according to the following example – to now stick to this particular case for the purpose of clarification: Orestes admits that he killed his mother, but if he does not provide a basis for freedom from responsibility for his actions, he has made his defense impossible.So he leads one, without which there wouldn't even be a goal.He says: “She had killed my father.” The alleged ground for acquittal is consequently that which contains the defence, as I have just shown, and without that ground there is not the slightest doubt that can be raised against a conviction.

一旦找到了免责依据，就必须寻找反驳意见，即其中包含指控，并针对我刚才提到的辩方提出的无罪释放理由提出指控。其设计如下。在奥瑞斯忒斯如此陈述他的无罪辩护：“我有权杀人，因为她杀死了我的父亲”之后，检察官将提出反驳，如下：“但是你不应该杀死她，她不应该在没有法律的情况下受到惩罚。”审判”。辩方反对解除指控，而公诉方则提出反驳，这必然导致法院必须作出裁决的问题，在我们国家，这被称为“裁决问题”，但在希腊，crinomenomon。它应基于反驳和所谓的豁免理由的组合，如下所示：当奥瑞斯忒斯声称杀死了他的母亲来为他的父亲报仇时，克吕泰墨涅斯特拉未经审判就被她的儿子杀死，这是正确的吗？二十五因此，这才是法院判决问题的正确方法。一旦找到，就必须让整个案件结构朝着这个目标前进。

Once you have found the basis for exemption from liability, you must look for the counterargument, i.e.that which contains the accusation and which is brought against the grounds for acquittal raised by the defense, which I just mentioned.It shall be designed as follows.After Orestes has formulated his plea for acquittal thus: “I had the right to kill, for she had killed my father,” the prosecutor will make a counterargument, as follows: “But it was not right that she should be killed by you and that she should be punished withouttrial".The defense's objection to discharge and the prosecutor's counter-argument necessarily lead to the question the court has to decide, what is called in our country the "question for decision" but in the Greekscrinomenomon.It shall be based on a combination of the counterargument and the alleged ground for exemption in the following way: When Orestes claims to have killed his mother to avenge his father, was it right that Clytemnestra was killed by her son without a trial?25This is therefore the correct method for arriving at the issue for the court's decision.Once it has been found, it is necessary that the entire structure of the case be directed towards this goal.

二十七在所有问题及其细分领域中，除事实认定问题外，法院判决的问题均应按照上述方式处理。在那里，人们既不会要求为某一行为提供正当理由——这一要求被拒绝了——也不会试图提出任何反驳，因为没有人对免除责任提出异议。相反，法院的判决是基于以下指控和否认。动作声明[intentio]：“你杀死了阿贾克斯二十六”否认[infitiatio]：“我没有。”法庭判决[iudicatio]的问题：“他杀了他吗？”正如前文所指出的，双方论点的全部重点都必须指向这一点，即法院要作出裁决的问题。如果案件涉及多个问题或其部分，则同一案件中需要法院裁决的问题也将是多个，但在所有案件中都必须使用相同的方法来发现这些问题。

27In all issues and subdivisions thereof, the question for the court's decision shall be found in the aforementioned manner, with the exception of the issue of fact-finding.There, one neither asks for justifying circumstances for an action – it is denied – nor seeks to come up with any counterarguments, since no objection to discharge from liability has been raised.The court's decision is instead based on allegations and denials, as follows.Action statement [intentio]: “You have killed Ajax26.” Denial [infitiatio]: “I have not.” Question for the court’s decision [iudicatio]: “Did he kill him?” As previously pointed out, the entire thrust of both parties’ speeches must be directed toward this point, the question for the court’s decision.If the case raises several issues or parts thereof, the questions for the court's decision will also be several in one and the same case, but in all cases they must be found using the same method.

我特意花了很大力气简短而清晰地讨论了迄今为止需要处理的问题。由于本书现在已经达到了足够大的范围，将其他问题的讨论推迟到后续的书中是更合适的，这样大量的文字就不会让你感到疲倦和注意力不集中。如果你发现我的工作节奏跟不上你的学习热情，你不仅应该从学科范围上寻找解释，还应该从其他任务占用我的时间上寻找解释。尽管如此，我还是会尽力加快工作进度，并打算勤奋地弥补因其他承诺而损失的时间，以便通过这份礼物，我能够尽可能丰富地满足您的愿望，这是对您愿意为我服务的感谢，也是我对您的承诺的表达。

I have deliberately taken pains to briefly and clearly discuss the issues that have so far required treatment.Since this book has now reached a sufficiently large scope, it is more appropriate to postpone the discussion of other problems to a subsequent book, so that a large amount of text does not make you tired and inattentive.If you find that my work pace does not keep pace with your study enthusiasm, you should seek the explanation not only in the scope of the subject but also in the fact that other tasks occupy my time.I will nevertheless try to speed up the work, and I intend to compensate for the time lost through other commitments with diligence, so that through this gift I will be able to fulfill your wishes as abundantly as possible, this as a thank you for your willingness to serve me and as an expression of my commitment to you.

1 我们应当在古代修辞学的持续争论背景下看待这一声明。我们的作者认为，修辞技巧不能被滥用：所说的内容既不能不真实，也不能不道德。为了反思，我们可以比较一下 II:12 中所说的内容。

1 The statement should be seen against the background of the ongoing debate for and against rhetoric in antiquity.The rhetorical technique, our author believes, must not be abused: what is said must be neither untrue nor immoral.For reflection, one can compare what is said in II:12.

2 在修辞学中，我们用拉丁语谈论格原因（复数）原因），分为三种主要类型或使尴尬。本教科书开头示范性别，来自于示威者，“展示”，“指出”，参见我们的“示威”。它主要指出不同的道德品质或缺点，“美德”和“恶习”。由于缺乏更合适的术语，示范性别翻译为“颂词”，这在引言中已得到指出和论证。然后如下审议性别拉丁语商榷，“考虑”，其中“权衡”支持和反对的不同理由，例如关于政治问题——这就是为什么它被翻译为“政治演讲”。最后如下司法性别被翻译为“法律演讲”或“审判演讲”。然后作者将以相反的顺序处理这些不同的类型。

2 In rhetoric, we speak of cases, in Latincause(in plural)causes),which are divided into three main types orembarrassThis textbook begins withdemonstrative gender,which comes fromdemonstrators,“show”, “point out”, cf. our “demonstration”.It is mainly about pointing out different moral qualities or shortcomings, “virtues” and “vices”.For lack of a more appropriate term,demonstrative gendertranslated as “panegyric speech” which is pointed out and justified in the introduction.Then follows heredeliberative genderof Latindeliberate,to “consider”, where different reasons for and against are “weighed” against each other, e.g.on a political issue – that is why this has been translated as “political speech”.Last followsjudicial genderwhich has been translated as “legal speech” or “trial speech”.The author will then treat these different genres in reverse order.

3 这里介绍了修辞的五个部分，即：发明、布置、演说、记忆和行动这里称之为发音。当作者处理这些问题时，他抛弃了传统秩序中的一些东西：总的来说，发明、处置、行动、记忆和演说。

3 Here are presented the five parts of rhetoric, namely:inventio, dispositio, elocutio, memoriaandactionwhich is called herepronunciation.When the author then deals with them, he throws something out of this traditional order: it becomes, by and large,inventio, dispositio, actio, memoriaandelocution.

第二卷

第二本书

BOOK II

SECOND BOOK

公元二世纪：1-50年

AD HERENNIUM II:1-50

1在第一本书《赫雷尼乌斯》中，我曾简要阐述了演说家必须处理的各种情况、他必须练习的演讲艺术的各个方面，以及他最容易学会掌握它们的方法。但是，由于不可能一次性涵盖所有主题，而且必须先写最重要的主题，以便您更容易掌握其余的主题，因此我决定先写最困难的问题。

1In the first book, Herennius, I have briefly stated the various cases an orator must deal with, the various aspects of the art of speech that he has to practice, and the methods by which he can most easily learn to master them.But, since it was both impossible to cover all the topics at once and necessary to write about the most important ones first, so that the remaining ones would seem all the easier for you to grasp, I decided to write about the most difficult questions first.

这些案件可以分为三种不同的类型：颂[属指示]，它们政治的[审议类] 以及那些合法的演讲[司法属]。迄今为止最困难的是法律演讲，这就是为什么在这本书和上一本书中我选择首先介绍它们。在演讲者必须掌握的五个要素中，寻找论据（inventio）的艺术是最重要的，也是最困难的。我也将在本书中基本完成对该主题的讨论，尽管我会将一些相关细节推迟到第三本书。1

The cases can be divided into three different genres: thosepanegyric[genus demonstrative], theypolitical[genus deliberative] and thoselegalthe speech [genus judiciale].By far the most difficult are the legal speeches, and that is why in this and the previous book I have chosen to present them first.Of the five elements that the speaker must master, the art of finding arguments [inventio] is the most important and difficult.I will also largely finish covering that topic in the present book, although I will postpone some related details until the third book.1

2我首先写了演讲的六个部分，在第一部分中我讲述了引言 [exordium]、事实陈述 [narratio] 和立场澄清 [divisio]，诚然，我没有讲得那么详细，但无论如何，我已经尽可能清晰地表达了你们的期望。我发现有必要对证明（confirmatio）和反驳（confutatio）进行全面的论述，这让我有理由澄清不同类型的质疑（constitutio causae）2] 及其细分。这揭示了针对每个给定案例找到问题及其细分的重要性。然后我解释了如何着手确定法院判决的问题；一旦完成，就必须确保演讲的整个结构都针对这一点。此后，我记得有很多情况都适用多个问题或其细分。

2I began by writing about the six parts of the speech and in the first book I told about the introduction [exordium], the presentation of facts [narratio] and the clarification of position [divisio], admittedly not in such detail, but nevertheless with as much clarity as I thought you would desire.I found it inevitable to then give a comprehensive treatment of proof [confirmatio] and refutation [confutatio], which gave me reason to clarify the different types of questioning [constitutio causae2] and their subdivisions.This revealed the importance of finding both the question and its subdivision for each given case.Then I explained how one should proceed to establish the question for the court's decision [iudicatio]; once this is done, one must ensure that the entire structure of the speech is directed towards that point.After this, I recalled that there are numerous cases where several issues or their subdivisions are applicable.

在我看来，剩下的任务是：首先，要表明在每一类问题或其分支中，可以用什么方法来寻找论证；其次，要表明什么类型的证明（希腊人称之为表皮肉瘤应分别应用和避免；这两个问题都涉及证明和反驳。然后，作为最后一点，我澄清一下人们在演讲中应该使用什么类型的结论 [conclusio]，即数字的六个部分中最后一个部分。首先，我打算解决如何适当构建每个个案的问题，然后我自然会特别关注最困难的案件类型。

The remaining task has seemed to me to be to show, first, what methods can be used to find arguments in each type of question or its subdivision, and secondly, what types of proof (which the Greeks callepicheremata)one should apply and avoid, respectively; both of these questions belong to proof and refutation.Then, as a final point, I clarify what type of conclusion [conclusio] one should use in their speeches, i.e.the one of the six parts of a number that comes last.First, I intend to address the question of how we should appropriately structure each individual case, and I will then naturally pay special attention to the type of case that is most difficult.

3在一个基于事实问题的案件中[constitutio coniecturalis3]，检察官的事实陈述应当带有点点怀疑，让人觉得什么也没做，什么也没说，没有人来也没有人去，总之，一切都不是无缘无故发生的。另一方面，辩护律师的事实陈述应该简单、清晰，并削弱所提出的怀疑。根据事实审查问题构建案件时，必须考虑六个不同的因素：可能性[可能]，排除[调和]，符号[符号]，指示[争论]，后续行为[连续] 和证据摘要[缓刑]。我现在将解释这些

3In a case based on the question of fact [constitutio coniecturalis3], the prosecutor's statement of facts should contain suspicions sprinkled here and there, so that one gets the impression that nothing has been done and nothing has been said, that no one has come or gone, in short, that nothing at all has happened without reason.The defense attorney's statement of facts, on the other hand, should consist of a simple and clear account combined with a weakening of the suspicions raised.When constructing a case based on the factual examination question, six different factors must be considered:probability[probable],exclusion[conlation],sign[sign],indication[argument],subsequent behavior[consecutive] andsummary of evidence[adprobation].I will now explain the meaning of each of these

（1）用概率论（probabile）来表明被告人从犯罪中获益，并且始终无法停止这种令人憎恶的行为。它分为主题[原因] 和道德[白色的]。

(1) Probability [probabile] is used to show that the accused benefited from the crime and that he has never been able to refrain from this type of abomination.It is divided intomotif[cause] andmorality[White].

（a）动机是指被告人实施犯罪是为了获得利益或者避免利益的动机。在这种情况下提出的问题是，他是否通过犯罪来寻求荣誉，金钱或权力等利益，是否想满足对爱或类似激情的渴望，或者他是否试图避免敌意，耻辱，痛苦或惩罚等劣势。

(a) The motive is what led the accused to commit the crime in the hope of gaining advantages or to avoid disadvantages.Questions asked in this context are whether he sought benefits such as honor, money or power through the crime, whether he wanted to satisfy his desire for love or some similar passion, or whether he tried to avoid some disadvantage such as hostility, disrepute, pain or punishment.

4在希望获得好处的情况下，检察官可以指出对方的贪婪，在避免不利的情况下，检察官可以指出对方的懦弱。另一方面，如果可能的话，辩护人应该否认存在任何动机，或者大大淡化它。然后，他应该强调每个从某件事中受益的人都被怀疑犯有罪行的不公正。

4In the case of hope for advantages, the prosecutor can point to the other party's greed, and in the case of avoidance of disadvantages, he can point to his cowardice.The defender, on the other hand, should, if possible, deny that there was any motive, or significantly downplay it.Then he should emphasize the injustice of everyone who has benefited from a certain thing being exposed to suspicion of a crime.

5（b）然后根据此人过去的行为来考察他的道德。检察官首先应该考虑该人以前是否犯过类似罪行。如果他想不出类似的事情，他就应该调查被告是否曾经受到过类似的怀疑，并且他应该停留在这一点上，意图证明该人的道德可以与他刚刚澄清的犯罪动机相协调，按照下面的例子。如果他声称被告是出于贪婪，他就应该证明自己一直都是贪婪的；如果动机是为了追求更高的职位，他就应该把他描绘成一个雄心勃勃的人。如果他找不到与动机相符的性格缺陷，他可以想出一个不相符的性格缺陷。如果他不能证明该人贪婪，他或许可以证明该人是一个不择手段的诱惑者，简而言之，试图指控该人至少犯下一些错误，但最好是尽可能多的错误，然后指出，一个在其他情况下可能行为如此邪恶的人犯下这样的罪行并不奇怪。如果对方当事人以其无可挑剔的行为和正直而闻名，检察官应该强调，现在需要审查的是他的行为而不是他的名誉，被告以前隐瞒了他的罪行，而他，检察官，现在打算表明被告与犯罪并非毫无关联。然而，作为辩护律师，如果可能的话，你应该首先强调客户无可挑剔的行为。如果这条路行不通，辩护人就必须撤退，寻找客户缺乏知识、缺乏理解、年轻、身体胁迫或劝说等理由。在此背景下，对于不属于所指控范围之内的事项，不应将其归咎于<...>4。但如果委托人的悲惨境遇和名声扫地对辩护构成了相当大的障碍，那么辩护方应该首先努力声称有人散布了关于无辜者的谣言，并利用不宜相信谣言的一般论点。但如果这些都无济于事，他应该作为最后的手段，声称这不是在审查人员面前对被告的道德的讨论，而是对对方指控的司法回应。
