50(3) We arouse the sympathy of our listeners by speaking of the changing vicissitudes of fate, by comparing our former happiness with our present misfortune, by enumerating and clarifying the consequences for us if we lose our goal, by pleadingly submitting to the people whose pity we wish to win, by revealing what our parents, children, and other relatives will suffer as a result of our misfortune, while emphasizing that our pain concerns their anxiety and distress, not our own distress, further by recounting the kindness, humanity, and compassion we ourselves have shown to others, by emphasizing that we have always or for a long time had to struggle with misfortunes, by complaining about our fate or our bad luck, and by showing that we will give evidence of strength of character and ability to endure adversity.The plea for pity should be brief; for nothing dries faster than a tear.

在本书中，我可能已经处理了整个修辞学中最困难的部分，因此本书应该到此结束。出于方便的原因，我打算将剩余规则的处理推迟到第三本书。如果您能以与我写作时所付出的努力相匹配的细心对待此书，我将因您分享我的知识而获得劳动回报，而您反过来也会称赞我的勤奋，并从您所获得的见解中找到快乐；你会对公开演讲的规则有更多的了解，我会以更大的热情去完成剩下的任务。而我确信这一切都会是结果；你对我而言并不陌生。现在让我转向剩下的教义，以便我可以做我最想做的事情，即满足你最公正的愿望。

In this book I have dealt with perhaps the most difficult sections in the whole of rhetoric, and therefore the book should end here.For reasons of expediency, I intend to postpone the treatment of the remaining rules until the third book.If you acquire this presentation with a care that corresponds to the efforts I have made in writing it, I will be rewarded for my labor by sharing my knowledge, while you, on your part, will praise my diligence and find joy in the insights you have gained; you will know more about the rules of rhetoric, and I will approach the remaining task with greater enthusiasm.And I know for sure that all this will be the result; you are no stranger to me.Let me now turn to the remaining doctrines, so that I may do what I most desire, namely, to satisfy your most just desire.

二十六笔者认为，错误在于开放。

26The author believes that the fault lies in the open.

二十七引文（抑扬格诗节）取自提图斯·马修斯·普劳图斯（Titus Maccius Plautus）的著作（c.公元前250-184年）喜剧特里努默斯，23-26。这里的作者理解拉丁语姓名其通常含义为“因为”，但事实上普劳图斯在此处可能另有含义，例如‘确实’。

27The quotes (iambic stanzas) are taken from Titus Maccius Plautus' (c.250-184 BC) comedyTrinummus,23-26.The author here understands the Latinnamein its usual meaning 'because', but in fact Plautus may well mean something else in this place, e.g.'truly'.

二十八马库斯·帕库维乌斯 (Marcus Pacuvius)，公元前 220-130 年，罗马悲剧家。不确定这句引文的出处（诗句的韵律是七行抑扬格，由七个半抑扬格组成）。

28Marcus Pacuvius, 220-130 BC, Roman tragedian.It is uncertain where the quote comes from (the verse meter is trochaic septenary, consisting of seven and a half trochae).

二十九本章（抑扬格诗篇）中的引文，至少是第一个，可能取自恩尼乌斯的戏剧。克瑞斯丰忒斯。

29The quotations in this chapter (iambic senar), at least the first one, may have been taken from Ennius' drama.Cresphontes.

三十参见四：52分配。

30Cf. IV:52division.

31人们认为这首诗（七行扬抑格）是恩尼乌斯诗歌中伊阿宋和美狄亚之间的对话的一部分。美狄亚流放（见上文注释25）。

31It has been assumed that this verse (trochaic septenary) is part of an exchange between Jason and Medea in Ennius'Medea exile(see note 25 above).

三十二参见二：24。

32Cf. II:24.

33这两个扬抑格七音节可能源自恩尼乌斯的戏剧泰厄斯忒斯。

33These two trochaic septenaries probably derive from Ennius' playThyestes.

三十四不确定这句引文（抑扬格诗句）出自哪部戏剧。

34It is uncertain from which drama the quote (iambic verses) is taken.

三十五参见定义 IV:35。

35See definition IV:35.

三十六埃阿斯要求将阿喀琉斯的武器交给他；参见见上文第一卷，注释 13。这些抑扬格七行诗可能取自阿修斯 (Accius) 的一部戏剧 (I:24)。

36Ajax demands that he be given Achilles' weapons; cf. above book I, note 13.These iambic septs may have been taken from a drama by Accius (I:24).

三十七此节及随后的抑扬格诗节的起源尚不明确。

37The origin of this and the following iambic stanzas is uncertain.

三十八在引用争议中，帕库维乌斯（在剧中）让安提俄珀（Antiope）泽图斯代表实际生活，而他的兄弟安菲翁代表音乐。

38In the referring dispute, Pacuvius (in the play) letsAntiope)Zethus represents practical life, while his brother Amphion represents music.

三十九翻译基于拉丁语不方便（“对方的缺点”）是错误的马桶。

39The translation is based on the Latininconvenient(“the disadvantages of the other”) is an error forcommode.

40这两座城市（阿尔巴富琴斯，位于罗马和亚得里亚海沿岸的维斯提亚人之间，包括佩纳城（Penna）或皮纳城（Pinna）在战争时期向罗马表达了忠诚。

40Both cities (Alba Fucens, midway between Rome and the Vestinians on the Adriatic coast, includingthe city of Penna or Pinna) had shown Rome its loyalty in times of war.

41苏尔皮基乌斯就是 1:25 中提到的同一个人；该事件发生于公元前 90 年至公元前 88 年。

41Sulpicius is the same man mentioned in 1:25; the events took place in 90-88 BC.

四十二拉丁语中“放逐”和“禁止”的表达是禁止水火“禁止（给予流放者）水和火”。

42The Latin expression for 'banishment', 'ban' isinterdictio aquae et ignis,“prohibition against (giving the exiled person) water and fire”.

第三卷

第三本书

BOOK III

BOOK THIRD

公元三世纪：1-40年

AD HERENNIUM III:1-40

1在之前的书中，我相信我已经足够详细地展示了如何为所有类型的法庭演讲寻找论据。我推迟了适用于政治和颂词演讲的方法，但现在我打算在本书中讨论它们，以便尽快向您完整解释寻找论据的艺术。修辞学的其余四个部分中，本书涵盖了其中三个部分，即提纲、表达和记忆。语言表述需要更详细的处理，因此我更愿意在第四本书中讨论这一部分，我相信我能够很快完成并发送给您，以便您能够获得修辞理论的完整介绍。与此同时，你应该学习基本原理，当你愿意的时候可以跟我学习，有时也可以自学，这样你就能跟上我的步伐，毫无阻碍地获取相关的有用知识。现在我请你们集中注意力，我将快速朝着我们既定的目标前进。

1In previous books, I believe I have shown in sufficient detail how to find arguments for all types of court speeches.I have postponed the methods applicable to political and panegyric speeches, but I now intend to treat them in this book, in order to have the art of finding arguments explained to you in its entirety as soon as possible.Of the four remaining parts of rhetoric, three are covered in the present book, namely, outline, delivery, and memorization.The linguistic formulation requires a more detailed treatment, and I have therefore preferred to discuss that part in the fourth book, which I believe I will be able to quickly complete and send to you, so that you will have access to a complete presentation of the theory of rhetoric.In the meantime, you should learn the basic principles, both in my company when you feel like it and occasionally through study on your own, with the goal that you will be able to keep pace with me without hindrance in acquiring the useful knowledge that is in question.I now ask you to sharpen your attention as I hurry forward towards our set goal.

2政治演讲要么是询问人们应该选择两种行动方案中的哪一种，要么是讨论人们应该选择几种行动方案中的哪一种。前一种类型的例子：什么似乎是最好的选择，是消灭迦太基还是保全迦太基？1后者的一个例子是汉尼拔2当从意大利被召回迦太基时，他会考虑是否应该留在意大利，返回家乡，还是前往埃及占领亚历山大。政治言论中的某些问题也是为了其自身利益而讨论的，例如如果参议院审议是否应该赎回囚犯3是否来自敌人。其他问题则是针对某些外部因素进行讨论和协商，例如如果参议院考虑是否应该将西庇阿从现行法律中豁免，以便他能够在法定最低年龄之前成为执政官。4其他问题可以先就其本身进行讨论，然后再结合一些外部因素提出建议，例如如果盟军战争期间参议院要审议盟军是否应该获得公民身份。5如果问题的性质本身就是讨论的基础，那么整个演讲就应该围绕问题本身展开，但如果讨论是由外部因素引发的，那么恰恰应该强调或淡化这个因素。

2Political speeches are either of the type that ask which of two courses of action one should prefer, or those that discuss which of several courses of action one should prefer.Example of the former type: What seems best, to wipe out or spare Carthage?1An example of the latter is about Hannibal2, when recalled to Carthage from Italy, would consider whether he should remain in Italy, return home, or head for Egypt and capture Alexandria.It is also the case that certain issues within political rhetoric are discussed for their own sake, e.g.if the Senate were to deliberate on whether it should ransom prisoners3from the enemy or not.Others are brought up for discussion and consultation with regard to some external factor, e.g.if the Senate were to consider whether it should exempt Scipio from the current law, so that he could become consul before the legal minimum age.4Other issues can be discussed first for their own sake and then turned into advice with some external factor in mind, e.g.if the Senate during the Allied War were to deliberate on whether the allies should receive citizenship or not.5In cases where the nature of the question itself is the basis for the discussion, the entire speech should revolve around the question itself, but in cases where an external factor gives rise to the discussion, it is precisely this factor that should either be emphasized or downplayed.

3谈论政治问题的演讲者应该在整个演讲过程中牢记实用性，以便将整个演讲的结构导向这一目标。政治演讲中的利益可以从两个不同的角度进行分析，即安全[情侣号角] 和荣誉[诚实地说]。

3Speakers who speak on a political issue should keep the utility aspect in mind throughout their speeches, so that they direct the structure of the entire speech towards this goal.The benefit is analyzed in political speeches from two different aspects, namelysecurity[couple's horn] andhonor[pars honesta].

（1）安全方面的目标是通过一切可用手段避免迫在眉睫或逐渐威胁的危险。其中包括武装部队[显示] 和列表[dolus]，我们可以单独处理，也可以一起处理。

(1) The safety aspect aims to avoid an imminent or gradually threatening danger by all available means.It includesarmed force[show] andlist[dolus], which we can either treat separately or together.

（a）武装力量由陆军、海军、武器、投掷机器、征兵等决定。

(a) Armed force is determined by armies, navies, weapons, throwing machines, conscription of men and the like.

(b) 该诡计利用金钱、承诺、伪装、草率行动、谎言和其他手段来达到其目的，如果将来我想写一些关于军事科学或公共管理的东西，我可以在更合适的时候讨论这个问题。6

(b) The ruse uses money, promises, pretense, hasty action, lies, and other means for its purposes, which I can discuss at a more appropriate time, if at some future time I feel like writing something about military science or public administration.6

（2）光荣的分裂为正确的事情[直肠] 和值得称赞的[值得称赞]。

(2) The honorable disintegrates intothe right thing[rectum] andthe praiseworthy[laudable].

（a） 正确的事情是按照美德和责任去做的事情。它又分解成智慧[审慎]，义[正义]，勇敢[坚韧] 和适度[谦逊]。7智慧意味着系统地区分善恶的能力。智慧这个词也用来指某一科学的知识；同样，智慧可以表示良好的记忆力和在各种事业中的经验。正义根据每件事物的特定价值赋予其自身的权利。勇敢意味着追求功绩，蔑视微不足道，为了一定利益而忍受艰辛。节制是一种能够控制欲望的性格。

(a) The right thing is that which is done in accordance with virtue and duty.It in turn decomposes intowisdom[prudentia],righteousness[justice],bravery[fortitudo] andmoderation[modesty].7Wisdom means the ability to systematically distinguish good from evil.The word wisdom is also used to refer to knowledge in a particular science; wisdom can also denote good memory and experience in a variety of undertakings.Justice grants each thing its own right according to its particular value.Bravery involves a pursuit of feats and a contempt for the insignificant, as well as enduring hardship for the sake of a calculated benefit.Temperance is a disposition that is able to control desires.

4我们可以在言语中运用智慧的各个方面作为论据，例如，当我们推荐一种选择而不建议另一种选择时，通过比较优点和缺点，或者在某些问题上主张采取这样的措施，我们自己可以知道如何在实践或理论上处理问题的所有细节，或者在我们可以诉诸自己或他人的经验的问题上推荐一种行动方案；在这种情况下，通过举例，我们可以很容易地说服我们的听众。

4We can use wisdom in its various aspects as a source of argument in our speech by comparing advantages with disadvantages, when we recommend one alternative but advise against another, or by pleading in some matter for such measures where we ourselves can possess knowledge of how the matter in all its details should be handled practically or theoretically, or by recommending a course of action in a matter where we can appeal to our own or others' experiences; in such a case we can easily convince our listeners by citing examples.

当我们强调对无辜者和乞求宽恕的人表示怜悯的必要性时，当我们提醒我们要以感激之心回报应得的人时，当我们指出对做错事的人进行报复的必要性时，当我们主张必须无条件地遵守诺言时，当我们强调尊重国家法律和习俗的特殊重要性时，当我们强调严格遵守条约和友好联盟的重要性时，当我们阐明我们有义务严格履行自然赋予我们对父母、神和祖国的义务时，当我们强调无私地照顾客人、委托人、血亲和姻亲的重要性时，当我们表明无论是奖励、恩惠、危险还是敌意都不能给我们偏离正道的权利时，最后，当我们强调在所有事务中确立法律面前人人平等的必要性时，正义的各个方面都为我们提供了论据。借助这些以及类似的源于正义的论据，我们将表明，我们希望在人民议会或某些委员会中倡导的立场是正义的，同时，我们将用相反的论据来证明另一种立场是不正义的。这意味着我们可以对建议性言论和劝阻性言论使用相同类型的论点。

Justice in its various aspects gives us arguments when we emphasize the necessity of showing mercy to the innocent and to those who beg for mercy, when we recall the propriety of repaying the deserving with our gratitude, when we point out the necessity of exacting revenge on wrongdoers, when we assert that promises must be kept unconditionally, when we emphasize the special importance of respecting the laws and customs of the state, when we emphasize the importance of strictly observing treaties and friendly alliances, when we clarify our duty to scrupulously fulfill the obligations to parents, gods and fatherland that nature has imposed on us, when we emphasize the importance of unselfishly caring for guests, clients, blood relatives and those related by marriage, when we show that neither rewards, favor, danger nor enmity give us the right to leave the right path, and finally when we emphasizes the necessity of establishing equality before the law as a guideline in all matters.With the help of these and similar arguments taken from justice, we shall show that the position we may wish to advocate in the people's assembly or in some committee is just, while with opposing arguments we demonstrate the unjustness of another position.This means that we can use the same type of argument for both recommendatory and discouraging speech.

5但是，如果我们将坚持英勇的必要性作为采取某种行动的动机，我们就可以强调设定和争取重要而崇高的目标是多么必要，因此，那些卑鄙和不值得勇敢者采取的行为应该被勇敢者拒绝，并被认为有损他们的尊严。此外，我们还要强调，巨大的危险和艰辛的努力绝不能成为放弃光荣政策的理由，死亡比鼻子更好，任何痛苦都不能迫使我们背叛我们的职责，在捍卫真理的过程中，人们绝不能害怕任何人的敌意，人们必须准备好面对一切危险，为祖国、父母、客人、朋友以及正义要求我们尊重的一切付出一切努力。

5But if we cite as a motive for a certain course of action the necessity of persevering in valor, we can emphasize how necessary it is to set and strive for important and lofty goals, and that actions that are base and unworthy of brave men should therefore be rejected by brave men and considered beneath their dignity.Furthermore, we can emphasize that great dangers and difficult efforts must not serve as a reason for abandoning an honorable policy, that death is preferable to the nose, that no pain can force us to betray our duty, that one must not fear hostility from anyone in one's defense of the truth, and that one must be prepared to face every danger and endure every effort for the fatherland, parents, guests, friends, and all that righteousness commands us to respect.

当我们谴责对荣誉、金钱和类似事物的过度渴望时，当我们让自然界划定每件事物的界限并向每个人展示什么是最足够的，当我们建议不要走得太远，当我们在所有情况下都指出正确的尺度时，适度的论点就会发挥作用。

Arguments taken from moderation come into use when we condemn excessive desire for honor, money, and similar things, and also when we let nature draw the limits of each individual thing and show what is most sufficient for each individual, when we advise against going too far, and when we indicate the right measure in all contexts.

6如果我们认为以这种方式从各种美德中得出的论点不值得考虑，那么这些论点的各个部分都应该被淡化。那么，这个想法就是，上述论点只是显得不那么重要——任何人都不可能相信一个人应该做出违背美德的行为。相反，人们可以声称事情并非如此，它给了我们理由去调动任何一种重要的美德，或者争辩说美德在于与上述相反的品质。如果可能的话，我们将表明对方所谓的正义实际上是懦弱、懒惰和误导性的慷慨；我们把他所谓的智慧归类为不相关的、空洞的和令人厌恶的知识；他所谓的温和，我们称之为昏睡和轻浮的冷漠，他所谓的勇敢，我们称之为角斗士的不分皂白的鲁莽。

6Arguments drawn in this way from various virtues should be toned down in all their parts, if we believe that they do not deserve consideration.The idea is then that the above-mentioned arguments are only presented as less important – it is out of the question that anyone would believe that one should act contrary to virtue.Instead, one can either claim that the matter is not of that nature, that it gives us reason to mobilize any single important virtue, or argue that virtue rather lies in qualities opposite to those cited.If it is possible, we shall show that what the opponent calls justice is in reality cowardice, sloth and misguided liberality; what he calls prudence we shall classify as irrelevant, garrulous and obnoxious knowledge; what he calls moderation we shall call lethargy and frivolous indifference; and what he calls bravery we shall call the injudicious recklessness of a gladiator.

7(b) 值得称赞的是，无论是在事情发生时还是在事情发生后，都能留下光荣遗产的事情。我选择单独处理值得赞扬的事情，并不是因为权利概念所包含的美德通常不会带来如此光荣的遗产，而是因为值得赞扬的事情当然源于权利，但却要求我们作为说话者对其进行与权利不同的处理。因此，在我们证明某件事是正确的之后，我们还必须证明它值得合格的评估者赞扬（例如，想象上级批准某件事，而下级不批准某件事），同盟国或全体公民，外国人民以及我们的后代。

7(b) What is praiseworthy is that which produces an honorable legacy, both at the time of the matter and later.I have chosen to treat the praiseworthy separately, not because the virtues encompassed by the concept of right would not usually lead to such an honorable legacy, but because the praiseworthy, which certainly has its origin in right, nevertheless requires that we as speakers give it a treatment separate from this.So, after we have shown that something is right, we must also show that it is worth praising by qualified assessors (if, for example,imagines that a higher estate gives its approval to something that a lower estate disapproves), of allies or all citizens, of foreign peoples and of our descendants.

在政治演讲中，论点是这样分布的，因此我现在将简要解释如何处理个案的各个部分。引言可以设计成直接开始，也可以设计成谨慎的方式，或者按照与法庭演讲相同的原则。如果事实陈述变得相关，则也应遵循相同的方法。

In a political speech, the arguments are thus distributed in this way, and I will therefore now briefly explain how to handle an individual case in all its parts.The introduction can be designed either as a direct start or as a cautious approach, or according to the same principles as in a court speech.If a factual presentation becomes relevant, the same method should also be followed there.

8因此，此类言语的目的在于实用，而实用又可分解为安全和荣誉两个方面。如果我们可以表明我们的立场考虑到了两者，我们就应该在演讲中致力于沿着这两条路线进行论证，但如果我们选择只沿着一条路线进行论证，我们只需解释我们将倡导哪种立场。现在假设我们打算以安全方面为基础进行推理。在这种情况下，我们将划分为武装部队[显示] 和规划[理事会]。对于我刚才在演讲中为了澄清和强调事情的实际含义而称之为“狡猾”的事情，我们作为演讲者应该用一个更体面的名字来称呼它为“策划”。如果我们声称正确的事物支配着我们的立场，并且正确的事物在其各个部分都是适用的，那么我们也应该利用这种四重划分；但如果不是所有的方面都可以考虑的话，我们就会引用尽可能多的方面。

8The purpose of speech within this genre is thus utility, and it in turn decomposes into the aspects of security and honor.If we can show that our position takes both into account, we should commit ourselves to arguing along both lines in our speech, but if we choose to argue along only one line, we simply explain which position we will advocate.Let's now say that we intend to base our reasoning on the security aspect.In that case, we will make a division intoarmed force[show] andplanning[council].For what I just called “cunning” in my presentation in order to clarify and emphasize the actual meaning of the matter, we as speakers should call “planning” with a more decent name.If we claim that what is right governs our position, and if what is right in all its parts is applicable, then we shall also make use of this fourfold division; but if not all aspects can be considered, we shall cite as many as do.

当我们想要证实先前提出的论点并反驳相反的论点时，就会用到证明和反驳的要素。第二本书解释了如何有条不紊地展开论证。8

The elements of proof and refutation come into use when we want to substantiate the previously presented arguments on our own behalf but refute the opposing ones.The way to methodically develop an argument is explained in the second book.8

但如果在一次会议中，一方以安全为依据，另一方以荣誉为依据，就像迦太基人所包围的那些人一样9在考虑采取什么措施时，安全倡导者应该使用以下论点。没有什么比安全更有益；任何人若不先按照安全的要求进行规划，就不能发挥自己的功绩；那些漫无目的地将自己暴露在危险中的人，即使是神也不会帮助；任何不能带来安全感的事情都不应被视为光荣。

But if in a council it happens that one party bases its position on the aspect of security and the other on the demands of honor, according to the example of those surrounded by the Carthaginians9When considering what measures to take, the advocate for security should use the following arguments.Nothing is more advantageous than security; no one can make use of his merits unless he has first planned according to the requirements of security; not even the gods help those who aimlessly expose themselves to danger; nothing should be considered honorable that does not create security.

9那些更愿意按照荣誉的要求而不是安全的要求进行辩护的人可以利用这些论点：任何时候都不能放弃美德；如果人们害怕痛苦，如果人们害怕死亡，那么痛苦和死亡都比羞辱和耻辱轻得多；人们应该考虑从耻辱中能得到什么——当然不是永生或永久的安全——而且没有人能保证，通过避免第一个危险，我们就能逃脱后一个危险；美德以不视死亡为极限为荣；甚至运气通常也会帮助勇气。10；生活光荣的人才能生活安全，而不是目前处于安全之中的人，而生活不光荣的人不可能永远安全。

9Those who prefer to plead in accordance with the demands of honor rather than those of security can use these arguments: Virtue must never be abandoned; both pain, if it is the one feared, and death, if it is the one feared, weigh less than shame and dishonor; one should consider what is gained by dishonor—certainly not immortality or permanent security—and there is no guarantee that by avoiding the first danger we will escape the latter; virtue places an honor in not perceiving even death as a limit; fortune also tends to come to the aid of bravery.10; it is he who lives honorably who lives in security, not he who is currently in security, while he who lives in dishonor cannot possibly be secure forever.

一般来说，这种类型的演讲往往与审判类型的演讲结尾相同，但在政治演讲中，特别适合引用尽可能多的历史例子。

In general, speeches in this genre tend to have the same endings as in the trial genre, with the exception that in political speeches it is particularly appropriate to cite as many examples from history as possible.

10我们现在来讨论颂词演说体裁（genus demonstrativum）。因为它包含赞扬和责备，所以赞扬的论据也应该通过诉诸其对立面来作为责备的基础。赞美的对象是外部环境[外在事物]，物理特性[语料库] 和性格特征[敌意]。

10We shall now turn to the genre of panegyric oratory [genus demonstrativum].Since it encompasses praise and blame, the arguments used for praise should also serve as a basis for blame by resorting to their opposites.The object of praise isexternal circumstances[external things],physical properties[corpus] andcharacter traits[animus].

(1) 外部环境包括可能因偶然、运气或不幸而发生的事物：血统、教养、财富、各种形式的影响力、声誉、公民身份、友谊和类似事物，以及它们的对立面。

(1) External circumstances include things that can occur by chance, luck or misfortune: lineage, upbringing, wealth, influence in various forms, reputation, citizenship, friendships and similar things, as well as their opposites.

(2) 身体特征包括大自然赋予我们身体的优点或缺点：速度、力量、美丽、健康以及它们的反面。

(2) Physical characteristics include the advantages or disadvantages that nature has given to our body: speed, strength, beauty, health and their opposites.

（3） 性格特征包括那些基于我们的判断和思考的特征：智慧、正义、勇气、节制以及它们的对立面。

(3) Character traits include those that are based on our judgment and our thinking: wisdom, justice, courage, moderation, and their opposites.

11这些都是在这种言论中应该用来证明和反驳的东西。介绍（直接开头类型）基于我们自己，从我们要讨论的是从观众或来自事物本身。

11These are the things that should be used for proof and refutation in this type of speech.The introduction (of the direct beginning type) is based onourselves,fromthe one we are going to talk about,fromthe audienceor fromthe thing itself.

（1）从我们自己开始：在悼词中，我们首先要说，要么是因为我们之间的友谊，责任要求我们发言；要么是因为我们同情心驱使我们必须发言，因为所赞扬的人的功绩是如此重要，每个人都应该渴望回忆这些功绩；要么是因为我们这样做是因为如果对一个人的赞扬能显示出他具有什么样的品格，那就太好了。在指责性演讲中，我们应该强调，对方应该受到指责，因为他对待我们的方式，或者我们是在原则性承诺的基础上发表讲话，因为我们发现紧迫的他的突出的邪恶和悲惨将被所有人所知，或者因为通过指责他人来澄清我们自己的价值会给我们带来满足感。

(1) Starting from ourselves: in a eulogy we begin by saying either that duty bids us speak because of the bonds of friendship between us, or that we are impelled to do so by our sympathies, because the merits of the person in question are of such a nature that everyone should feel a desire to recall them, or that we do so because it is good if the praise of a person shows what kind of character he has.In a blaming speech, we should emphasize that the person in question deserves to be blamed because of how he has treated us, or that we are speaking out of a principled commitment, as we find iturgentthat his outstanding evil and wretchedness will become known to everyone, or because it gives satisfaction to clarify what we ourselves value through the blame of others.

(2) 从我们将要谈论的人开始：在悼词中，我们说我们担心我们无法找到足够的词语来描述他的善行，每个人都应该宣扬他的功绩，但他的功绩却让所有赞美他的人都无法用言语表达。在训斥演讲中，我们应该说一些似乎可以通过改变几个词来表达相反意思的话，我只是举了一个例子。

(2) Starting from the one we are going to speak about: in a eulogy we say we fear that we cannot find words sufficient for his good deeds, that everyone should proclaim his merits but that his exploits defy the eloquence of all those who praise him.In a reprimanding speech, we should say what, with a few words changed, seems to be able to be said with the opposite meaning, of which I just gave an example.

12（3）从听众开始：在悼词中，我们声明我们将非常简短，仅回顾所讨论的人的功绩，因为听众已经认识他；另一方面，如果他不为人知，我们就应该努力让听众产生认识这样一个人的愿望：因为听到我们悼词的人会感受到悼词对象所知道或感受到的同样的对美德的承诺，我们希望能够轻易地让那些我们希望的人喜欢这个人的事迹。谴责性演讲则相反：由于听众对所讨论的个人有所了解，我们解释说，我们只想用几句话来谈谈他的悲惨遭遇；如果他们不认识他，我们就应该努力让他们认识他，以避免他的邪恶；由于观众与我们所谴责的对象毫无相似之处，我们坚信他们会厌恶地拒绝他的生活方式。

12(3) Starting from the audience: in a eulogy we explain that we should be very brief with the intention of only recalling the merits of the person in question, since he is already known to the audience; if, on the other hand, he is unknown, we should try to give the audience a desire to get to know such a man: since those who hear our eulogy feel the same commitment to virtue that the object of the eulogy has known or feels, we hope to be able to easily get those we wish to like the man's deeds.A reproachful speech goes in the opposite direction: since the audience knows the individual in question, we declare that we intend to speak in just a few words about his wretchedness; but if they do not know him, we shall try to make them know him in order to avoid his wickedness; since the audience bears no resemblance to the object of our reproach, we express the conviction that they will distance themselves with disgust from his way of life.

（4）从事情本身出发：我们声明自己也不知道我们究竟应该首先赞扬什么；我们担心说了这么多之后，我们还是会忽略更多内容以及其他类似内容。在指责性言论中使用具有相反含义的陈述。

(4) Starting from the matter itself: we declare ourselves not to know exactly what we should praise above all; we fear that after having said much we shall nevertheless pass over still more, and other things of similar content.Statements with the opposite meaning are used in accusatory speech.

十三如果按照刚才提到的其中一种方法进行介绍，则不一定需要进行任何事实陈述。但如果出现这种情况，例如当我们必须对所谈论的人所做的某些行为进行表扬或责备时，他们应该被包括在第一本书中。11应用给定的事实陈述规则。

13If the introduction is carried out in accordance with one of the methods just mentioned, it does not necessarily need to be followed by any factual presentation.But if such a situation arises, for example when we have to give an account of some action performed by the person we are talking about, with praise or blame, they should be included in the first book.11The given rules for factual presentation are applied.

立场澄清应按以下方式进行。我们阐明我们想要赞扬或责备的事情，然后我们描述感兴趣的事件，观察它们的顺序，以便清楚地了解相关人员做了什么以及他采取了哪些预防措施。但首先要陈述人物性格上的优点或缺点，然后说明他是如何处理外貌特征和外界环境带来的优点或缺点的，以及在这样做的过程中表现出什么样的性格特征。

The clarification of the position shall be carried out in the following manner.We clarify what we intend to praise or blame, then we describe events of interest, observing their order, so that it is clear what the person in question has done and what precautions he has taken.But first, one should state the merits or shortcomings of the person's character, and then show how he has dealt with the advantages or disadvantages caused by physical characteristics and external circumstances, and what character traits he has shown in doing so.

当描述某人的生活时，应遵循以下顺序。

When describing someone's life, the following order should be observed.

（1）在外在情况中，应在悼词中以世系为标题提及该人的祖先；如果他出身高贵，就强调他与祖先平起平坐或超越祖先；如果他出身高贵，就强调他依靠的是自己的功绩，而不是祖先的功绩。在谴责的言辞中，如果有人出身高贵，就会说他给祖先带来了耻辱；尽管他的血统并不显赫，但他也成为了他们的耻辱。关于他的成长经历，悼词中写道，他的整个童年都享受着良好而充满关爱的成长环境，学习了许多有益的知识。这段言论是否带有指责性？<…>12。

(1) In matters of external circumstances, the ancestors of the person in question should be mentioned under the heading of lineage in eulogies; if he is of high birth, it is emphasized that he has been the equal of his ancestors or surpassed them, but if he is of low lineage, it is emphasized that he has relied on his own merits and not those of his ancestors.In a reproachful speech, one says that he has been a disgrace to his ancestors, if he is of noble birth; if his lineage is insignificant, he has nevertheless managed to become a disgrace to them as well.Regarding his upbringing, it is said in eulogies that throughout his childhood he enjoyed a good and nurturing upbringing, filled with useful studies.Is the speech accusatory <…>12.

14（2）接下来，应该谈身体方面的优势。如果一个人天生拥有美丽的外表，那么可以说，这为他带来了赞美，而不是像其他人那样，给他带来伤害和耻辱。如果他异常强壮和敏捷，那他是通过光荣而勤奋的训练才变得如此的；如果他从不生病，那是因为他关心自己的健康，并且有能力控制自己的欲望。在谴责性演讲中，如果当事人拥有上述身体优势，我们会说他滥用了自己像任何角斗士一样，由机会和自然所赋予的优势；如果他不具备这些优点，我们会说，缺乏美貌是唯一不能归咎于他自身放荡的身体缺陷。

14(2) Next, one should move on to bodily advantages.If a person has a beautiful appearance by nature, it is said that it has served him to his praise and not, as is the case with others, to his harm and dishonor.If he is unusually strong and fast, it is because he has become so through honorable and diligent training; if he is never sick, it is because he cares for his own health and his ability to control his desires.In a censuring speech, if the person in question possesses the aforementioned physical advantages, we shall say that he has abused what he, like any gladiator, has been given by chance and nature; if he does not possess these advantages, we shall say that the absence of beauty is the only physical defect that cannot be attributed to his own licentiousness.

（3）然后我们回到外部环境，讨论一下相对于这些环境，他的性格表现出了什么优点或缺点。他曾经富有还是贫穷，担任过什么权力职位，享有什么样的声誉，有过哪些友谊和敌对关系，在与敌人的冲突中表现出什么样的勇气？他为何招致敌意？他对朋友表现出了什么样的忠诚、仁慈和服务？当他富有时他表现如何？当他贫穷时他表现如何？当他掌权时，他表现出了什么样的态度？如果他死了，他的死因是怎样的？十三这又导致了什么结果？

(3) Then we return to the external circumstances to discuss what merits or defects in his character he has shown with regard to them.Has he been rich or poor, what positions of power have he held, what reputation has he enjoyed, what friendships and hostile relations have he had, and what courage has he shown in conflicts with enemies?Why has he incurred enmity?What loyalty, benevolence, and service has he shown to his friends?How has he behaved when he was rich and how when he was poor?What attitudes has he demonstrated when he held a position of power?If he is dead, how was his death?13and what did it lead to?

15但在所有特别适合研究人类性格的情况下，我们都应该检查上述四种美德的适用程度。例如：在赞扬的演讲中，我们应该说一个行为表现出正义，另一个行为表现出勇敢，第三个行为表现出节制，第四个行为表现出谨慎。在斥责演讲中，我们宣称一个行为表明了放纵，另一个行为表明了懦弱，第三个行为表明了愚蠢，第四个行为表明了不诚实。

15But in all those situations where human character lends itself particularly well to study, we should examine the extent to which the four virtues mentioned above are applicable.So for example:In a speech of praise, we should say of one action that it shows justice, of another that it shows bravery, of a third that it shows moderation, and of a fourth that it shows prudence.In a reprimanding speech we declare that one action reveals intemperance, another cowardice, a third stupidity, and a fourth dishonesty.

从这个演讲中可以很清楚地看出应该如何从这三个方面来对待赞扬和责备的演讲，如果我可以补充一点的话，没有必要在赞扬或责备的演讲中考虑所有这些方面，因为通常情况下，并不是所有方面都适用，而且通常它们的适用程度都很小。14，无需提及。因此，我们应该选择那些可能给人留下最深刻印象的部分。

It is quite clear from this presentation how one should treat praise and blame speeches in all three aspects, if I may just add that it is not necessary to consider all of these in praise or blame speeches, since it often happens that not all of them are applicable and just as often that they are applicable to such a small degree.14, that they do not need to be mentioned.One should therefore select the parts that seem likely to make the strongest impression.

结论应该简短，并在演讲结束时以概括的形式呈现。在他们自己期间15在演讲中，我们可以插入几个简短的题外话，并使用一般性的论点。

Conclusions should be short and take the form of a recapitulation at the end of the speech.During themselves15In the speech we can insert several short digressions and use general arguments.

这种类型虽然在实际生活中很少遇到，但仍然不应被忽视。尽管我们可能只有少数机会实践这一点，但这并不意味着我们就会减少尽可能熟练地运用这一技巧的努力，而且，如果这种体裁本身的使用频率较低，那么在法律和政治演讲中仍然经常会有大段的赞扬或谴责的内容。因此，让我们假设这种类型也占据了我们研究精力的相当一部分。

This genre, although rarely encountered in practical life, should still not be neglected.For the fact that we may only have occasion to practice it on a few occasions should not diminish our efforts to do this as skillfully as possible, and if this genre is less often used for its own sake, there are still often long sections in both legal and political speeches that are laudatory or censuring.Let us therefore assume that this genre can also claim a considerable portion of our study effort.

现在我已经完成了修辞学中最困难的部分，并仔细讨论了在每种演讲类型中寻找论据的艺术，现在是时候继续讨论剩余的部分了。因此我现在要谈论性格。

Now that I have finished the most difficult part of rhetoric and carefully treated the art of finding arguments in each type of speech, it is time to move on to the remaining parts.I will therefore now talk about disposition.

16因为我们通过提纲将发现的论点整理好，以便每个论点在陈述中都有其特定的位置，所以有必要研究提纲应该遵循什么方法。有两种类型的大纲：一种遵循艺术规则，而另一个则适应暂时的情况。

16Since it is through the outline that we bring the arguments found into order, so that each of them has its specific place in the presentation, it is necessary to examine what method should be followed for the outline.There are two types of outline: one followsthe rules of art,while the other is adapted totemporary circumstances.

（1）当我们遵守我在第一本书中阐明的戒律时，我们的性格就遵循艺术的规则。16， IE。当我们把演讲分为引言、陈述事实、澄清立场、证据、反驳和结论，并按照我之前的指示在演讲时遵循这个顺序。此外，艺术规则不仅应成为我们处理言语整体方式的基础，也应成为我们处理每个单独论点的基础，因此，我在第二本书中展示的那些17分为陈述、陈述理由、理由支持、修饰和总结。

(1) Our disposition follows the rules of art, when we observe the precepts which I set forth in the first book16, i.e.when we divide the speech into introduction, statement of facts, clarification of position, evidence, refutation and conclusion and follow this order when speaking in accordance with my previous instructions.Furthermore, the rules of art should form the basis not only for our way of disposing speech as a whole, but also for each individual argument, so that those which I have shown in the second book17divided into statement, reason for the statement, support for the reason, embellishment and summary.

17因此，艺术规则提供了两种类型的提纲，一种用于整个演讲，另一种用于个别论点。

17The rules of the art thus provide two types of outline, one for the speech as a whole and another for individual arguments.

（2）但还有另外一种处置方式，那就是说话者在必须放弃正常的顺序时所采取的方式，他可以根据临时情况自行调整方式，例如：如果你以陈述事实或一些非常沉重的话语开始演讲称重辩论或宣读文件，或者在介绍之后先讨论证据，然后再陈述事实，或者对顺序进行任何其他类似的改变。除非情况确实需要，否则这一切都不应该发生。因为如果听众似乎对对方的连珠炮似的讲话完全充耳不闻并失去了注意力，那么跳过介绍是有利的。18并以事实陈述或一些有分量的论点开始演讲。如果证明合适（并不总是必要的），那么您可以返回介绍并提出其主要思想。如果事情看起来很难辩护，以致没有人能够平静地听完介绍，那么你可以先陈述事实，然后再回到介绍的主要思想。如果事实陈述不太可信，就应该提出一些有力的论据。当所讨论的问题本身使得有必要调整艺术所规定的安排并遵守某些规则时，人们往往必须诉诸这种改变和重新安排。

(2) But there is another kind of disposition, and that is that which the speaker resorts to when it is necessary to abandon the regular order, and which he adapts at his discretion to temporary circumstances, e.g.if you start the speech with the statement of facts or something very heavyweighingarguments or by reading out a document, or if after the introduction one moves on to the evidence and only then to the presentation of the facts, or if one makes any other similar change in the order.None of this should happen unless the situation really demands it.Because if the audience seems to have completely turned a deaf ear and lost attention as a result of the other party's barrage of words, then it is advantageous to skip the introduction.18and begin the speech either with the factual presentation or with some weighty argument.If it proves appropriate (it is not always necessary), you can then return to the introduction and present its main idea.If the matter appears to be very difficult to defend, so that no one is able to listen to the introduction with composure, you can start with the presentation of the facts and then return to the main idea of ​​the introduction.If the factual presentation is not very credible, one should start with some weighty argument.One must often resort to changes and rearrangements of this kind when the very question under discussion makes it necessary to adjust the disposition prescribed by art, observing certain rules.

18在证明和反驳论点时，建议遵循以下概要。最有分量的论点放在开头和结尾，中等强度的论点放在中间，那些虽然不具有约束力，但在演讲中并非没有价值的论点，那些单独提出时力量较弱，但与其他论点结合起来就会获得力量和可信度的论点。因为在陈述事实之后，听众急于知道此事是否有证据，因此有必要立即提出一些有力的论据。由于很容易记住最后说了什么，因此在演讲结束时提出一个额外的强有力的论点供观众考虑也是一个优势。如此分配论据将毫无困难地导致事业的胜利，就像战场上整齐排列的士兵一样。

18When it comes to proving and refuting arguments, it is advisable to observe the following outline.The most weighty arguments are placed at the beginning and at the end, with medium-strength arguments placed in between, and those that, while not binding, are not without value in the speech, those that, when presented individually, are weak but that, when combined with others, gain strength and credibility.For immediately after the presentation of the facts, the listener is anxious to know whether there is any evidence in the matter, and it is therefore necessary to immediately present some weighty argument.Since it is easy to remember what was said last, it is also an advantage to also come up with an extra strong argument at the end of the speech for the audience to consider.Such a distribution of arguments will without any difficulty lead to victory in the cause, just as an orderly array of soldiers does in battle.

19许多人认为，演讲者从演讲中获益最多，并且演讲对于产生说服力的贡献最大。就我而言，我很难说在这五个部分中哪一个部分是最重要的。19，但这并不妨碍我坦率地同意这场演出极其重要。因为，如果没有演讲，那么，即使论据充分、语言设计引人入胜、对演讲内容进行巧妙安排、对所有这些内容进行熟练的记忆，也都毫无价值，就如同演讲没有其他部分一样。由于没有关于这个主题的书面介绍（每个人都说几乎不可能对声音、面部表情和手势进行解释，因为这些东西会影响我们的感官），而且表演在演讲艺术中扮演着如此重要的角色，我认为应该仔细研究整个问题。

19Many have argued that it is the presentation that the speaker benefits most from and that it contributes more than anything else to creating persuasion.For my part, I am hardly prepared to say that there is any single part that has the greatest importance out of all five.19, which does not prevent me from quite frankly agreeing that the performance is of extremely great importance.For well-founded arguments, an appealing linguistic design, an artful arrangement of the parts of the speech, and a skillful memorization of all this have as little value without the delivery as the delivery without the other parts.Since there is no written presentation on the subject (everyone has said that it is hardly possible to write an explanation about voice, facial expressions and gestures on the grounds that these things affect our senses) and since performance plays such an important role in the art of speech, I believe that the whole issue should be studied with great care.

演出分为两个部分，语音处理[声音形象] 和肢体语言[身体动作]。

The performance breaks down into two parts,voice processing[figure of voice] andbody language[body movement].

声音有其独特的本质，这是通过有意识的关注和训练获得的。

The voice has its own individual nature, which it acquires through conscious focus and training.

20可以从三个不同的角度来描述：力量[声音大小]，耐力[语气坚定] 和灵活性[声音柔和]。声音的强弱本质上是自然的；声音训练当然可以增强力量，但主要目的是为了保持力量。然而，声音的持久力很大程度上取决于发声训练；朗诵练习20在某种程度上改善了它，但最重要的是保留了它。声音的灵活性，即我们在演讲过程中根据目的改变演讲方式的能力正是朗诵练习所能提供的。出于这些原因，我认为没有必要对声音强度甚至声音耐力提出建议，因为前者是自然的，而后者是通过声音训练来形成的，但我建议人们从熟悉这门艺术的人那里获得声音训练的规则。然而，现在我似乎应该处理声音耐力，即通过朗诵练习来保持声音耐力的程度，以及声音灵活性，这对演讲者来说尤为重要；这也是通过朗诵训练获得的。

20It can be described from three different points of view:strength[magnitude of voice],endurance[firmness of voice] andflexibility[softness of voice].Vocal strength is essentially natural; vocal training can certainly increase strength somewhat, but is primarily intended to preserve it.The endurance of the voice, however, is highly dependent on voice training; declamation exercises20improves it somewhat but above all preserves it.Flexibility in the voice, i.e.Our ability to vary it during speech according to our purposes is something that declamation exercises in particular can provide.For these reasons, I see no reason to give advice about vocal strength, or even about vocal endurance, since the former is natural and the latter is conditioned by vocal training, but I would like to advise that one obtain rules for vocal training from those who are familiar with that art.However, it seems appropriate that I now deal with vocal endurance, namely to the extent that it is maintained through declamation exercises, and vocal flexibility, which is particularly important for the speaker; this too is acquired through training in declamation.

21（1）演讲时保持声音稳定最可靠的方法是在开场白时尽量使用平静、柔和的声音。因为如果在气管因轻松的言语而变得柔软之前就大声喊叫，气管就会受损。还建议加入较长的停顿，因为当你呼吸时声音就会恢复，只要你保持沉默，气管就有时间休息。此外，不要一直大声说话，而是要切换到对话的语调，因为通过变化本身，您可以避免在某个声音水平上浪费精力，而是可以利用整个音域。还应避免大声呼喊；太过尖锐和刺耳的惊呼会造成冲击，损害气管，这样，一声惊呼就可能使声音的响度丧失殆尽。不过，在演讲结束时一口气说完长句子可能是合适的。这会使喉咙温暖并使气管保持充盈。如果你以不同的方式使用你的声音，它就会恢复到平滑而稳定的声音。有多少次，就像这种情况一样，我们没有理由对大自然心存感激？对我来说，有利于声音的保存也有助于表演的愉悦。21，这样既对我们的声音有好处，又能赢得听众的认可。

21(1) The most reliable way to maintain a steady voice during a speech is to use as calm and subdued a voice as possible in the introduction.Because the windpipe is damaged if you fill it with loud shouts before it has had time to soften with relaxed speech.It is also advisable to include longer pauses, as the voice then recovers while you breathe and the trachea has time to rest as long as you remain silent.Furthermore, it is necessary not to speak loudly all the time, but instead switch to a conversational tone, because through the variation itself, you avoid wasting your energy on a certain voice level and can instead utilize the entire register.One should also avoid shrill exclamations; an exclamation that is too sharp and shrill creates a shock that damages the trachea, and thus the sonority of the voice can be lost with a single exclamation.However, it may be appropriate to say long sentences in a single breath at the end of the speech.This warms the throat and keeps the trachea filled.If you use your voice in a varied way, it will find its way back to a smooth and steady sound.How often, just like in this case, do we not have reason to feel grateful to nature?For what I describe as beneficial for the preservation of the voice also contributes to the pleasantness of the performance.21, so that what is good for our voice at the same time wins the listener's approval.

22一开始保持低调的语调有利于保持耐力。还有什么比在演讲开始时把音量开到最大更难看的呢？停顿可以加强声音，通过将句子彼此分开使句子更清晰，并给听众思考的时间。通过不一直大声说话，可以保留声音，而听众则从变化中找到极大的乐趣，因为说话者通过对话的语气吸引听众的注意力，或者通过感叹引起听众的注意。尖锐的叫喊不仅会损害声音，还会刺激听众，因为这种叫喊有失尊严，更适合女性的叫喊，而不适合说话者应有的男性尊严。演讲结束时，语流连续，有利于声音的发声。这难道不是听众在听完整个演讲的结论时最兴奋的事情吗？由于同样的因素促进了声音的耐力和表演的优雅，因此我将两者放在同一个背景下进行讨论，并在这样做的过程中，我提出了我认为合理的关于耐力的观点，以及关于优雅的类似观点。我将在适当的时候讨论剩余的问题。

22It is beneficial for endurance if you maintain a subdued tone of voice at the beginning.What's more unsightly than the highest volume at the beginning of a speech?Pauses strengthen the voice, make sentences clearer by separating them from each other, and they give the listener time to think.The voice is preserved by not speaking loudly all the time, and the listener, for his part, finds great pleasure in the variation, as the speaker keeps his attention captured through conversational tone or arouses it through exclamation.Shrill exclamations damage the voice and also irritate the listener, because they have something undignified about them and are more suitable for women's shouting than for the masculine dignity that should distinguish the speaker.At the end of the speech, a continuous flow of words is beneficial to the voice.And isn't that precisely what most excites the listener when he listens to the conclusion of the entire speech?Since the same things promote the endurance of the voice and the grace of performance, I have treated both in one and the same context, and in doing so, I have presented the views on endurance that I found justified, with similar views also on grace.I will discuss the remaining issues in due course.

23（2）由于声音的灵活性是一个完全属于修辞学理论的问题，因此我有必要对其进行更详细的论述。我们可以把它分成三个音调，即称呼[sermo] 和辩论[contentio] 当我们想要绣[放大]某事。对话语气涉及一种接近日常讲话的轻松声音。在辩论中，使用充满活力的声音，适合证明和反驳。当你修饰某物时，你说话要么激起听众的愤怒，要么激起听众的怜悯。

23(2) Since the flexibility of the voice is a question that falls entirely within the doctrine of rhetoric, it behooves me to devote a more detailed treatment to it.We can divide it into three tones, namely those we use whenCall[sermo] anddebate[contentio] and when we wantembroider[amplification] something.Conversational tone involves a relaxed voice that is close to everyday speech.In debate, an energetic voice is used, suitable for proof and refutation.When you embroider something, you speak to either arouse anger or pity in your audience.

(a) 对话语气有四种不同的用途：内容严肃的段落、解释、事实陈述和笑话。严肃的演讲具有一定的尊严和克制的语气的特点。解释意味着表明某件事可能或不可能发生。事实陈述反映已经发生或可以假定已经发生的事情。通过开玩笑，你可以让听众以得体、有文化的方式嘲笑某事。

(a) Conversational tone is used for four different purposes: in passages with serious content, explanations, statements of fact, and jokes.Serious speech is characterized by a certain dignity and a restrained tone of voice.Explanations mean showing how something could or could not have happened.Factual statements reflect things that have happened or can be assumed to have happened.By joking, you can make your listeners laugh at something in a decent and cultured way.

(b) 在辩论中，人们要么连贯地讲话，要么断断续续地讲话。语流连贯，即语速要快，音量要饱满。辩论中断音很常见，人们说话的声音尖锐刺耳，偶尔会有一些短暂的停顿。

(b) In debates, people speak either coherently or in staccato.The coherent flow of words means a high speech tempo with full voice volume.Staccato is common in debates, and people speak in a sharp and piercing voice, occasionally interrupted by short pauses.

24(c) 绣花意味着煽动和抱怨。煽动性言论是通过夸大犯罪来激起听众愤怒的言论。哀歌是一种通过阐述逆境来引起听者怜悯之心的言语。

24(c) To embroider something means to incite and to complain.Inciting speech is speech that, by exaggerating a crime, provokes anger in the listener.Lamentation is speech that, by expounding on adversity, arouses pity in the listener.

由于声音的灵活性是根据三个不同的音调范围来评估的，而这些音调范围又分为八个使用领域，因此，现在我解释哪种声音治疗适合这八个领域中的每一个似乎是合理的。

Since the flexibility of the voice is assessed with regard to three different tonal ranges and these are in turn divided into eight areas of use, it seems reasonable that I now explain which voice treatment is suitable for each of these eight areas.

（1）当用对话语气表达任何严肃的内容时，应尽量使用平静、柔和的声音，张大喉咙，但不要听起来像个悲剧演员。22而不是扬声器。（2）讲解时，声音要细弱一些，常常插入停顿，并标出各个部分，这样，我们说话的方式本身就给听众留下了将所讲解的内容植入并铭刻在头脑中的印象。（3）在使用对话语气陈述事实时，要注意语调的变化，使之听起来像是在准确地叙述每个事件的发生过程。如果我们想表示某件事做得很快，我们应该说得快一点，但如果我们想表示某件事做得不慌不忙，我们应该放慢速度。然后，我们将尽一切可能使自己的发音适应单词的内容，时而尖锐，时而温和，时而次悲伤或快乐。如果事实报道中有理由引用关于我们报道所关注的事情的陈述、问题、答案或疑惑的表达，我们应该努力用声音表达所有相关人员的感受和想法。

(1) When a conversational tone is used for any passage with serious content, one should use as calm and subdued a voice as possible, with the throat wide open, but not so that one begins to sound like a tragic actor.22instead of a speaker.(2) In explanations one should use a somewhat thinner voice, often inserting pauses and marking separate sections, so that by the very manner of speaking we give the impression of implanting and engraving in the minds of the listeners the things we are explaining.(3) When using conversational tone for factual statements, it is necessary to observe a varying tone of voice, so that it appears as if we are recounting each event exactly as it occurred.If we want to show that something was done quickly, we should speak a little faster, but if we want to indicate that something was done without haste, we should slow down.We shall then in every possible way adapt our pronunciation of the words to their content and speak now sharply, now gently, nowtimessad or happy.If in the factual report there is reason to quote statements, questions, answers or expressions of wonder about the things our report concerns, we should strive to use the voice to express the feelings and thoughts of all the people involved.

二十五（4） 然而，如果用谈话的语气讲笑话，就应该轻轻地让严肃的语气让位于有教养的笑话，声音中略带颤抖，谨慎地露出一丝微笑——但不要有一丝笑意。(5) 在辩论中，无论是连续不断地说话，还是断断续续地说话，我们都应当稍微提高声音，并确保连续不断的词语在发音上得到相应的表达。23语调要有变化，说话要快而响，这样我们才能根据话语的强势流动来调整音量。（6）在断奏总音中，演奏者应该用最深沉的胸腔音调发出尽可能清晰的感叹，我的建议是让每个感叹都伴有同样长的停顿。（7）用劝诫的语气去激怒别人时，声音要很细，力度要适中。您应该观察到均匀的音调形成、频繁的变化和最快的语速。（8）抱怨时，声音要柔和，音调要低，停顿要多，句子要长，转变要明显。至此，语音讲完了，现在似乎该讨论一下肢体语言了。

25(4) If, however, the conversational tone is used for jokes, one should gently let the serious tone give way to cultured jokes with a slight tremor in the voice and a cautious hint of a smile – but without a hint of laughter.When we speak in debates either in a continuous flow of words or in staccato, we should (5) in the former case raise our voice slightly and ensure that the uninterrupted lines of words are given a corresponding expression in the way we pronounce them.23The tone of voice should be varied and the words should be pronounced quickly and loudly, so that we can adjust the volume of our voice to the powerful flow of words.(6) In staccato total, one should produce the clearest exclamations possible with the deepest chest tones, and my advice is to let each exclamation be accompanied by an equally long pause.(7) When we use the tone of exhortation to provoke, the voice should be very thin and moderately strong.You should observe even tone formation, frequent variations and the highest speech tempo.(8) When complaining, we should use a subdued voice, low pitch, frequent pauses, long periods, and clearly marked shifts.With this, the voice is finished, and it now seems appropriate to discuss body language.

二十六肢体语言是指对身体动作和面部表情的控制，以适应并增加所说内容的可信度。24因此，面部表情应适度而活泼，肢体动作不应过分优雅或过分笨拙，这样我们才不会觉得自己是演员或日工。现在，使用声音的不同方式的规则似乎也适用于肢体动作。（1）当用谈话语气谈论严肃的内容时，应该站立不动，用轻柔的右手动作和与谈话内容相适应的面部表情说话，表达出喜悦、悲伤或一些中性的情绪。（2）用对话的语气解释时，身体应从肩膀处稍微向前弯曲。当你想向听众解释某件事并激发他们的浓厚兴趣时，将脸尽可能地靠近听众是一种自然的姿态。（3） 当使用对话语气陈述事实时，可以采用与严肃段落中相同的动作。（4）讲笑话时，我们的外表要表现出一定程度的兴奋，但手势不要改变。

26Body language refers to the control of body movements and facial expressions that suits and lends increased credibility to what is being said.24It is therefore appropriate that the facial expression be characterized by both moderation and liveliness, while the body movements should be neither strikingly graceful nor clumsy, so that we do not see ourselves as actors or day laborers.The rules for the different ways of using the voice now appear to also apply to body movements.(1) For when using a conversational tone for passages with serious content, one should stand still and speak with light right-hand movements and facial expressions that are appropriate to the content of what is being said and that express joy, sadness, or some neutral emotion.(2) When using a conversational tone for explanations, one should bend the body slightly forward from the shoulders.It is a natural gesture to bring your face as close as possible to your audience when you want to explain something to them and arouse their lively interest.(3) When using a conversational tone in factual statements, the same movements as those just indicated for serious passages can be appropriate.(4) When it comes to jokes, we should show a certain level of excitement in our appearance, but without changing our gestures.

二十七（5）如果要用连贯的语言进行辩论，则应选择快速的手臂动作、生动的面部表情和充满活力的目光。（6）但在断奏说话时，应偶尔快速地伸出手臂，来回走动，偶尔跺一下右脚，并用有活力的目光注视某物。（7）如果用脏话的语气来挑衅，适当的姿势要慢一些，要谨慎一些，但除此之外，要遵守辩论规则，说话要连贯。（8）如果用绣花来表示哀悼，可以拍打自己的大腿，用手捶打自己的头，并不时做出缓慢而有规律的手势，表现出悲伤、困惑的神情。

27(5) If debating in a coherent flow of words, one should choose rapid arm movements, a lively facial expression, and an energetic gaze.(6) But when speaking staccato, one should occasionally stretch out one's arm very quickly, walk back and forth, occasionally stamp one's right foot, and fix one's gaze on something with energetic gaze.(7) If you use the tone of the expletive to provoke, it is appropriate to use somewhat slower and more cautious gestures but otherwise follow the rules for debate with a coherent flow of words.(8) If, on the other hand, one uses the embroidering for lamentation, one can slap oneself on the thigh, hit one's head with one's hand, occasionally make slow and regular gestures, and show a sad and confused look.

当我尝试用语言表达肢体动作、用文字模仿语调时，我意识到自己承担的任务十分艰巨。现在我根本没有想到能够以书面形式对这些事情进行详尽的论述。但即使这项任务不可能完成，另一方面，我的观点是，做我所做的事情不会浪费精力，因为我在这里的意图是让人们关注所需要做的事情——剩下的就留给实践吧。然而，你应该记住的一件事是，良好的表演会给人一种错觉，让人觉得所说的话是发自内心的。

I am not unaware of the difficult task I have undertaken, as I have attempted to express body movements in words and imitate voice inflections in writing.Now I have in no way imagined that it would be possible to give an exhaustive treatment of these things in writing.But even if the task were impossible, my opinion, on the other hand, was that it would not be wasted effort to do what I have done, since my intention here has been rather to draw attention to what is required – I leave the rest to practice.One thing you should keep in mind, however, is that a good performance creates the illusion that what is being said comes directly from the heart.

二十八现在让我把这些论证保存在宝库里，交给所有修辞部分的守护者，即记忆[回忆录]。记忆力是否可以通过系统训练得到，或者是否是一种天生的能力，我们将在适当的时候进行讨论。现在我打算讨论这个话题，好像它超越了任何讨论，理论和规则在这里非常重要。就我而言，我相信记忆是有方法的——我将在另一个背景下阐述我的观点的理由。首先，我要向你们介绍记忆的本质。

28Let me now pass to the treasury where the arguments found are preserved, to the guardian of all the parts of rhetoric, namelymemory[memoir].Whether memory can be made the subject of systematic training or is an exclusively natural ability, we will discuss at some other appropriate time.Right now I intend to address the topic as if it were beyond any discussion, that theory and rules are of great importance here.For my part, I believe that there is a method for memorization – I will present the reasons for my opinion in another context.To begin with, I'm going to tell you about the nature of memory.

记忆有两种，一种是自然的，另一种是基于技术的。自然记忆是深植于灵魂之中，与思考能力同时产生的，而技术性记忆则是通过一定的教学和系统的训练而得到强化的。但正如天生的优秀品质也经常与后天习得的优秀品质相竞争，而艺术反过来又加强和增加了我们天生所赋予的优势，所以这里的情况也一样，一个人的自然记忆，如果接受了非常好的二十九通常与基于技术的记忆相似，正如后一种记忆反过来又保留了自然能力，并通过有条不紊的训练提高了自然能力。由此可见，自然记忆应该通过教学来强化，以使其变得更加有效，而通过技术获得的记忆能力则依赖于先天记忆。在这种情况下，这条格言的适用性与其他艺术领域一样，即天赋赋予知识光彩，就像理论知识赋予天赋光彩一样。因此，即使是那些天生记忆力好的人也会受益于我打算留下的规则，你自己很快就会明白这一点。即使这些人凭借其天生的能力并不需要我们的帮助，我们仍然有正当理由去帮助那些天生记忆力不太好的人。我现在打算从技术角度来解决记忆问题。

There are two kinds of memory, one of which is natural and the other based in technology.Natural memory is embedded in our soul and arose simultaneously with the ability to think, while technically based memory is strengthened by a certain type of teaching and systematic training.But just as natural excellence also often competes with learned excellence, and art in turn strengthens and increases the advantages we have bestowed upon us by nature, so it is the same here, so that the natural memory of an individual who has received a very good one29is often similar to the memory based on technology, just as the latter type of memory in turn preserves and through methodical training improves the natural ability.It follows from this that natural memory should be strengthened through teaching, so that it becomes extra effective, and that the memory ability acquired through technology is dependent on innate memory.The maxim applies no more or less in this case than in other arts, that talent lends brilliance to knowledge, in the same way that theoretical knowledge lends brilliance to innate talent.Even those who have a good memory by nature will therefore benefit from the rules I intend to leave, something that you yourself will soon understand.And even if such people, relying on their innate ability, did not need our help, there would still be legitimate reason for our desire to assist those whose innate memory is not as good.I now intend to address the memory based on technology.

基于技术的记忆包括地方[基因座] 和图片[想象]。我所说的地方是指自然或人类赋予的有形、引人注目且本身完整的形式的事物，以便我们能够轻松地将其附加并保留在我们的自然记忆中，例如建筑物、两根柱子之间的空间、角落、拱门等。图像是我们想要记住的某些图形、符号和象征。例如，如果我们如果我们想记住一匹马、一头狮子或一只鹰，我们应该把它们的图片放在特定的地方。

The technology-based memory consists ofplaces[loci] andpictures[imagines].By places I mean things that either nature or man has given a tangible, eye-catching and in itself completely complete form, so that we are easily able to attach and retain it in our natural memory, e.g.a building, the space between two columns, a corner, an arch, and the like.Images are certain figures, signs and symbols for what we want to remember.If we, for example,If we want to remember a horse, a lion or an eagle, we should place pictures of them in specific places.

三十现在我将向您展示要考虑什么样的地方以及如何找到要放置在那里的图片。

30I will now show you what kind of places to think about and how to find pictures to place there.

(1) 就像识字的人可以根据听写来书写并阅读所写的内容一样，掌握记忆术的人也可以将所听到的内容放在这样的地方，并借助记忆从那里检索出来。这些地方与蜡或纸莎草有着非常明显的相似之处，图像与信件有着非常明显的相似之处，图像的排列和位置与书写有着非常明显的相似之处，而呈现方式与阅读有着非常明显的相似之处。如果我们想要记住很多东西，我们就必须获得很多地方，以便能够在这些众多的地方放置各种各样的图像。我认为，还必须将地点按一定的顺序排列，这样，顺序的缺乏就不会妨碍我们从任何地点开始寻找图像的能力，无论其位于开始或结束的位置，并且在我们的演示中呈现赋予这些地点的东西。为了进行比较，我们可以假设我们看到大量熟人站成一排。那么，从队伍的开头、结尾还是中间开始列出它们的名字对我们来说都无所谓了，对于按一定顺序排列的地方也是如此：无论我们从哪一端开始，选择哪个地方，我们都可以通过图像的提醒来报告我们对这些地方的委托。

(1) Just as literate people can write from dictation and read what they have written, in the same way those who master mnemonics can place what they have heard in such places and, with the help of memory, retrieve it from there.The places bear a very tangible resemblance to wax or papyrus, the images to letters, the arrangement and placement of the images to writing, and the presentation to reading.If we want to remember a lot, we must therefore acquire many places in order to be able to place a variety of images in this multitude of places.In my opinion, it is also necessary to place the places in a certain sequence, so that lack of order does not hinder our ability to find the images, starting from any place and regardless of its location at the beginning or end, and in our presentation to present what has been entrusted to these places.For the sake of comparison, we can assume that we see a large number of our acquaintances standing in a line.Then it doesn't matter to us whether we start listing their names from the beginning, end or middle of the line, and the same goes for places that are placed in a certain order: whichever end we start at and whichever place we choose, we will be able to report what we have entrusted to the places by being reminded by the images.

31因此，位置也应按照特定的顺序排列。

31For this reason, the places should also be placed in a specific order.

我们应该格外小心地去选择那些地方，让它们永远铭刻在我们的记忆中。因为图像就像字母一样，在不再需要时就会被删除，而位置——就像蜡一样——应该是永久的。为了避免我们意外地犯下位置数量的错误，建议每五个位置标记一次。例如，如果我们第五名是金手，第十名是我们熟悉的德西姆斯二十五，那么接下来就很容易将相似的字符放在第五个位置上。

We should inculcate the places we have chosen with extra care, so that they are forever etched in our memory.For while images, like letters, are erased when they are no longer needed, places – like wax – should be permanent.And so that we do not accidentally make a mistake regarding the number of places, it is advisable to mark every fifth one.If we, for example,marks the fifth place with a golden hand and the tenth with someone familiar to us with the first name Decimus25, it then becomes easy to place similar characters in every fifth place in the following.

此外，将拍摄地点放置在荒凉地区比放置在人口稠密的地区更有效，因为来回走动的人群会干扰图像并使其变得不那么清晰，而人口稀少的地区则可以完整地保留这些人物。此外，您应该选择外观和特征不同的位置，以便它们彼此之间能够明显区分开来。因为如果有人让一行中的几个列空间构成位置，相似性会让他感到困惑，这样他就不知道在每个位置上放了什么。它们的尺寸和范围也应该适中，因为如果它们太大，图像就会不清楚，但另一方面，如果它们太小，它们往往似乎无法应对放置在那里的图像。

Furthermore, it is more effective to place the locations in a deserted area than in a densely populated area, because the amount of people moving back and forth disturbs and makes the images less sharply defined, while an unpopulated area preserves these figures intact.Furthermore, you should select locations that are different in appearance and characteristics, so that they can appear clearly separated from each other.For if someone lets several column spaces in a row constitute places, the similarity will confuse him, so that he will not know what he has placed in each individual place.They should also be moderate in size and extent, because if they are too large the images will be unclear, but if, on the other hand, they are too small they often seem unable to cope with images being placed there.

三十二此外，拍摄地点不能太亮也不能太暗，以免图像被阴影或光线遮挡。各个地方之间的空间应该适度大，比如说大约 30 英尺，因为想象力就像视觉一样，无论将要观察的事物移得太远还是太近，都会变得更弱。

32In addition, the locations must be neither too bright nor too dark, so that the images are not obscured by shadows or glare from the light.The spaces between the places should be moderately large, let us say about 30 feet, for the power of imagination, like vision, will otherwise become weaker, whether one moves the thing to be viewed too far away or very close.

现在，对于已经获得了更广泛的知识的人来说，想出任意数量的运作良好的场所当然是很容易的。尽管如此，那些不相信自己能找到足够好的地方的人仍然可以想到任意多的地方。在你的想象中，你可以想象任何区域并设计和建造任何你想要的地方。如果您对我在这里提供的座位不满意，那么您可以发挥自己的想象力，设计一个供您自己使用的区域，并在那里放置合适且方便的独立座位。关于这些地方，说的已经够多了。我们现在将讨论图像及其功能。

Now it is certainly easy for someone who has acquired somewhat more extensive knowledge to think up any number of well-functioning places.Nevertheless, anyone who may not believe they can find places that are good enough can still think of as many as they want.In your imagination, you can imagine any area and design and construct any place you want.If you are not satisfied with the supply of places that I have made available here, you can therefore use your own imagination to devise an area for your own use and place suitable and conveniently accessible, separate places there.That's enough to say about the places.We will now turn to the images and how they function.

33（2）既然图像必须与所描述的事物相似，我们自己就应该选择与所有可能的事物相似的事物供自己使用。那么相似之处应该分为两类，其中之一涉及那些东西[res] 和其他文字[动词]。与事物的相似性表现在我们对具体事物创建概括图像时，而与词语的相似性则形成于将每个专有名词或称谓的记忆与图像联系起来时。

33(2) Since the images must resemble the things depicted, we ourselves should make a selection of similarities with all possible things for our own use.The similarities should then be of two types, one of which concernsthe things[res] and the otherthe words[verb].Similarities with things are expressed when we create summary images of the specific thing, while similarities with words are formed when the memory of each individual proper name or appellative is linked to an image.

（a）我们常常可以通过一个符号或一个图像来记住一件事物的全部内容，如下例所示。公诉人指控，被告人毒害了一名男子，且其犯罪动机是继承财产，并进一步解释说，有许多目击证人和知情人士。如果我们希望记住这一点以便于我们进行辩护，我们必须首先对整个事情有一个大致的了解。如果我们能记住这个人的长相，我们就应该让他卧病在床。但是，如果我们不认识这个人，我们就应该想象某个出身不太低微的病人，这样我们就能更快地回忆起他。我们将被告安置在床边，让他右手拿着一个杯子，左手拿着写字板，同一只手的无名指上拿着一只公羊的睾丸。二十六这样，我们就能记住目击者、遗产和中毒者。

(a) We can often remember a thing in its entirety through a single sign or a single image, as in the following example.The prosecutor has alleged that the defendant poisoned a man and that inheritance was the motive for the act, and he has further explained that there are many witnesses and insiders.If we wish to commit this first point to memory to facilitate our defense, we must form a picture of the whole matter in our first place.If we can remember the appearance of the man in question, we should leave him to lie sick in bed.But if the person in question was unknown to us, we should imagine some sick man of not too low birth, so that he can be recalled to memory that much more quickly.We place the accused by his bed and let him hold a cup in his right hand, writing tablets in his left hand, and on the ring finger of the same hand the testicles of a ram.26That way we can remember both the witnesses, the legacy and the poisoned man.

三十四然后我们把其他的指控点依次放在如下的位置，一旦我们想要回忆什么，我们就可以借助这些特殊的位置和精心标记的图片，轻松地在记忆中查找我们想要的东西。

34Then we place the other points of accusation in turn in the following places, and as soon as we want to recall something, we can easily look up what we want in our memory with the help of the special places and the carefully marked pictures.

(b) 当我们用图像来表达与文字的相似性时，我们承担了更艰巨的任务，并且不得不更加绞尽脑汁。我们应该按照以下方式解决该任务：

(b) When we use images to express similarities with words, we take on a more difficult task and are forced to rack our brains more.We should solve that task in the following way:

我是我的主宰者二十七父母

Iam domum itionem reges Atndae27parant

（“现在，阿特柔斯的儿子们开始返回家园”）

(“Now the sons of Atreus begin their return journey home”)

如果我们想要记住这节经文，那么首先应该让多米提乌斯双手伸向天空，站在那里，接受马修斯雷克斯 (Marcius Rex) 家族成员的鞭打。二十八– 这对应于现在，我要回家见国王了。其次，伊索普斯和辛贝尔在《阿伽门农和墨涅拉俄斯》中扮演阿伽门农和墨涅拉俄斯。伊菲革涅亚二十九 –它对应于蛛科一对三十。这样，所有的词31来表达。但是，只有当我们设法通过符号本身来刺激自然记忆时，这种图形表示的安排才会有效，这样我们才能对自己重复两到三遍相关的诗句。次然后再把文字用图画表达出来。这种方法意味着利用技术来帮助自然。因为如果两者都适用，那么如果失去了对方的支持，它们就会失去效力，然而，技术和理论却能带来更大的好处。如果不是担心这样会偏离我的意图，我就无法保持我在演讲中追求的简洁性和清晰度，我会毫不犹豫地进一步调查这个问题。

If we want to remember this verse, it is appropriate to first have a Domitius standing with his hands stretched out to the sky while being whipped by members of the Marcius Rex family.28– this then corresponds toNow, I am going home to the kings.In the second place, Aesopus and Cimber are dressed up for the roles of Agamemnon and Menelaus inIphigenia29 –it corresponds toAtridae pair30. In this way, all words will31to expression.But such an arrangement of pictorial representations only works if we manage to stimulate the natural memory through the notation itself, so that we repeat to ourselves the verse in question two or three times.timesand only then express the words in pictures.This method means that nature is helped by technology.For if both apply, they lose in force if they are deprived of the support of the other, with the addition, however, that technology and theory are of considerably greater benefit.I would not hesitate to investigate this further, were it not for my fear that by thus deviating from my intention I would not succeed in maintaining the brevity and clarity I strive for in my presentation.

三十五现在通常会出现这样的情况：一些图像强烈、清晰，很适合回忆，而另一些图像则模糊、微弱，几乎无法唤起记忆。因此，考虑造成这些差异的原因非常重要，这样通过了解原因，我们就可以知道应该避免哪些图像以及应该努力追求哪些图像。这里的情况是，大自然本身教会了我们应该如何进行。对于我们在生活中遇到的那些微不足道、普通而又平凡的事情，我们通常不会记住它们，因为在这种情况下，我们的心灵不会受到任何新事物或引起我们惊奇的事物的影响。但是如果你看到或听到一些特别可耻、不光彩、不寻常、宏大、难以置信或荒谬的事情，你往往会记住它很长时间。你刚才听到的大部分内容都被遗忘了，而你往往对童年时期发生的事情记忆犹新，其原因无非是日常事物很容易被遗忘，而那些不寻常的和以前未知的事物则会保留更长时间。

35Now it usually happens that some images are strong, sharp and well suited for recall, while others are unclear and weak and almost incapable of evoking memories.It is therefore important to consider what causes these differences, so that with knowledge of the cause we can know which images we should avoid and which we should strive for.The situation here is that nature itself teaches us how we should proceed.For the insignificant, common, and mundane things we are confronted with in life, we usually do not remember them because in such cases the mind is not affected by anything new or something that arouses our wonder.But if you see or hear something that is particularly shameful, dishonorable, unusual, grand, incredible, or ridiculous, you tend to remember it for a long time.Most of what you heard just now is forgotten, while you often have very clear memories of things that happened during childhood, and the reason for this can be none other than that everyday things easily fall out of memory, while the unusual and the previously unknown remain longer.

三十六太阳的升起、运行和落下并不奇怪，因为它们每天都在重复；但日食之所以引起人们的惊奇，是因为它很少发生，而且日食比月食引起人们更大的惊奇，是因为后者更为常见。因此，大自然表明，它本身并不关注日常和平凡的事物，而是受到新事物和某种引人注目的事件的影响。因此，艺术应该模仿自然，发现自然的愿望并遵循其指示。因为当谈到人类的创造力时，从来不是自然占主导地位、理论训练占主导地位；开始在于先天，最终在于后天的修炼。

36The rising, setting, and setting of the sun are not a cause for wonder because of their daily repetition; but solar eclipses are a cause for wonder because they occur rarely, and solar eclipses are more a cause for wonder than lunar eclipses because the latter are more common.Nature thus shows that it itself does not pay attention to everyday and ordinary things, but that it is influenced by what is new and by events that are striking in some way.Art should therefore imitate nature, find what nature desires and follow its instructions.For when it comes to human inventiveness, it is never the case that nature has the last word and theoretical training the first; the beginning lies in the innate disposition, while the final goal is reached through training.

三十七因此，我们应该创造能够长久保留在我们记忆中的图像。如果我们设计出尽可能引人注目的相似之处，如果我们使用的图像数量不多或不太清晰，但能表达某种动作，如果我们使图像格外美丽或格外丑陋，如果我们用皇冠或紫色衣服装饰其中一些，那么相似性在我们看来就更加明显，或者如果我们以某种方式破坏图像，例如，让其中一个血迹斑斑、满身泥土或涂满红漆，使其看起来更加引人注目，或者让图片包含一些荒谬的细节，因为这也会让我们更容易记住它们。那些容易记住的东西，只要我们用心设计符号，用手指触摸时也很容易记住。但重要的是，我们要不断地用内心的眼睛快速概览所有原始位置，以保持图像的新鲜。

37We should therefore create images of the type that can remain in our memory for a very long time.We succeed in this if we design similarities that are as striking as possible, if we use images that are not too numerous or unclear but that express some kind of action, if we make the images either exceptionally beautiful or exceptionally ugly, if we adorn some of them with crowns or purple clothes, for example, so that the similarity appears that much more marked to us, or if we somehow disfigure the images by, for example,Letting one of them be bloody, covered in dirt or smeared with red paint to give it a much more striking appearance, or by letting the pictures contain some ridiculous details, because that also leads to us remembering them more easily.Things that are easy to remember can also be easily remembered when we finger them, provided we design the signs for them with care.But it is then important that we constantly make quick overviews of all the original places with our inner eyes in order to keep the images current.

三十八我知道，大多数撰写有关记忆的希腊人都选择提供与一定数量的单词相对应的图像列表，以便那些想要记住这些图像的人可以随时获得，而不必费力自己去寻找它们。由于各种原因，我不喜欢他们的系统，主要是因为从无数的单词中获取仅对应一千个的图像是荒谬的。当我们被迫从无穷无尽的词汇中记住一件事又一件事时，它们能有什么用呢？此外，为什么要剥夺某人的主动性，为他们提供现成的一切，让他们不必自己构建任何东西？顺便说一句，人们对相似程度的感知不同。因为，正如我们常常会遇到的情况一样，如果我们说一个外表与另一个外表相似，却得不到所有人的支持，这仅仅是因为人们对事物的看法不同，图像也是如此，因此，我们自己选择的合适的图像在别人看来却很平淡。

38I know that most Greeks who have written about memory have chosen to provide lists of images corresponding to a number of words, so that those who want to learn such images by heart will have a ready supply and will not have to make the effort to search for them themselves.For various reasons, I dislike their system, mainly because it is ridiculous to obtain images that only correspond to a thousand from the countless number of words.What good can they do, when from the infinite supply of words we are forced to remember one thing and then another?Furthermore, why would you want to deprive someone of their initiative by providing them with everything ready-made so that they don't have to construct anything themselves?Incidentally, people have different perceptions of the degree of similarity.For just as it often happens that we do not get everyone's support if we say that one appearance resembles another, simply because people perceive things differently, the same is true with images, so that the image we ourselves have chosen as apt appears bland to others.

三十九因此，每个人都应该获得适合自己的图像。最后，老师要教授正确的方法，以便学生在每一个案子中都能找到自己想要的东西，为了澄清起见，可以举出一个或另一个典型的例子，但不必列举所有相关的案例。例如，当我讨论介绍的设计时，我陈述的是一种设计方法，而不是列出一千种不同类型的介绍，我认为同样的方法也适用于图像。三十二

39Therefore, everyone should obtain the images that suit them.Finally, it is up to the teacher to teach the correct approach, so that in each individual case one can find what one is looking for, and for the purpose of clarification, to cite one or another typical example, but not to present all the relevant cases.For example, when I discuss the design of introductions, I am stating a method for design and not giving a list of a thousand different types of introduction, and the same approach applies, in my opinion, to images.32

现在，为了避免您认为记住单个单词太复杂或用处不大，并因此满足于记住事物本身，认为这样更有用、更适用，我必须向您解释为什么我绝不反对记住单词。我的观点是，那些想要不费力气、不费力气地掌握简单事物的人必须首先练习更困难的任务。我在这里讨论单词记忆的原因并不是为了让我们能够背诵诗句，而是为了通过这样的练习来提高具有实际用途的记忆能力，这样当我们从更严格的训练转向另一种记忆时就不会给我们带来任何努力。

Now, lest you believe that memorizing individual words is too complicated or of little use, and therefore settle for memorizing the things themselves in the belief that it is more useful and applicable, I must explain to you why I in no way disapprove of memorizing words.My opinion is that those who want to master simpler things without effort and trouble must first practice more difficult tasks.The reason I have discussed the memorization of words here is not that we should be able to recite verses by heart, but that through such exercises one should improve the kind of memorization of things that has a practical use, so that it does not cause any effort for us when we move from the more demanding training to the other type of memorization.

40然而，在每个学科中，没有持续实践的理论教学都不会有太大的效果，对于记忆术来说尤其如此，如果没有勤奋、投入、工作和准确性的确认，教学几乎毫无意义。您可以确保拥有尽可能多的位置，并且这些位置以最大程度的规律性进行设计；当谈到放置图像时，您应该每天练习。因为虽然其他方面的学习经常会受到各种任务的阻碍，但在这个特定问题上，我们不需要受到任何干扰。一天中，我们无时无刻不想记住一些东西，尤其是当我们忙于一些更重要的事情时。既然一个人拥有良好的记忆力，那么你就不能忽视，为了获得如此巨大的优势，一个人应该做好承受何种努力的准备；一旦您体验过它的好处，您就会充分意识到这一点。我的目的并不是进一步激发你对记忆艺术的兴趣；否则，看起来好像我对你的雄心壮志感到失望，或者好像我对此事所说的还不够多。

40In every discipline, however, theoretical teaching without continuous practice has little effect, but this is especially true of mnemonics, where teaching means almost nothing if it is not confirmed by diligence, commitment, work and accuracy.You can ensure that you have as many spaces as possible and that these are designed regularly to the greatest extent possible; when it comes to placing images, you should practice daily.For while various tasks often hinder us in other studies, in this particular matter we need not be disturbed by anything.There isn't a moment in the day that goes by without us wanting to commit something to memory, and this is especially true when we are busy with some more important matter.Since one benefits from a good memory, it cannot escape you, therefore, what efforts one should be prepared to endure in order to gain that which involves such considerable advantages; this you will fully realize, once you have experienced its benefits.It is not my intention to further encourage your interest in the art of memory; otherwise it could appear as if I were despairing of your ambition, or as if I had said less about the matter than it requires.

我现在来谈谈修辞的第五部分。我对你的建议是，反复回顾前面的所有部分，并且——这非常重要——通过练习巩固你的知识。

I will now turn to the fifth part of the rhetoric.My advice to you is that you repeatedly go through all the previous parts in your memory and – which is very important – consolidate your knowledge through practice.

1 老加图(参见 IV:7) 以在所有演讲的结尾而闻名，无论主题是什么，他都会对主题提出一个请求。

1 Cato the Elder(cf. IV:7) is known for having concluded all his speeches, regardless of topic, with a single plea for the former.

2 此时正值第二次布匿战争（公元前 218-202 年）的最后阶段。

2 The situation is the final stage of the Second Punic War (218-202 BC).

3 公元前216年坎尼战役后就出现了这种情况。

3 Such a situation had arisen after the Battle of Cannae, 216 BC.

4 担任执政官的法定最低年龄为 43 岁，但普布利乌斯·科尔内利乌斯·西庇阿·埃米利安努斯于公元前 147 年当选执政官时只有 37 岁。

4 The statutory minimum age for the consulship was 43, but Publius Cornelius Scipio Aemilianus was only 37 when he was elected consul in 147 BC.

7 These are the four “cardinal virtues” which could then be divided into more specific virtues and which became the basis of moral philosophical theory in the West from antiquity to the 19th century.

8 参见二：28-46。

9 暗指公元前 216 年第二次布匿战争期间卡西利努姆城的人们的推理方式。

10这句古老谚语的一个著名变体是幸运之神帮助强者，“幸运女神坚定地站在他们这一边”，出自特伦斯，福尔米奥，203.
