第四卷

第四卷书

BOOK IV

LIBER QUARTUS

公元 4:1-69

AD HERENNIUM IV:1-69

1由于在本书中，Herennius，我写了关于语言设计的内容，并且在这样做时——与处理这个主题的希腊作家的做法相反——在需要的语境中使用我自己的例子，我必须用几句话解释我的方法，这是出于必要而不是自由选择；从我在之前的书中避免写序言和离题内容这一事实可以清楚地看出这一点。在进行了一些必要的初步说明之后，现在我打算按照我的意图向你们解释修辞艺术的其余部分。但如果您首先注意希腊作家的立场，您将更容易理解我的方法。

1Since in the present book, Herennius, I write about linguistic design and in doing so – contrary to the practice of the Greek authors who have treated this subject – use my own examples in the contexts where such are needed, I must explain in a few words my approach, which is due to necessity and not free choice; this is clear enough from the fact that in previous books I have dispensed with both prefaces and digressions from the subject.After some necessary preliminary remarks, it is now my intention to explain to you, in accordance with my intentions, the remaining parts of the rhetorical art.But it will be easier for you to understand my method if you first take note of the positions of the Greek authors.

出于多种原因，他们认为他们必须在指导中总结出如何以正确的方式美化语言设计，并在每种情况下都引用一些著名演说家或诗人的例子。他们认为，这首先是出于谦虚，因为不满足于提供理论指导，还热衷于自己树立榜样，会被视为一种吹嘘；这将是自我展示，而不是修辞艺术。

For several reasons they believe that they must conclude their instructions on the proper way to beautify linguistic design with examples in each case from some well-known speaker or poet.Primarily, they say, this is dictated by modesty, since it can be perceived as a kind of boasting not to be content with providing theoretical instruction but also to seem keen to produce exemplary examples yourself; it would be to put oneself forward instead of the art of rhetoric.

2因此，这首先是一种谦虚的感觉，这意味着一个人不想给人留下只接受和喜欢自己的印象。我们可以以恩尼乌斯为例吗？1或格拉古2，而放弃它们并引用自己的观点则显得有些冒昧。其次，他们说，例子可以作为证明。与证词类似，例子证实了教学所关注的内容，但仅奠定了初步的基础。那么，在争论中或在法庭上，这个人难道不会显得很可笑吗？3用他自己的亲身证词来捍卫他的事业？举个例子就像证词一样，是为了证明某件事。因此，例子必须取自尽可能最好的来源，这样用来证明某事的证据就不需要反过来证明。必然的情况是，一个人要么喜欢自己，最喜欢自己发明的东西，要么喜欢别人写的东西，然后转向最好的资料来源。如果你认为自己比所有人都优秀，那么老年人享有的声誉又如何呢？他们身上散发出的权威性难道不不仅为论据增添了分量，而且还激发了人们试图模仿他们的兴趣吗？当然，如果有人给予人们通过模仿获得与格拉古或克拉苏一样的技能的希望，那么它就会唤醒所有人的雄心壮志并激发他们的热情。4。

2It would therefore be above all a feeling of modesty, which means that one does not want to give the impression of accepting and liking only oneself.Can we take examples from Ennius?1or Gracchus2, it simply seems presumptuous to dispense with them and instead cite one's own.Second, they say, examples act as testimonials.Not unlike a testimony, the example confirms what teaching draws attention to but only lays an initial foundation for.Would not that man then seem ridiculous, as in a dispute or before a court of law?3defends his cause with his own personal testimonies?An example, like a testimony, is given to prove something.Consequently, the example must be taken from the best possible source, so that what is cited to prove something does not in turn need to be proven.It is necessarily the case that one either prefers oneself to everyone else and likes best what one has invented, or one prefers what others have written and then turns to the best sources.If you think you are better than everyone else, what about the reputation that the old people enjoy?Isn't it true that the authority that emanates from them not only gives weight to the arguments but also stimulates people's interest in trying to imitate them?Well, of course it awakens ambitions in all men and fuels their zeal if one gives them the hope of acquiring through imitation the same skill as a Gracchus or a Crassus.4.

3最后，他们说，完美的知识在于能够从广泛散布和穿插在如此多的诗歌和演讲中的所有高度多样化的文本段落中进行如此仔细的选择，以至于人们可以在艺术的各个方面引用各种例子。如果仅靠勤奋就能做到这一点，那么人们无疑应该为不遗余力地做这件事而受到赞扬，但事实上，除非人们完全掌握了修辞艺术，否则这项任务是不可能的。因为有谁能够在不具备完美掌握的情况下，在浩瀚而分支繁多的文学作品中指出并选择艺术所需要的一切呢？当普通人读到好的演讲或诗歌时，他们会喜欢演讲者和诗人，却不明白他们为什么喜欢，因为他们不知道引起他们特别喜爱的东西在哪里，也不知道它是什么，也不知道如何产生。但是，如果一个人能够理解这一切，并且不仅能选择最恰当的例子，还能为所有那些特别值得在教科书中处理的事情制定各种规则，那么他一定是这个领域的杰出大师。这是最高水平的技能——还能在自己的艺术表现中使用借用的例子！

3Finally, they say, perfect knowledge lies in the ability to make such careful selections from among all the highly diverse passages of text that are widely scattered and interspersed in so many poems and speeches that one can cite examples of every kind on all points within the art.If this could be done by mere diligence, one would undoubtedly deserve praise for not having spared such trouble, but in fact the task is impossible unless one has a complete mastery of the art of rhetoric.For is there anyone who, without possessing perfect mastery, can indicate and select all that art requires in the extensive and widely branched literature?When ordinary people read good speeches or poems, they like the speakers and poets without understanding why they do so, because they cannot know where that which arouses their particular delight is found, nor what it is, nor how it has come about.But he who understands all this and can not only select the most apt examples but also formulate various rules for all those things which especially deserve to be treated in a textbook, he must necessarily be a superior master in this field.This is the highest level of skill – to also manage to use borrowed examples in one's own representation of art!

4当希腊人坚持这些立场时，他们更多的是通过自己的声誉而不是论据的真实性来令人信服。5因为我担心的是，有些人可能会认为与我的观点相反的观点是有道理的，仅仅因为它是由修辞学的创始人所持有的，并且这些人现在因其年龄而得到普遍认可。但如果你抛开他们的名声，而是逐一进行基于事实的比较，你就会意识到古老并不总是优先的。首先，我认为他们关于谦虚的言论可能是一个非常幼稚的论点。如果保持沉默或不写任何东西是谦虚的表现，那么他们为什么还要写作或说话呢？但是，如果他们至少以自己的名义写了一些东西，为什么他们的谦虚会阻止他们自己写所有的东西呢？这就好比一个参加奥运会跑步的人，站在起跑线上后，说那些开始比赛的人太无耻了，而他自己却留在起跑线后面，告诉别人拉达斯或博伊斯库斯6参加地峡运动会7。希腊作家也这么做。他们先是出现在修辞的赛道上，然后又说那些努力运用修辞所包含的内容的人行为无耻；相反，他们赞美一些古代的演说家、诗人或一些作品，但不敢投入到修辞的争论中。

4When the Greeks assert these positions, they convince more through their reputation than through the truth of the arguments.5For what I fear is that some may consider the opinion, which is opposite to mine, to be proven simply because it was held by those who were the originators of rhetoric and who are now generally recognized by reason of their age.But if you disregard their reputation and instead make a factually based comparison point by point, you will realize that antiquity does not always take precedence.Firstly, I think that their talk about modesty is perhaps a very childish argument.For if it is an expression of modesty to remain silent or to write nothing, then why do they write or speak at all?But if they write at least something in their own name, why does their modesty prevent them from writing everything themselves?It is as if someone who has come to the Olympic Games to run, after taking the starting position, were to say that those who have started the race are shameless, while he himself remained behind the starting line and told others how Ladas or Boiscus6ran in the Isthmian Games7The Greek writers do the same.First they appear on the racetrack of rhetoric, but then they say that those who strive to apply what is included in rhetoric act shamelessly; instead they praise some ancient speaker or poet or some writing, but without daring to throw themselves into the rhetorical race.

5我不太愿意这么说，但我担心，他们在追求对谦虚的赞扬时，却表现出了相反的行为。“你到底是什么意思？”有人可能会问。“你们编写自己的教科书，为我们制定新的规则——但你们无法亲自确认这些规则，只能借用别人的例子。问题在于，你是否在厚颜无耻地利用他人的成果来美化自己的名声。”确实，如果古代的每一位演说家和诗人都拿走这些作者的书籍，并清空其中的财产，那么这些作者就不会再想把任何东西视为自己的了。

5I hesitate to say it, but I'm afraid that in their pursuit of praise for modesty, they are demonstrating the opposite.“What do you really mean?” one might ask.“You write your own textbook, you formulate new rules for us – but you cannot confirm the rules yourself, but borrow examples from others.The question is whether you are not acting shamelessly by exploiting the work of others to glorify your own name.” And indeed it is so, that if each of the ancient orators and poets were to take the books of such authors and empty them of what is their property, then there would be nothing left that these authors would want to consider their own.

“但是，”有人现在反对道，“由于例子类似于证词，因此，像证词一样，它们也应该从最可靠的人那里获得。”首先，举出例子不是为了证实，也不是为了证明，而是为了说明。例如，当我们说有一个由相似词尾组成的格时，引用克拉苏的我们能够并且必须（“我们可以而且应该这样做”）8，我们不是作见证，而是举个例子。证词和例子的区别在于，通过例子，我们重点突出我们所谈论的是条件性的，而我们证实正如我们所说，有些事情正在发生。

“But,” someone now objects, “since examples are similar to testimonies, it is appropriate that they, like testimonies, be obtained from the most reliable men imaginable.” First of all, examples are given neither to confirm nor to testify, but to illustrate.For example, when we say that there is a figure consisting of similar word endings and in doing so quote Crassus'what we can and must(“which we both can and should”)8, we are not giving a testimony but giving an example.The difference between a testimony and an example is that with the example wehighlights howwhat we are talking about is conditioned, while with the testimony weconfirms thatSomething is happening as we say.

6此外，证词必须与主张一致，否则就无法支持主张。9但希腊作家的实践与他们的说法不符。为什么不呢？嗯，因为他们承诺编写一本教科书，但大多是从那些缺乏修辞知识的人那里取例子。那么我想问：如果一个人自己没有按照修辞规则写过任何东西，他怎么能证明他所写的修辞价值呢？看起来他们的行为违背了他们的承诺。因为当他们承担编写有关该主题的教科书的任务时，人们认为他们是在说他们自己已经想到了他们打算教给别人的东西，但是当他们写作时，他们实际上是在向我们展示别人已经想到的东西。

6Furthermore, the testimony must be consistent with a claim, otherwise it cannot support the claim.9But the practice of the Greek authors does not match what they claim.And why not?Well, because they promise to write a textbook but mostly take examples from those who lack knowledge of rhetoric.Then I ask: how can someone prove the value of what he has written about rhetoric without himself writing anything in accordance with the rhetorical rules?It seems like they are acting contrary to their promises.For when they undertake the task of writing a textbook on the subject, one thinks that they are saying that they themselves have thought up what they intend to teach others, but when they write they are instead showing us what others have thought up.

“但是，”有人又说，“困难恰恰在于在众多选择中进行选择。”你说的困难是什么意思？它需要工作还是需要技术技能？仅仅因为某件事需要努力并不能保证结果会很辉煌。有许多劳动密集型任务的完成并不一定需要你吹嘘，除非你认为即使亲手抄写整部戏剧或演讲稿也已经是做了一件光荣的事情。但如果你真的认为这样的任务对技术技能有很高的要求，那么如果你能在微不足道的事情中找到与重要的事情相同的乐趣，你就有可能显得不习惯更困难的任务。因为对于一个完全没有受过教育的人来说，按照你所说的方式进行选择当然是不可能的，但许多人即使不掌握技术也能做到这一点。

“But,” someone says again, “it is precisely in choosing between many alternatives that the difficulty lies.”What do you mean by difficult?That it requires work or that it requires technical skill?Just because something requires work doesn't guarantee that the result will be brilliant.There are many labor-intensive tasks whose completion you do not necessarily need to boast about, unless you would think that even by copying out entire plays or speeches with your own hand you have done something honorable.But if you really think that such a task places high demands on technical skill, you run the risk of appearing unaccustomed to more difficult tasks if you can find the same joy in insignificant things as in important ones.For to choose in the way you speak of is certainly impossible for someone who is completely uneducated, but many can do it without possessing technical mastery.

7任何对修辞学，特别是语言设计稍有了解的人，都能认识到一切按照艺术规则设计的东西，但只有受过全面教育的人才能自己运用它们。例如，如果你想要从恩尼乌斯的悲剧中挑选出句子，或者从帕库维乌斯的信使报告中挑选出10然后就认为自己博学多识，只是因为你做了一些完全没有受过教育的人不会做的事情，那么你就太天真了，因为任何受过中等教育的人都很容易做同样的事情。同样，如果你从演讲或诗歌中选择一些明显具有修辞艺术特征的例子，并认为你做了一些非常巧妙的事情，只是因为没有受过教育的人做不到，那你就错了。因为通过这一点，我们看到您知道一些事情，但我们需要其他迹象才能明白您知道很多事情。但如果辨别用艺术写的东西是一门艺术，那么按照艺术的规则来写自己就更是艺术了。因为，文笔优美的人很容易就能看出别人写得好，而能轻松引用的人却不一定需要自己这样做。11写得好。尽管这是一门伟大的艺术，但他们应该在其他场合使用它，而不是在他们自己发明、设计和表演某些东西时使用它。简而言之，他们应该运用自己的修辞知识，让自己成为榜样，而不是成为善于在别人身上寻找榜样的人。

7Anyone who has heard a little about rhetoric, and especially about linguistic design, can recognize everything that is designed in accordance with the rules of the art, but only the one who is thoroughly educated can apply them himself.For example, if youwants to pick out sentences from Ennius' tragedies or messenger reports from Pacuvius'10and then consider yourself extremely well-read, just because you do something that the completely uneducated wouldn't do, then you are naive, because anyone with moderate education easily does the same thing.Likewise, you are mistaken if you choose examples from speeches or poems that show clear signs of rhetorical art and think that you have done something very artful, just because no uneducated person can do it.For through this we see that you know some things, but we need other signs before we understand that you know a lot.But if it is an art to discern what is written with art, then it is even more artful to write yourself according to the rules of art.For he who writes artfully easily recognizes the well-written in others, but he who can quote with ease does not necessarily need to do so himself.11write well.And even though it is a great art, they should use it on other occasions and not when they are expected to invent, design and perform something themselves.In short, they should use their rhetorical knowledge rather to be seen as role models themselves than as those who are skilled in finding role models in others.

那些认为应该使用借用例子的人已经受到了足够的反驳。现在让我们来研究一下人们对此事还有什么进一步的看法。我的意思是，借用别人的例子会犯错误，而借用许多人的例子则会犯更大的错误。我们先来研究一下后一点。如果我现在接受借用例子的原则，我会强调必须借用单一作者的例子。首先，我的对手无法提出任何反对意见，因为这种方法可以让他们选择和赞扬任何人，无论是诗人还是演说家，只要他们能为他们提供各种需要的例子，他们就可以信赖他们的声誉。其次，对于该学科的学生来说，重要的是他是否相信每个人都可以学会一切，或者没有人可以学会一切，或者不同的说话者会获得不同事物的技能。因为如果他相信一个人可以掌握一切，他自己也会努力掌握一切。但如果他对那件事感到绝望，他就会练习有限数量的技能。他自然会对此感到满意，因为修辞学老师本身并不能够展示一个人的所有技能。当引用加图、格拉古家族、莱利乌斯、西庇阿、加尔巴、波西纳、克拉苏、安东尼乌斯的例子时12以及其他人的作品，当同时引用诗人和历史学家的作品时，学者将不可避免地相信，所有例子只能从他们所有人的作品中综合得出，而单个作者甚至无法提供哪怕是几个例子。

Those who believe that borrowed examples should be used have thus been sufficiently contradicted.Let us now examine what further views one may have on the matter.I mean then that they make mistakes who borrow examples, and they sin even more by taking examples from many.Let's examine the latter point first.If I now accepted the principle of borrowing examples, I would emphasize that one must then borrow from a single author.First, my opponents would be unable to raise any objection, since this method would enable them to select and praise anyone, poet or orator, who provided them with examples for every need, someone on whose reputation they could rely.Secondly, it is of importance to the student of the subject whether he believes that everyone can learn everything, or that no one can learn everything, or that different speakers acquire skill in different things.Because if he believes that a single individual can master everything, he will also strive for mastery in everything himself.But if he despairs about that matter, he will practice a limited number of skills.And he will naturally be content with them, since the rhetoric teacher himself is not able to demonstrate all the skills of a single individual.When examples are thus cited from Cato, the Gracchi, Laelius, Scipio, Galba, Porcina, Crassus, Antonius12and others, and when both poets and historians are cited, then the student will inevitably believe that the sum of the examples could only have been taken from all of them taken together and that an individual author could hardly have supplied even a few.

8因此，他将满足于模仿一位作者，并对掌握所有作者共同展示的一切感到绝望。是毛泽东。不相信一个人能够掌握一切，这对学生来说是不利的，我现在的意思是，如果他们只从一个人那里获取例子，没有人会开始这样想。但是教科书作者自己认为任何人都不可能掌握语言设计的所有部分，因此，他们既没有给出自己的例子，也没有给出一两个作者的例子，而是从所有演讲者和诗人那里获取的例子，这一点很重要。如果有人想表明艺术并不能提高语言能力，那么他可以有理由地使用这样的论点：没有人能够独自成功掌握修辞的所有部分。那么，如果该主题的教科书作者本人也同意这一点，并支持那些不愿意承认艺术价值的人，那不是很荒谬吗？

8He will therefore be content to imitate a single author and despair of being able to master all that all of them together have demonstrated.It is Mao.It is to the student's disadvantage not to believe that a single individual can master everything, and I now mean that no one would start thinking that way if they took their examples from just one.But the textbook authors themselves have considered it impossible for anyone to master all parts of linguistic design, and it is therefore significant that they have neither given their own examples nor those from one or two authors, but have taken them from all speakers and poets.If someone wanted to show that art does not improve the ability to speak, then he could with some justification use this argument that no one alone has succeeded in mastering all the parts of rhetoric.Isn't it ridiculous then if a textbook author on the subject himself agrees with this and supports those who do not want to recognize the value of art?

这样，我已经表明，如果人们选择总是借用例子的方法，那么人们就应该只从一个例子中选取。

I have thus shown that one should have taken examples from only one, if one had chosen the method of always borrowing examples.

9从下文中我们就会明白，一个人根本就不应该借钱。首先，教科书作者给出的例子应该体现他本人所拥有的技能。我们可以想象一个商人提供紫色布料或其他东西，并说：“从我这里购买，但我将从其他人那里获取样品给你看。”他们就是这么做的，卖出产品却在别处寻找样品；他们声称拥有大量小麦，但却无法拿出一把作为样品。关于 Triptolemus十三当他把粮食赐给人类时，他自己从其他人那里借来的，或者如果普罗米修斯14当他想在凡人中传播火种时，他自己却带着陶罐到处向邻居乞讨煤炭，这看起来一定很滑稽。这些向全人类传授演讲艺术的老师们，难道没有意识到，当他们向别人借钱来兑现自己的诺言时，他们是在自取其辱吗？如果有人声称发现了水流丰沛但隐藏得很好的泉眼，并且在他最渴的时候说出这句话，而他却没有任何可以解渴的东西，他岂不被嘲笑吗？既然这些教科书的作者不仅声称自己拥有这些泉源，而且他们自己就是泉源，既然他们现在肩负着为所有干渴的人才提供水源的任务，那么，他们难道没有意识到，如果在这样的承诺中，他们自己却因缺水而枯萎，那他们就会出丑吗？查尔斯没有学到15以这样的方式制作雕像，以至于他的老师吕西波斯展示了米隆的头部、普拉克西特莱斯的手臂和波利克里托斯的躯干，而他却无法亲眼看到老师亲自做这一切；如果他愿意的话，他可以主动研究别人的作品。我们的教科书作者相信，采用不同的方法可以更好地教授学习该科目的学生。

9From what follows we will understand that one should not have borrowed at all.First and foremost, the example a textbook author gives should demonstrate the skill he himself possesses.One can imagine a merchant offering purple cloth or something else with the words: “Buy from me, but I will get samples from someone else to show you.” Just so do those who sell a commodity but look for samples elsewhere; they claim to have heaps of wheat without being able to produce a handful as a sample.About Triptolemus13, when he bestowed grain on mankind, borrowed it himself from other people, or if Prometheus14, when he wanted to spread fire among mortals, he himself went around with a clay pot and begged coal from his neighbors, they would have appeared comical.Don't these teachers, who teach all of humanity the art of speech, see that they make themselves ridiculous when they borrow from others to fulfill their promises?If someone claims to have discovered richly flowing but well-hidden springs and says this at the very moment when he is thirsty the most, yet without having anything to quench his thirst with, would he not be ridiculed?Since such textbook authors not only claim to own these springs but also to be the springs themselves, and since they now have the task of giving water to all thirsty talents, do they not realize that they will make a fool of themselves if, in the midst of such promises, they themselves wither for lack of water?Chares did not learn15to make statues in such a way that his teacher Lysippos showed a head by Myron, arms by Praxiteles and a torso by Polykleitos, but he could see with his own eyes the master himself doing all this; he could, if he so wished, study the works of others on his own initiative.Our textbook authors believe that those studying the subject can be taught better with a different method.

10此外，借用他人的例子不可能特别适合教科书，因为作为一个练习演讲者，人们会避免展示修辞技巧，因此通常对理论细节很轻视，而另一方面，作为一名教师，人们必须提供符合规则的恰当的例子；当您以演讲者的身份出现时，您会使用技巧来隐藏艺术，以便它不会显露出来并被所有人看到。因此，最好也使用您自己的例子来促进对艺术的理解。

10Furthermore, examples borrowed from others cannot possibly be particularly suitable for a handbook, since as a practicing speaker one avoids showing rhetorical technique and therefore generally takes theoretical details very lightly, while on the other hand as a teacher one must give apt examples that must correspond to the rules; when one then appears as a speaker, one hides the art with one's technique, so that it does not emerge and become visible to everyone.Consequently, it is better to use your own examples as well to facilitate understanding of the art.

最后，我想说的是，我发现这种方法是最好的，同时考虑到我保留了希腊语技术术语的翻译。这些对于我们的语言来说是陌生的，对于我们自己的传统中缺失的概念，不可能找到常用的语言表达。因此，这些条款最初看起来会让人感到不舒服，这是不可避免的，但这应该归咎于这件事，而不是我的。我的演讲的剩余部分将通过例子来说明。但如果我选择从别人那里抄袭，那么这本书的优点就会全部归于别人，而那些尴尬和陌生之处则会被认为是我的特殊贡献。因此我也避免了这种不便。

Finally, I would like to say that I have found this method to be the best, also considering that I leave the Greek technical terms in translation.These are foreign to our language, and for concepts that were missing from our own tradition, it would have been impossible to find commonly used linguistic expressions.It is therefore inevitable that the terms will initially seem quite uncomfortable, but this is to be blamed on the matter and not on me.The remainder of my presentation will be taken up by examples.But had I then chosen to take them from others, it would have led to all the merits in the book being attributed to others, while the awkwardness and strangeness would be considered my special contribution.I have consequently avoided that inconvenience as well.

尽管我赞扬希腊人是修辞学的创始人，但出于上述原因，我并没有将他们的方法应用于实例。现在是时候讨论语言设计规则了。我的目的是将这些规则分为两部分。首先，我将讨论修辞风格的类型，然后我打算阐明这种风格应始终具有哪些特征。

Although I praise the Greeks as the originators of rhetoric, for the reasons given above I have not applied their approach to examples.It is now time to move on to the rules for linguistic design.My intention is then to divide these rules into two sections.First I will talk about the types of rhetorical style that fall into, then I intend to clarify what characteristics should always characterize such style.

11因此，有三种这样的类型，称为风格层次[数字]；它们内部运转着每一个正确形成的言语。第一个叫做升高[figura gravis]，另一个中间风格[figura mediocris] 第三个简单的[扩展图]。16高雅文体的特点是文字高雅、优美，行文流畅。中等风格由较低尊严的词语组成，但不是最低级或最日常的词语。简单风格的特点是简化为最日常的自然语言形式。

11Thus, there are three such types, which are calledstyle levels[figurae]; within them every correctly formed speech moves.The first one is calledelevated[figura gravis], the othermiddle style[figura mediocris] and the thirdsimple[extended figure].16The elevated style is characterized by elevated and beautiful words in a smoothly flowing stream.The middle style consists of words of a lower, but not the lowest or most everyday, dignity.The simple style is characterized by its reduction to the most everyday form of natural speech.

（1）如果演讲者的每一个观点都用所能找到的字面或比喻意义上的最优美的词语来表达，如果演讲者选用那种在修饰和呼吁怜悯时出现的崇高句子，如果演讲者使用具有崇高尊严的思想比喻或词语（我稍后会回到这一点），那么，这篇演讲就是以崇高的风格形成的。17。以下可以作为这种风格的例子：

(1) A speech is formulated in the sublime style if every single point is clothed in the most beautiful words in the literal or figurative sense that can be mustered, if one selects sublime sentences of the kind that occur in embroideries and appeals for pity, and if one uses such figures of thought or words that possess sublime dignity, to which I will return later.17The following can serve as examples of this style:

12“法官先生们，你们当中有谁能为这样一个计划将祖国出卖给敌人的人制定出足够严厉的惩罚吗？有什么恶行能与此罪行相比，有什么惩罚能对付这种恶行呢？对于那些冒犯自由人、玷污母亲、伤害他人，甚至杀害他人的人，我们的祖先采取了最严厉的惩罚；对于这种最严重、最不虔诚的罪行，他们没有规定明确的惩罚。在其他犯罪中，只有个人或少数人受到他人犯罪的影响，但参与这种犯罪的人准备通过单一计划对所有公民施加最可怕的打击。噢，野蛮的性格！噢，多么残忍的意图！噢，男人被剥夺了一切人类情感！他们敢做什么或者他们现在可以制定什么计划？是的，敌人将如何打开祖先的坟墓，推倒城墙，兴高采烈地冲进城市，他们将如何摧毁神庙，屠杀最重要的人，将其他人拖入奴役，将母亲和自由人抛弃给敌人的欲望，城市将如何被无情地烧毁后倒塌！这些不信神的人不相信他们已经实现了他们的计划，直到他们看到我们神圣的家园变成可怜的灰烬。法庭上的先生们，我无法用言语来形容他们行为的残暴程度，然而，当我想到我没有必要告诉你们这些时，我就不那么担心了。因为您的爱国精神毫不犹豫地告诉您，对于一个想要牺牲所有人幸福的人，您应该将他驱逐出他想要埋葬在最普通的敌人所实施的无神暴政下的国家。”

12“For is there anyone among you, gentlemen of the judges, who can devise a punishment severe enough for such a man, who harbored plans to betray his fatherland to the enemy?What evil deed can be compared to this crime, what punishment can be severe enough for this evil deed?Our ancestors used the most severe punishments against those who had offended a freeborn, defiled a mother, wounded, or, worst of all, killed someone; for this most grievous and most impious crime they did not prescribe any definite punishment.In other crimes, only individuals or a few are affected by the crime of another, but those who are involved in this crime prepare to inflict the most terrible blows on all citizens in a single plan.Oh, barbaric disposition!Oh, cruel intentions!Oh, men stripped of every human feeling!What have they dared to do or what plans can they now forge?Yes, how the enemies will open the tombs of their ancestors, tear down the city walls and rush into the city with joy, how they will destroy the temples of the gods, slaughter the most important, drag others into slavery, abandon mothers and freedmen to the desires of the enemy, and how the city will collapse after being set on fire without any mercy!These godless men do not consider themselves to have accomplished their plans until they have seen our sacred homeland transformed into a pitiful heap of ashes.I lack words, gentlemen of the court, to describe the outrageousness of their actions, which, however, worries me less when I consider that I have not had to tell you this.For your patriotic disposition tells you without further ado that the man who wanted to sacrifice everyone's happiness, you should expel him from the state, which he wanted to bury in a godless tyranny exercised by the most common enemies."

十三（2）演讲以中间风格进行，如果，正如我之前所说，我们18稍微降低水平，但不会降至最低水平，如下所示：

13(2) The speech moves in the middle style, if, as I said earlier, we18lowers the level slightly, but without going down to the lowest level, as follows:

“法官先生们，你们知道我们在与谁作战：我们的盟友已经习惯于为我们而战，并与我们一起勇敢而坚定地保卫我们的帝国。他们必然对自己、自己的资源和自己的士兵有着充分的了解，此外，他们与我们距离很近，并与我们一起参与所有事务，这使得他们能够对罗马人民的所有不同权力资源做出同样正确的评估。当他们决定对我们发动战争时，我想问，是什么给了他们对战争事业的信心？当他们意识到他们的绝大多数盟友都没有背叛对我们的责任？当他们注意到他们没有足够的士兵，没有有能力的将军，没有公共财政资源，简而言之，没有进行战争所需的一切？即使是与邻国发生边界争端，或者他们认为整个冲突可以在一场战斗中决定，他们无论如何都会在各方面做好更充分的准备和武装——如果他们只是用他们微不足道的力量来剥夺我们对世界的统治权，那就更加奇怪了，所有的国家、国王和人民都屈服于我们的统治之下，有些是被迫屈服的，有些是自愿屈服的，因为他们被罗马人民用武力或慷慨击败了。有人可能会问：“但这不正是弗雷格拉的居民19主动尝试做什么？’当然，但是当他们看到弗雷格拉的情况后，他们有更充分的理由放弃他们的计划。对于没有经验的人来说，那些缺乏在每一个具体情况下寻求历史相似之处的能力的人，很容易因为无知而犯下错误，而那些知道别人遭遇过什么的人，很容易根据别人的遭遇来计划自己的行动。那么，他们夺取武器是否毫无动机、毫无希望呢？谁能想到，如果没有军队可以依靠，有人会愚蠢到敢于挑战罗马人民的至高无上的地位？因此他们肯定有某种动机，除了我所说的以外，还会有什么呢？”

“Gentlemen judges, you see who we are fighting against: it is against allies, who have been accustomed to fighting for us and together with us protecting our empire with bravery and commitment.It is inevitable that they have a good knowledge of themselves, their own resources and their own men, but in addition, their proximity to us and participation with us in all matters has made it possible for them to make equally correct assessments of all the different resources of power of the Roman people.When they had decided to wage war against us, what was it, I ask, that gave them confidence in their warlike enterprise, when they realized that the vast majority of their allies did not betray their duties towards us, and when they noticed that they had no access to soldiers in sufficient numbers, no capable generals, no public financial resources, in short, nothing of what is needed to carry out a war?Even if it were a border dispute with their neighbors, or if they believed that the entire conflict could be decided in a single battle, they would in any case come better prepared and armed in every respect - how much more strange it is then, if it is only with their insignificant forces that they try to deprive us of the world domination to which all nations, kings and peoples have bowed, some forced by force, others voluntarily, after they were defeated by the Roman people either by force of arms or by generosity.Someone may ask the question: 'But wasn't that precisely what the inhabitants of Fregellae19tried to do on their own initiative?' Certainly, but with so much better reason they should then abandon their plans, as they saw how things went for Fregellae.For people without experience, those who lack the ability to seek parallels from history in each individual situation, can very easily fall into error due to their ignorance, while those who know what others have suffered can easily plan their actions based on the fates that have befallen others.Have they then seized weapons without motive and without harboring any hopes?Who imagines that anyone could be so foolish as to dare to challenge the supremacy of the Roman people, if he has no troops to rely on?They must therefore have had some motive, and what could it be other than what I say?”

14（3）至于简单文体，甚至至于最低级的日常用语，可以如下例示：

14(3) For the simple style, which descends even to the lowest everyday language, the following may serve as an example:

“当时他正好在澡堂，洗完澡后就开始揉搓自己。他刚要进入水池，你瞧，那道身影突然出现了。“听着，孩子，”他说，“你的奴隶刚刚给了我一个小费。现在你必须付钱。’由于他还年轻，不习惯被陌生人称呼，所以他脸红了。随后那道身影以更大的声音重复了同样的话，并且还说了些别的话。男孩艰难地说道：“但是你可以让我考虑一下。”然后，那名男子开始大声喊叫，其声音很容易让任何人感到尴尬。这听起来如此厚颜无耻和残忍。我甚至不认为这是在夏至。20他训练自己的声音，主要是在后台和诸如此类的地方。男孩完全糊涂了，这没什么奇怪的。他的耳朵里除了老师的抱怨声什么也没有，而且他从来没有经历过这样的吼叫。“他在哪里能遇到这样一个完全无耻的恶作剧者，他认为自己不会失去任何名誉，但却可以允许自己做任何事而不会损害他的名誉？”

“He happened to be in the bathhouse at that time, and after he had washed himself, he began to rub himself.He was just about to go into the pool, when that figure suddenly appeared, you see.'Listen, boy,' he said, 'your slaves just gave me a tip.Now you have to pay.' Young as he is and not used to being addressed by a stranger, he blushed.Then that figure repeated the same thing in a louder voice and also said something else.With a little difficulty, the boy managed to get out a 'but you can let me think about it.' The man then started shouting in a voice that could easily make anyone blush with embarrassment.It sounds so brazen and brutal.I don't even think it's at the Solstice.20He has trained his voice, mostly backstage and in those kinds of places.The boy was completely confused, and there was nothing strange about that.He still has nothing else ringing in his ears but his teacher's whining, and he's never experienced a yelling like this."For where could he have met such a completely shameless prankster, who didn't think he had any reputation to lose but could allow himself anything without worsening his reputation?"

15通过上面的例子，我们能够理解不同层次的风格：这里展示了简单的风格，然后是高级风格，最后是中级风格。然而，在追求这些风格层次时，必须确保不会陷入任何密切相关的错误风格。（1）高尚的风格是值得称赞的，但在其附近有一种应该避免的风格；如果我们称之为充气[figura sufflata]，这似乎是一个恰当的术语。正如肿胀常常与健康的身体相似一样，当用新的或古老的词语、不自然的比喻或比主题所需更高级的短语表达某件事时，缺乏经验的人常常会将肿胀和膨胀的言语视为高级的言语，例如：

15The examples above themselves thus make it possible to understand the different levels of style: here the simple style was illustrated, the elevated style, and finally the intermediate style.However, when striving for these levels of style, one must ensure that one does not end up in any closely related incorrect style.(1) The exalted style, which is praiseworthy, has in its vicinity a style which should be avoided; if we call itinflated[figura sufflata], it seems to be an apt term.For just as swelling often bears resemblance to the healthy body, inexperienced people can often perceive swollen and inflated speech as elevated, when something is expressed with either new or archaic words, with strained metaphors, or with phrases that are more elevated than the subject requires, e.g.:

“因为背叛祖国的人，即使被投入海王星的深渊，也无法完全赎罪。“因此，对这个人进行严厉的惩罚吧，他竖起了战争之山，却摧毁了和平的平原。”大多数陷入这种风格并偏离最初风格的人，都被其表面上的崇高性所欺骗，无法看穿其浮夸的表现方式。

“For he who betrays his fatherland through high treason will not have fully atoned for his crime, even if he is cast down into the depths of the Neptunian abysses."So exact punishment from this man who has towered up the mountains of war but wiped out the plains of peace." The majority of those who fall into this style and stray from the one they started with are deceived by its apparently exalted character and are unable to see through the bloated manner of presentation.

16（2）如果那些决定使用中间风格的人未能完成它，他们就会误入附近的一种风格，这种风格被称为风格无转向[genus fluctuans]，因为它随波逐流，缺乏达到决心和男性力量表达的能力。例如：

16(2) If those who decide to use the middle style fail to complete it, they stray into a style that is nearby and is called a stylewithout steering[genus fluctuans], because it drifts here and there and lacks the ability to reach an expression of determination and masculine power.An example is the following:

“当我们的盟友想要与我们作战时，如果他们真的是主动行动，并且没有来自这里的许多恶毒而无耻的人的帮助，他们无疑会一次又一次地计算他们的选择是什么。“任何想要成就大事的人通常都会考虑太久。”如果你这样说话，你就无法吸引听众的注意力。风格完全混乱，无法抓住任何东西并赋予其完美的圆形。

“When our allies wanted to fight against us, they would undoubtedly have tried time and again to calculate what their options were, if they were really acting on their own initiative and did not have a lot of helpers from here, malicious and impudent men."For all who want to accomplish great deeds tend to think too long." If you speak that way, you cannot maintain the listener's attention.The style is completely disorganized and unable to grasp anything and give it a perfectly rounded shape.

（3）那些不能以真正优雅的方式表达自己的人，当他们选择简单的风格时，最终会以一种干巴巴、毫无生气的方式表达自己，这种表达方式可以恰当地称为贫穷的[流放属]。一个例子：

(3) Those who are unable to express themselves with real elegance, when they have chosen the simple style, end up in a dry and bloodless manner of presentation, which can appropriately be calledpoor[genus exile].An example:

“他走向澡堂里的男孩。然后他说，“你的奴隶打了我。”然后男孩对他说：“我会考虑的。”然后那个男人带着脏话过来了，他喊叫的声音越来越大，当时在场的人很多。”这里的语言完全是软弱而简单的，没有达到朴素风格的目的，即用自然、精心挑选的词语来表达。

“He walked up to the boy in the bathhouse.Then he says: ‘Your slave here has struck me.’ Then the boy says to him: ‘I will think about the matter.’ Then the man came with abusive words, and he shouted louder and louder, while many were there.” The language here is completely weak and simple, because it does not achieve the purpose of the simple style, namely a way of presentation based on natural and well-chosen words.

每一个层次的风格，无论是高级风格还是中级风格和简单风格，都可以用修辞手法来修饰，我将在后面讨论。21如果谨慎使用，它们会增强风格，就像颜色一样，但如果它们频繁出现，它们会扭曲风格的特征。但在讲话过程中，要变换语调的层次，以中庸语调代替高雅语调，以朴素语调代替中庸语调，如此反复交替。这种变化很容易避免过度饱和。

Each level of style, the elevated style as well as the middle style and the simple style, can be embellished with rhetorical figures, which I will discuss later.21If used sparingly, they enhance the style, as do colors, but if they appear frequently, they distort the character of the style.However, during the speech, the level of style should be changed, so that the elevated style is replaced by the middle style and the middle style by the simple style, after which they can alternate with each other over and over again.This kind of variation makes it easy to avoid oversaturation.

17在说明了语言设计中必须具备的风格层次之后，我们现在将研究正确和完美的语言设计中必须具备的风格特质。最能满足说话者目的的语言形式应该具有以下三个特点：明晰[优雅的]，巧妙的句子结构[组成] 和表现力[庄重/华丽]。

17After this account of the stylistic levels that one has to operate within in linguistic design, we will now examine the stylistic qualities that must be present in a correct and perfect linguistic design.The form of language that best serves the speaker's purposes should be characterized by three characteristics:clarity[elegant],artful sentence construction[conposition] andexpressiveness[dignified/ornate].

（1）清晰度是指一切内容看起来都清楚、明确。它分为正确的拉丁语[拉丁裔] 和明晰[解释]。

(1) Clarity is what makes everything seem to be said clearly and distinctly.It is divided intocorrect Latin[Latinitas] andclarity[explanation].

(a) 正确的拉丁语可以保证语言的纯洁性，不受任何错误的影响。有两种类型的错误可能会污染拉丁语，即谬误[独唱] 和野蛮[野蛮行为]语法错误是指一组单词中包含的某个单词与前面的单词组合不正确。当词语选择不正确时，就会出现野蛮行为。我将在我的语法教科书中解释如何避免这些错误。22

(a) Correct Latin safeguards a pure language, free from every error.There are two types of errors that can taint Latin, namelysolecism[soloecism] andbarbarism[barbarism].Solecism means that a group of several words contains a word that is combined with a previous one in an incorrect way.Barbarism exists when the choice of words is incorrect.I will explain how to avoid these errors in my grammar textbook.22

(b) 清晰度旨在使演示易于理解和清晰。它通过常用词和特殊表达两种方式实现。常用词是日常用语中出现的词，而特殊表达是或可能是仅与当前讨论的主题相关而出现的词。

(b) Clarity aims to make the presentation easy to understand and clear.It is realized by two means, commonly used words and special expressions.Commonly used words are those that occur in everyday speech, while special expressions are or may be words that only occur in connection with the topic currently being discussed.

18（2）艺术性的句式是指词语的排列方式，使文章具有统一的风格特征。如果我们避免频繁出现使风格变得丑陋和空洞的声音冲突，那么这个目的就达到了。例如独立的枯草芽孢杆菌（“空中悬挂着最诱人的果实”），同样，如果我们避免一遍又一遍地重复同一个字母。下面的诗句可以说明这个错误——当谈到这里的错误时，我可以随意借用别人的例子：

18(2) An artistic sentence structure means that the words are arranged in such a way that the text acquires a uniform stylistic character.This purpose is served if we avoid frequently recurring vocal encounters that make the style ugly and gaping, e.g.Bacae aereae amoenissimae inpendebant(“in the air hung the most inviting fruits”), likewise if we avoid repeating the same letter over and over again.That error can be illustrated by the following verse – for when it comes to errors here, I feel free to borrow examples from others:

O Tite、tute、Tati、tibi tanta、暴君、tulisti23

O Tite, tute, Tati, tibi tanta, tyrant, tulisti23

（“哦，提图斯·塔提乌斯，暴君，这一切都是你自作自受的”）

(“O Titus Tatius, tyrant, you have brought all this upon yourself”)

同一位诗人还说：

And from the same poet:

quoiquam quicquam quemquam, quemque quisque 方便, 否定24

quoiquam quicquam quemquam, quemque quisque conveniat, neg24

（“否认某人犯有某罪，无论谁指控谁”）

(“denies that anyone [is guilty?] of anything, regardless of who accuses whom”)

此外，我们应该避免不必要地重复相同的词语，例如：

Furthermore, we should avoid unnecessary repetition of the same words, such as:

Nam cuius Rationis Ratio non extet, ei

Nam cuius rationis ratio non extet, ei

理性比率非 est fidem habere admodum二十五

rationi ratio non est fidem habere admodum25

（“一个没有任何理由支持的理由，

(“A reason that is not supported by any reason,

因此没有理由去相信）

that reason there is no reason to trust”)

我们也不应该使用具有相同结尾的长行单词：

We should also not use long lines of words with the same ending:

Flentes、plorantes、lacrimantes、obtestantes

Flentes, plorantes, lacrimantes, obtestantes

（“哭泣，哀叹，流泪，哀叹”）

(“Crying, lamenting, shedding tears, lamenting”)

此外，我们应该避免随意移动单词，除非可以以艺术的方式完成，我稍后会讨论这一点。二十六科利厄斯二十七经常犯这个错误，例如在以下段落中：之前的书本中有 res ad te scriptas、Luci、misimus、Aeli（“在上一本书中，我把这些事件的叙述献给了你，卢修斯，埃利乌斯”）。还应避免使用冗长的短语，因为这会刺激听众的听觉和说话者的呼吸。这些是你在构造句子时应该避免的错误。我剩下的工作现在将致力于表现力。

Furthermore, we should avoid moving words around unless it can be done in an artistic way, something I will discuss later.26Coelius27constantly makes this mistake, e.g.in the following passage:In priore libro has res ad te scriptas, Luci, misimus, Aeli(“In the previous book I dedicated to you, Lucius, the account of these events, Aelius”).One should also refrain from long drawn-out phrases, which irritate both the listener's hearing and the speaker's breathing.These are the errors you should avoid when it comes to sentence construction.My remaining work will now be devoted to expressiveness.

（3）通过多种方式的装饰，获得风格上的表现力。这里分为修辞手法[exornationes verborum] 和修辞手法[免除刑罚]。通过修辞手法，语言本身被赋予了引人注目的修饰，而修辞的意思是，不是词语，而是思想本身的内容被赋予了某种修饰的形式。

(3) Expressiveness in the style is gained by decorating it in a variety of ways.Here, a division is made intofigures of speech[exornationes verborum] andfigures of speech[exornationes sententiarum].Through figures of speech, the language itself is given a striking embellishment, while figures of speech mean that not the words but the content of the idea itself is given some kind of embellished form.

19 首语重复[repetitio] 意思是同一个词连续地开头几个短语，无论这些短语表达的是相似还是不同的想法，例如：“这是您的功劳，我们将向您表示感谢，这一行动将归功于您。”或者：“西庇阿消灭了努曼西亚，西庇阿摧毁了迦太基，西庇阿创造了和平，西庇阿拯救了国家。”二十九同样：“你敢在论坛上露面吗？你敢面对光明吗？你敢出现在这些人面前吗？你敢说话吗？你敢向他们要求什么吗？你敢恳求免除惩罚吗？你能为自己辩护些什么呢？您认为必须做出什么样的让步？你不是违背了你的誓言吗？你不是背叛了你的朋友吗？你没对你父亲动手吗？简而言之，你不是已经把自己弄脏了吗？耻辱。？”这个人物大大美化了演讲，也赋予了演讲很大的严肃性和力量。因此，我的意思是，你可以用它来美化风格，也可以用它来增强风格。

19 Anaphora[repetitio] means that one and the same word begins several phrases in succession, whether these express similar or different thoughts, e.g.: “Yours is the merit for this, to you we shall show our gratitude, to you this act will be brought to honor.” Or: “Scipio wiped out Numantia, Scipio destroyed Carthage, Scipio created peace, Scipio saved the state.”29Likewise: “You dare to show yourself at the Forum?Do you dare to face the light of day?You dare to appear before these men?Do you dare to speak?Do you dare to ask for anything from them?Do you dare to plead for impunity?What can you say in your defense?What kind of concessions do you think must be made?Haven't you broken the oath you swore?Haven't you betrayed your friends?Haven't you laid a hand on your father?Haven't you, in short, soiled yourself with every conceivabledisgrace.?"This figure considerably embellishes the speech and also gives it a great measure of seriousness and power.I therefore mean that you can use it both to embellish the style and to give it strength.

在溢泪[conversio] 并不像刚才那样重复第一个词，而是一次又一次地回到最后一个词，例如：“迦太基人因罗马人民的正义而被击败，因罗马人民的武器而被击败，因罗马人民的慷慨而被击败。”同样：“社会团结一旦丧失，自由也就丧失了，国家本身也就丧失了。”或者：“盖乌斯·莱利乌斯三十是一位新晋贵族，一位才华横溢、学识渊博、意志坚强、胸怀大志的人；因此，他是这个国家的杰出人物。”进一步问道：“你是在要求他们宣告你无罪吗？那么，你们要求的就是他们作伪证，要求他们对自己名誉的漠不关心，要求罗马法律界向你们的肆无忌惮屈服。”

Atepiphora[conversio] one does not repeat the first word, as just now, but one returns again and again to the last, e.g.: “It was through the justice of the Roman people that the Carthaginians were defeated, through its weapons they were defeated and through its generosity they were defeated.” Likewise: “After the unity of society has been lost, freedom has been lost, the state itself has been lost.” Or: “Gaius Laelius30was a newly ennobled man, a talented man, a learned man, a man of good will and good ambitions; consequently, he was the foremost man of the state.” Further: “Is it their acquittal of you that you ask for?Then it is their perjury you ask for, it is their indifference to their own reputation you ask for, and it is the capitulation of the Roman legal community to your unbridledness you ask for.”

20 辛普洛斯[conplexio] 被称为这两个格法的组合，因此人们既使用了补充语，又使用了前面提到的首语重复，即第一个词重复多次，最后一个词一次又一次地回到，例如：“那些经常破坏条约的人是谁？迦太基人。是谁在战争中表现出如此残忍？迦太基人。玷污意大利的人是谁？迦太基人。那些乞求宽恕的人是谁？迦太基人。所以你们问问自己，他们表达自己的意愿是否合适。”进一步说：“参议院已经定罪的人，人民已经定罪的人，舆论已经定罪的人，你真的能投票支持他无罪释放吗？”

20 Symploce[conplexio] is called the combination of these two figures, so that one uses both epiphora and the previously mentioned anaphora, i.e.The first word is repeated several times and the last word is returned to time and again, e.g.: “Who are those who have often broken treaties?The Carthaginians.Who are they who have shown such cruelty in their warfare?The Carthaginians.Who are they who have defiled Italy?The Carthaginians.Who are they who beg for forgiveness?The Carthaginians.Ask yourselves, then, how appropriate it is for them to have their will expressed.” Further: “He whom the Senate has condemned, he whom the people have condemned, he whom public opinion has condemned, can you really vote for his acquittal?”

经过双关语[traductio] 你可以重复同一个词几次而不会被认为是令人不安的。相反，它使风格更加优雅，例如：“如果一个人的生活中没有比生命更甜蜜的东西，他就缺乏过上有道德的生活的能力。”或者：“你称他为男人。但如果他是个男人，他绝不会如此残忍地追求另一个人的生命。但是，你说，那是他的敌人。“所以他想对敌人进行报复，以至于他自己也被发现是自己的敌人？”同样：“把财富留给富人。如果你想获得财富，同时保持美德，你会发现财富甚至不配成为美德的婢女。”

Bypun[traductio] you can repeat the same word several times without it being perceived as disturbing.On the contrary, it gives the style increased elegance, e.g.: “He who has nothing sweeter in his life than life, he lacks the ability to live a life of virtue.” Or: “You call him a man.But if he had been a man, he would never have pursued another man's life with such cruelty.But, you say, it was his enemy.Did he then want to exact such revenge on an enemy that he himself was found to be his own enemy?” Likewise: “Leave the wealth to the rich.For if you wish to acquire wealth while maintaining virtue, you will find that wealth hardly even deserves to be the maidservant of virtue.”

21当同一个词首先以一种含义使用，然后以另一种含义使用时，就存在同一种图形，例如为什么这么好学？治愈，它会给你很多东西curas（“为什么你担心吗？关于这件事，我讲了很多，这会让你们忧虑？”），更远姓名阿玛瑞iucundum sat, si curtur ne quid insitamari（“因为被爱可以很甜蜜，如果你确保那里什么都没有苦的”）和维尼安对你来说，如果我有参议院veniam（“我将会到来如果参议院给我允许”）。

21The same kind of figure exists when the same word is used first in one meaning, then in another, e.g.Why is it so studious?cures,which gives you many thingscuras (“WhyAre you worried?so much about this matter, which will cause you manyconcern?"),furtherNameamariiucundum sit, si curetur ne quid insitamari (“Becauseto be lovedcan be sweet, if you make sure there's nothing therebitter”)and Veniamto you, if I have the senateveniam (“Iwill cometo you, if the Senate gives mepermission”).

在目前介绍的四种修辞手法中，相同词语的频繁重复并不是因为词语缺乏。相反，这是一个语言细化的问题，通过听觉来感知比用语言解释更容易。

In the four rhetorical figures presented so far, the frequent repetition of the same words is not due to a paucity of words.Rather, this is a matter of linguistic refinement, which is easier to perceive by hearing than to explain with words.

对立[contentio] 是一种由对立面构成的句子结构，如下例所示：“这种暗示开头令人愉快，结尾却很苦涩。”或者：“对你的敌人，你表现得很和解；对你的好友，你却毫不留情。”同样：“当一切平静时，你会变得困惑，但当一切困惑时，你会保持冷静。”当需要冷血时，你会充满热情，但当需要热情承诺时，你却表现得完全冷漠。当需要沉默时，你就大喊；当该说话的时候，你却变得沉默。你在这里却想离开；你走了却想回来。战争时期，你们滔滔不绝地呼吁和平；和平时期，你们却渴望战争。在集会上你们讲道德的语言，在战场上你们却胆怯得连战号的响声都忍受不了。”这种文体的点缀给人留下了深刻的印象，为演讲增色不少。

Antithesis[contentio] is the figure in which the sentence is built up by opposites, as in the following example: “This ingratiation gives a pleasant beginning but a bitter end.” Or: “To your enemies you show yourself conciliatory, to your friends relentless.” Likewise: “When everything is calm, you become confused, but when everything is confused, you maintain your calm.When cold-bloodedness is necessary, you burn with zeal, but when passionate commitment is called for, you show yourself to be completely cold.When silence is desirable, you shout; when it is appropriate to speak, you become mute.You are here but want to be gone; you are gone but want to come back.In time of war you speak incessantly for peace, in time of peace you desire war.In the assembly you speak of virtue, on the battlefield you are too cowardly to even endure the sound of the battle trumpet.” This kind of embellishment of style makes a strong impression and lends brilliance to the speech.

22 撇号[exclamatio] 用于表达痛苦或愤怒，指的是对人、城市、地方或其他事物的称呼，例如：“现在我转向你，Africanus31即使在您去世后，您的名字仍会为国家带来荣耀和荣誉！“正是你们骄傲的孙辈，用自己的鲜血，滋养了敌人的残忍。”同样：“不忠的 Fregellae三十二，你因犯罪而很快地扭曲了自己！你的光芒曾经照亮过意大利，但现在你的根基却所剩无几了。”或者：“你们这群强盗，你们伏击诚实的人，你们想要杀害每一个无辜的公民！你的诽谤就这么成功，难道是法庭的不公正吗？”如果我们在正确的地方谨慎地使用这个比喻，即当问题的重要性似乎需要它时，我们可以在听众中激起我们想要的愤怒程度。

22 Apostrophe[exclamatio] is used to express pain or outrage and means addressing a person, a city, a place or something else, e.g.: “Now I turn to you, Africanus31, whose name, even after your death, brings glory and honor to the state!It is your joyful grandchildren who, with their own blood, have nourished the cruelty of their enemies.” Likewise: “Faithless Fregellae32, how quickly you have twisted away as a result of your crime!Your radiance recently illuminated Italy, but now there are barely any remnants of your foundations left.” Or: “You band of robbers, who lay ambushes for honest people, you have sought the life of every innocent citizen!Has your slander been so successful because of the injustice of the court?” If we use this figure in the right place and sparingly, namely when the importance of the issue seems to call for it, we can arouse in the listener the degree of outrage we desire.

这反问句[interrogatio] 是一种并不总是能给人留下深刻印象或增添风格的人物。但是，在列举了对手的不利之处之后，它又强化了先前的论点，例如：“当你如此全神贯注于言行所有这些事情时，这是否意味着你正在试图诱使盟友脱离国家？是否有必要授权某人来违背你的计划并阻止其实施？”

Therhetorical question[interrogatio] is a figure that does not always make a strong impression or adorn the style.But it does so when, after enumerating the points that are to the opponent's disadvantage, it reinforces the previous argument, according to the following example: “When you were thus fully occupied in word and deed with all these things, did that mean that you were trying to induce the allies to defect from the state or not?And was it necessary or not that someone be authorized who could go against your plans and prevent their implementation?”

23 审议[ratiocinatio] 意味着我们会问自己所说的一切的依据是什么，并且我们经常会向自己寻求对个别陈述的解释。

23 Deliberation[ratiocinatio] means that we ask ourselves what is the basis for everything we say, and we often turn to ourselves to get an explanation of individual statements.

以下可以作为一个例子：“如果我们的祖先因为一个罪孽而谴责一个女人，他们的意思是，通过这一次审判，她已经被判犯有许多罪行。这怎么可能呢？他们认为这名女子不贞洁，还犯有投毒罪。为什么？是的，因为一个将自己的身体交付给最低级欲望的人必定会有很多恐惧。那么是哪些呢？丈夫、父母以及她认识的所有人都可能因她的耻辱而受到影响。进而？对于她如此恐惧的人，她必然会不惜一切代价去毒害他们。为什么？因为任何高尚的动机都无法约束一个因为罪行严重而生活在恐惧之中、因为放荡而大胆、因为女性天性而鲁莽的女人。但是，他们对于这名被判投毒罪的妇女有何看法呢？人们认为她也必然是不贞洁的。为什么呢？因为没有什么比不道德的爱和无节制的欲望更能诱惑她做出这种恶行，而且如果女人的品格败坏，她的身体就不被认为是贞洁的。但当她们对待男人时，她们不也采取同样的态度吗？绝对不是。为什么？因为男人会因为各种欲望而犯下各种罪行，而女人则因为一种激情而犯下各种罪行。”此外：“我们的祖先制定了这样的规则，即如果国王在战斗中被俘，就不能剥夺他的生命，这是件好事。为何如此？因为利用机遇赋予我们的优势去惩罚那些刚刚被同样的机遇置于最高地位的人是不公正的。但是我们难道忘记他曾率领军队对抗我们吗？我忽略了这一点。为什么呢？因为可以要求勇敢的人把为胜利而战的人视为敌人，把失败的人视为同胞，这样，战争就可以因勇敢而缩短，和平就可以因人性而促进。但如果他赢了，他难道不会采取同样的行动吗？不，不确定他是否真的那么明智。但你为什么还要饶过他呢？因为我的习惯是远离愚蠢，而不是模仿愚蠢。”

The following may serve as an example: “If our ancestors condemned a woman for a single sin, they meant that by this single judgment she had been convicted of many crimes.How was this possible?The woman they judged as unchaste, she was also considered guilty of poisoning.Why?Yes, because he who has given his body over to the lowest desires must have many to fear.Which ones then?Husband, parents and everyone else she understands might be affected by her dishonor.And then?Those whom she fears so greatly, she inevitably tries to poison at all costs.Why?Because no honorable motive can restrain a woman who lives in terror because of the enormity of her crime, who is bold because of her wantonness, and who is reckless because of her feminine nature.But what did they think of the woman who had been convicted of poisoning?It was believed that she was necessarily also unchaste.Why that?Because nothing could have tempted her to this evil deed more easily than immoral love and unbridled lust, and if the woman's character was corrupt, her body was not considered chaste.But didn't they take the same approach when it came to men?By no means.And why?Because men are driven to all sorts of crimes by varying desires, while it is a single passion that attracts women to all sorts of crimes.” Furthermore: “It was good of our ancestors to introduce the rule not to deprive any king of his life if he had been taken prisoner in battle.How so?Because it would have been unjust to use the advantages that chance has given us to punish those whom the same chance had just before placed in the most exalted position.But shall we forget that he led an army against us?I ignore that.Why that?Because a brave man can be required to consider those who fight for victory as enemies but to regard those who are defeated as his fellow men, so that war may be shortened by bravery and peace promoted by humanity.But if he had won, wouldn't he have acted the same way?No, it's not certain that he would have been that wise.But why are you sparing him then?Because it is my habit to distance myself from foolishness, not to imitate it.”

24这种修辞手法特别适合用于对话语气的段落，听众的注意力不仅被其精致的风格所吸引，还被他对说话者的反应的好奇心所吸引。

24This figure is particularly well suited to passages in a conversational tone, and the listener's attention is held captive both by the refined style and by his curiosity about the speaker's response.

格言[sententia] 指的是取自实际生活的表达，它以浓缩的形式表明了生活中已经发生或应该发生的事，例如：“我们所有的开始都是困难的。”或者：“那些一直很幸运的人往往并不崇尚美德。”同样地：“不被任何可耻习惯所奴役的人应该被视为自由人。”或者：“永远得不到满足的人和没有足够的人一样贫穷。”此外：“最好的生活方式是你可以选择的；习惯应该让它具有吸引力。”不应低估这种简单的句子，因为不需要任何理由的简短陈述可以带来极大的乐趣。但也可以使用有论据支持的句子，例如：“一切美好生活的规则都应以美德为基础，因为只有美德才能主宰自己，而其他一切都受命运的支配。”同样：“那些被某人的财富所诱惑去培养友谊的人，一旦他的财富消失，他们都会逃离家园。因为当建立联系的因素消失时，就不再有任何理由维持友谊了。”

Maxim[sententia] refers to an expression taken from practical life and which in a concentrated form either shows what happens or what should happen in this life, e.g.: “All our beginnings become difficult.” Or: “It is not above all the one who has always been lucky who usually reveres virtues.” Likewise: “He should be considered free who is not a slave to any shameful habit.” Or: “He who never gets enough is as poor as he who does not have enough.” Furthermore: “The best lifestyle is something that one can choose; habit should make it appealing.” Simple sentences of this kind should not be underestimated, since a brief statement that does not require any justification can give great pleasure.But one can also use sentences that are supported by arguments, for example: “All rules for a good life should be based on virtue, for virtue alone is master of itself, while everything else is subject to the dominion of fate.” Likewise: “Those who are attracted by someone’s wealth to cultivate his friendship, all flee their homes as soon as his fortune is melted together.For when what gave rise to the association has disappeared, then there is no longer any reason to keep the friendship alive.”

还有一种句子类型，可以用两种方式来表述。他们无需任何理由就能站得住脚：“那些在顺境中相信自己逃脱了命运所有打击的人是错误的；但是，那些在幸福中担心不幸的人是明智的。”其中可能还包括一个原因：

There is another type of sentence, which can be formulated in two ways.They may stand without a stated reason: “They are mistaken who in times of prosperity think they have escaped all the blows of fate; but they think wisely who in times of happiness fear misfortune.” They may also include a reason:

二十五“那些认为应该忽视年轻人所犯的罪过的人是错误的，因为这个年龄并不妨碍进行有意义的研究。但那些对年轻人进行特别严厉管教的人是明智的，这样他们就会希望尽早获得能够支持他们一生的美德。”

25“Those who believe that the sins of youth should be overlooked are mistaken, for that age is no obstacle to meaningful study.But those who discipline young people especially severely act wisely, so that they will want to acquire as early as possible the virtues that can support them throughout their lives.”

如果我们真的想表现得像诉讼律师而不是道德家，那么就应该谨慎使用句子。如果运用得当，它们可以大大美化风格。而且，当听者看到某个案例能够用现实生活中无可辩驳的事实来说明时，他也会默默地表示赞同。

Sentences should be used sparingly, if we truly want to appear as litigators and not moralists.Properly applied, they embellish the style very considerably.Moreover, the listener will give his silent approval when he sees that the individual case can be illustrated with an irrefutable fact from practical life.

对比[contrarium] 意思是两个互相矛盾的陈述，用一个陈述简洁地证明另一个陈述，例如：“对于一个总是与自己的利益作斗争的人，你怎么能希望他会促进别人的利益呢？”或者：“你们知道他在友谊中不忠诚，为什么你们认为他能够作为敌人表现出忠诚呢？或者说，你怎么能指望他，一个在私下里一直傲慢得令人无法忍受的人，会变得通情达理、表现出自我意识呢？33当他上台时？如果一个人在与朋友交谈时从未说过一句真话，你怎么能相信他在公开场合不会撒谎呢？同样：“我们害怕在平地上与那些被我们从山上赶下来的人作战吗？那些在人数众多的时候还不能与我们抗衡的人，难道我们还会担心他们现在人数少了而超过我们吗？”

Contrast[contrarium] means that of two contradictory statements, one is used to briefly and simply prove the other, e.g.: “For he who has always fought against his own interests, how can you hope that he will promote the interests of others?” Or: “For he whom you have come to know as faithless in friendship, why do you think that he will be able to show loyalty as an enemy?Or how can you hope that he, who has been unbearably arrogant as a private person, will become accommodating and show self-awareness?33when he comes to power?And he who has never spoken a word of truth in conversation with his friends, how can you believe that he will refrain from lying when appearing in the assembly of the people?” Likewise: “Do we fear to fight on level ground against those whom we have driven down from the hills?Those who could not compete with us when they were more numerous than us, do we fear that they will be superior to us now that they are fewer?”

二十六该图形应设计为简短而连贯的字符串。它通过简短而简洁的形式吸引听众，但最重要的是，通过所述的对比，它以非常有效的方式满足了说话者对证据的需求。从不容置疑的事物中，衍生出不容置疑的事物，使得反驳变得不可能或极其困难。

26This figure should be designed as a short and coherent string of words.It is appealing to the ear through its short and concise form, but above all, through the stated contrast, it satisfies the speaker's need for evidence in a very effective way.From something that is not subject to doubt, something that is is derived in a way that makes refutation impossible or extremely difficult.

冒号[membrum orationis] 表示一个简短而完整的句子，但并没有表达出整个思想，而后面跟着另一个冒号。以下可以作为一个例子。“一方面，你帮助了敌人。”这是一个独立的冒号。还必须补充另一句：“另一方面，你伤害了朋友。”两颗太妃糖可以组成一个修辞格，但最好、最完美的类型是三颗太妃糖组成的修辞格，例如：“你帮助了敌人，伤害了朋友，而你没有考虑到自己的最大利益。”同样：“你没有为国家谋福利，也没有为朋友谋福利，也没有抵抗敌人。”

Colon[membrum orationis] denotes a short and complete sentence, which, however, does not express the entire thought but is in turn followed by another colon.The following can serve as an example.“On the one hand, you helped an enemy.” This is a stand-alone colon.It must be supplemented with another: “On the other hand, you injured a friend.” Two figures of speech may form a rhetorical figure, but the best and most perfect type is that which consists of three figures, e.g.: “You helped an enemy, you injured a friend, and you did not think of your own good.” Likewise: “You have not provided for the good of the state, nor have you been of benefit to your friends or offered resistance to your enemies.”

来[articulus] 指的是单个词语之间的区别太大，以致讲话变得不连贯，如下例所示：“你的敏锐、声音和外表吓坏了你的对手！”同样：“你通过嫉妒、不公正、权力和背叛消灭了你的敌人！”这个图形与前面提到的图形在表现力上的差异在于，前者向目标移动的速度更慢、频率更低，而后者攻击的间隔更近、速度更快。前者的形象是手臂向后拉，通过手的扭转将剑指向对手的身体，而后者的形象是看到身体是如何通过多次重复和快速的打击而受到严重伤害的。

Come[articulus] refers to such a distinction of individual words that the speech becomes choppy, as in the following example: “You have frightened your opponents by your sharpness, voice, appearance!” Likewise: “You have eliminated your enemies by envy, injustice, power, treachery!” The difference in expressive power between this figure and the one previously mentioned is that the former moves more slowly towards its goal and less frequently, while the latter strikes at closer intervals and more quickly.The former figure gives the impression that the arm is pulled back and that the sword is directed towards the opponent's body by a twist of the hand, while in the latter figure one seems to see how the body is severely wounded by many repeated and rapid blows.

二十七一个时期[continuatio] 由表达完整想法的完整短语组成。它最有用的用途有三种：句子、反义词和结尾。谚语示例：“对于一个凭借美德而非运气获得更强大防御能力的人来说，命运无法对他造成太大伤害。”反义词的例子：“如果一个人不把很大的希望寄托在机会上，机会又能给他带来什么重大的伤害呢？”结尾示例：“但是，如果命运对那些将所有计划都交给运气的人拥有最大的权力，那么我们应该小心，不要把一切都交给命运，以免她对我们的控制力过强。”在这三种情况下，词群本身对于句型的表达力都至关重要，因此，除非说话者能够在一连串的词语中对句子、反义词或结论给予额外的强调，否则他的修辞能力就显得微不足道了。但否则，如果没有必要的话，使用这种句号来表达某些事情可能是合适的。

27Aperiod[continuatio] consists of a full-fledged phrase that expresses a completed thought.There are three occasions when it is most useful to use it: in sentences, opposites, and endings.Examples of sentences: “Fortune cannot do much harm to a man who has acquired a stronger defense in virtue than in chance.” Examples of opposites: “For if someone does not attach great hopes to chance, what significant harm can chance do him?” Examples of endings: “But if Fortune has the greatest power over those who have left all their plans to chance, we should be careful not to put everything in Fortune’s hands, so that she does not gain too great a dominion over us.” In all three of these cases, the word cluster itself is of such great importance for the expressive power of the period that the speaker’s rhetorical ability appears insignificant if he cannot give extra emphasis to the sentence, the opposite or the ending in a stream of words.But also otherwise it may be appropriate, if not necessary, to express certain things using this kind of periods.

等结肠[conpar] 是一个由几颗焦糖组成的图形的名称，我们已经讨论过了三十四，音节数大致相同。为了达到这个目的，人们不应该去数音节——这实际上是幼稚的——但是习惯和练习会赋予人们如此高的技能，以至于人们可以直观地设计出在音节数方面相互对应的韵律，例如：“在战场上，父亲遭遇了死亡，在家里，儿子准备了婚礼；预兆之后是灾难。”同样：“其他人的成功都是命运的眷顾，而这个人的美德是他勤奋努力的结果。”

Isocolon[conpar] is the name of a figure consisting of several caramels, which we have already talked about34, with approximately the same number of syllables.To achieve this, one should not have to count syllables – that would actually be childish – but habit and practice give such great skill that one intuitively forms kola that correspond to each other in number of syllables, e.g.: “On the battlefield the father met death, at home the son prepared a wedding; the omens were followed by disasters.” Likewise: “Others are granted success by Fortuna; this man’s virtue is the result of his diligence.”

二十八在这个图中，经常会出现音节数不完全相同但看起来相同的情况，例如冒号为一个或为空的情况。两个音节较短，或者一个冒号中有更多音节，而另一个冒号包含一个或多个更长或更完整的音节，因此这些音节的长度和完整性超过了前一个冒号中的较大音节数。

28In this figure it can often happen that the number of syllables is not exactly the same and yet appears to be, as when a colon is one or empty.two syllables shorter, or when there are more syllables in one colon while the other contains one or more longer or fuller syllables, so that the length and fullness of those syllables outweigh the greater number in the previous colon.

同视者三十五[similiter cadens] 是指在同一个句子中出现两个或多个具有相同格结尾的单词的情况，例如Hominem laudem egentem virtutis，丰富的祝福？（“我应该赞扬一个没有美德但有很多运气的人吗？”）。或者：Huic omnis in pecunia spes est, a sapientia est animus remotus; Diligentia conparat divitias, neglegentia corrumpit animum, et Tornen, cum tia vivit, neminempraese ducit hominem（“他把所有的希望都寄托在金钱上，智慧对他来说完全陌生；他通过勤奋获得财富，通过轻浮毁掉自己的品格。尽管如此，他相信通过这样的生活方式他并不比其他人差。

Homoioptoton35[similiter cadens] is the name of the figure where two or more words with the same case endings occur in the same sentence, e.g.Hominem laudem egentem virtutis, abundantem felicitatis?(“Shall I praise a man who is devoid of virtue but abounds in luck?”).Or:Huic omnis in pecunia spes est, a sapientia est animus remotus; diligentia conparat divitias, neglegentia corrumpit animum, et tornen, cum tia vivit, neminempraese ducit hominem(“He puts all his hope in money, wisdom is completely foreign to him; by his industry he acquires wealth, by his frivolity he ruins his character.Nevertheless, he believes that by this way of life he is no worse than any other person.

同源词[similiter desinens] 表示词尾相同，即使是非变通词，例如Turpiter audesfacere、nequiterstuds dicere、vivis insidiose、delinquis studioose、loqueris odiose（“你敢于做出可耻的行为，你努力说出轻浮的话；你的生活方式引起怨恨，你明知故犯地犯罪，你说出仇恨的话”）。或者：Audaciters territas, humiliters placas（“你的大胆令人恐惧，你的谦逊令人心安”）。

Homoioteleuton[similiter desinens] means that the word endings are the same, even if they are inflexible words, e.g.Turpiter audes facere, nequiter studes dicere, vivis insidiose, delinquis studiose, loqueris odiose(“You dare to act shamefully, you strive to speak frivolously; your way of life arouses resentment, you sin knowingly and willfully, you speak hatefully”).Or:Audaciters territas, humiliters placas(“You are terrifying in your audacity, conciliatory in your humility”).

这两个修辞手法，后者指的是相似的词尾，前者指的是相似的格尾，彼此非常相似，这就解释了为什么那些熟练运用它们的人通常将它们结合在同一个演讲段落中。它是通过以下方式获得的：Perditissima Ratio est amorem petere, pudorem fugere, diligere foram, negelegere famam（“追求爱情而忘记礼仪的要求，追求美而损害自己的名誉，这是极其应受谴责的”）。这里，不仅具有格屈折的单词以相同的词尾结尾，而且缺乏格屈折的单词也以相同的词尾结尾。

These two figures, the latter of which refers to similar word endings and the former to similar case endings, strongly resemble each other, which explains why those who handle them with skill usually combine them in one and the same passage of speech.It is obtained in the following way:Perditissima ratio est amorem petere, pudorem fugere, diligere formam, negelegere famam(“It is utterly reprehensible to pursue love and forget the demands of decency, to love beauty and jeopardize one’s reputation”).Here, not only words with case inflection end in the same endings, but also words that lack such endings.

二十九 双关语[adnominatio] 是一种通过改变单词中的声音或字母来创建一个几乎相同的新单词的结构，以便使用彼此相似的单词来表达完全不同的东西。有很多不同的方法。（1）用同一个字母的缩写或收缩表示，例如：Hic qui se magnifice iactat atque ostentat,可敬罗马人之前venit（“这个人，让自己如此引人注目，如此自夸，被卖为奴隶前他来了去罗马”）。（2）相反的方法得出那么，哪些男性面临风险呢？胜利，它们现在是铁了vincit（“这些人失败在骰子游戏中，它们他是否让立即地打在铁中”）。三十六（3）通过同一封信的延伸，例如欣克鸟弧菌甜蜜导致鸟弧菌（“鸟类”我们从这里到荒地”）。（4）用同一字母的缩写：Hic，tametsi videtur esse Honoris cupidus，tantum tamen库里亚姆爱量子库里亚姆？（“让我们知道，这个人似乎雄心勃勃，但他是否同样爱着教廷[=参议院] 就像角斗士一样教廷？“）。(5) 添加字母如下：他自己可以做到。脾气暴躁，不同意数学obtemperare（“这个人可以掌握除非他愿意服从爱”）。（6）删除以下字母：硅莱诺的维他塞特·塔姆夸姆母狮，传统的人生三十七（“如果他开枪的话耦合器就好像他们狮子，他仍然会活着”。（7）颠倒字母如下：法官们，看看纳沃在习惯相信邪恶（“陪审团的先生们，请考虑一下，你们是否更愿意相信一个勤劳超过一个徒劳男人”）。（8）通过换文如下：dtligere oportet quem velis diligere（“你必须选择你可以将要爱”）。

29 Paronomasia[adnominatio] is the figure where, by changing sounds or letters in a word, one creates a new one that is almost identical, so that words that are similar to each other are used to express completely different things.There are many different approaches.(1) By abbreviation or contraction of the same letter, e.g.Hic qui se magnifice iactat atque ostentat,venerablebefore the Romansvenit (“This man, who makes himself so remarkable and is so boastful,was sold into slaverybeforehe cameto Rome”).(2) The opposite method givesHere, what men are at risk?vincit,they are iron nowvincit (“The men whom thisdefeatsin dice games, themdoes he letimmediatelybeatin iron”).36(3) By extension of the same letter, e.g.Hincaviumsweetness leads toavium(“The Birds’sweetness for us from here tothe wasteland”).(4) By abbreviation of the same letter:Hic, tametsi videtur esse honoris cupidus, tantum tamencuriamlove quantumCuriam?(“Let it be known that this man seems ambitious, but is he therefore equally in love withthe curia[=senate house] as in the gladiatorCuria?”).(5) By adding letters, as follows:He could do it himself.temperer,nisi amori mathobtemperare (“This man couldmasterhimself, unless he preferred toobeylove”).(6) By deleting letters, as follows:Silenone'svitaset tamquamlioness,vitae tradidisset see37(“If he had shotcoupleras if they werelion,he would still be alive”).(7) By reversing letters, as follows:See, judges, whethernavoonhabitbelieve in evil(“Consider, gentlemen of the jury, whether you would rather trust aindustriousthan onevainMAN").(8) By exchanging letters, as follows:Dtligere oportet quem velis diligere(“You mustchooseone that you canwilllove").

这些是双关语类型，涉及字母的轻微改变、加长、重新排列等。

These are the types of paronomasia that involve letters being slightly changed, lengthened, rearranged, etc.

三十但也有其他类型的词语相似性不那么明显，尽管也没有达到完全没有相似性的程度。这些图形类型之一可以通过以下示例来说明：Quid veniam、quisim、quem insimulem、cuiprosim、quae postulem、brevi cognoscetis（“我为何而来，我是谁，我指控谁，我帮助谁，我要求什么，你很快就会知道”）。这里，有些词语表现出一定的相似性，诚然不像前面的情况那么明显，但偶尔还是可以使用的。以下是另一种类型的示例：Demus operam, Quirites, ne omnino patres应征入伍者他妈的（“公民们，让我们阻止参议员们据称已成为被骗了”。在这个双关语中，相似度比前一种情况要大，但比前面提到的情况要小，因为不仅添加了字母，而且同时也删除了字母。

30But there are other types where the similarity in words is not so prominent, although not to the point where similarity is completely absent.One of these figure types can be exemplified by the following:Quid veniam, quisim, quem insimulem, cuiprosim, quae postulem, brevi cognoscetis(“Why I come, who I am, whom I accuse, whom I help, what I ask for, you will soon know”).Here, some words show a certain similarity, admittedly not as obvious as in the previous cases, but which can nevertheless be used occasionally.The following are examples of another type:Demus operam, Quirites, ne omnino patresconscripts circumscriptsfuck you(“Citizens, let us preventthe senatorsis reputed to have becomeduped”).In this paronomasia, the similarity is greater than in the previous case but less than in the previously mentioned ones, since letters have not only been added but at the same time also been removed.

第三种类型是基于一个或多个专有名词出现在不同的格中。

There is a third type, which is based on one or more proper nouns appearing in different cases.

31名字示例：“亚历山大”三十八来自马其顿的他从小就刻苦训练，以培养坚强的性格。亚历山大的功绩为全世界赢得了荣誉和名声。每个人都害怕亚历山大，但同时又深爱着他。如果亚历山大的寿命更长，马其顿的长矛就会飞越海洋。”这里，同一个专有名词不断以新的格形式出现。如果你使用几个不同格形式的专有名词，就会出现以下双关语：“不该死的死亡阻止了提比略·格拉古三十九继续领导国家。盖乌斯·格拉古40成为类似暗杀的受害者，这次暗杀突然将这位热心的爱国者从国家中心夺走。萨图尼努斯41被邪恶之人欺骗，一场犯罪的背叛夺走了他的生命。这是你的血，德鲁苏斯四十二洒落在你家的墙壁上和你父亲的脸上。刚才他们服从了苏尔皮西乌斯43但不久之后，他们不仅阻止他活下去，而且还阻止他被埋葬。”

31Example of a name: “Alexander”38from Macedonia trained hard from boyhood to achieve strength of character.Alexander's merits have won honor and fame throughout the world.Everyone feared Alexander but at the same time loved him dearly."Had Alexander been given a longer life, the Macedonians' lances would have flown across the ocean." Here, one and the same proper noun has been given in constantly new case forms.If you use several proper nouns in different case forms, the result is a paronomasia of the following kind: “An undeserved death prevented Tiberius Gracchus39from continuing to lead the state.Gaius Gracchus40fell victim to a similar assassination, which suddenly snatched this ardent patriot from the heart of the state.Saturninus41was deceived into believing evil men, and a criminal treachery robbed him of his life.It is your blood, O Drusus42, which has sprinkled the walls of your home and the face of your father.Just now they obeyed Sulpicius43in everything, but shortly afterwards they prevented him not only from living but also from being buried.”

三十二最后这三种修辞手法，第一种基于相同的格结尾，第二种基于相同的词结尾，第三种基于双关语，在实际讲话中应该极少使用，因为它们似乎不可能不经过努力和努力就形成。然而，这种表演更适合娱乐性演讲，而不是针对实际问题的演讲。四十四如果演讲者频繁使用这样的比喻，他的可信度、给人留下印象的能力以及他的严肃性就会受到损害。他不仅丧失了作为演讲者的权威，而且使用这种以精神和优雅为特征而非尊严或美感的风格手法也引起了冒犯。宏伟和美丽的事物能让人长久愉悦，而灵性和优雅的表达却很快就会使耳朵——我们最疲惫的感官——感到厌倦。如果经常使用这些图形，就会给人一种喜欢孩子气的讲话风格的印象，但是如果谨慎使用它们，改变它们的设计，并在整个演讲过程中传播它们，这些引人注目的装饰就会为演讲增添吸引人的光彩。

32These last three rhetorical figures, the first of which is based on the same case endings, the second on the same word endings, and the third on paronomasia, should be used extremely rarely in real speech, since they do not seem to be possible to formulate without work and effort.However, performances of this kind are more suitable for entertaining speeches than for speeches on a real issue.44The speaker's credibility, his ability to make an impression, and his seriousness are therefore undermined if he makes frequent use of such figures.Not only is his authority as a speaker lost, but he also causes offense by using this stylistic device, which is characterized by esprit and elegance, not dignity or beauty.What is grand and beautiful can long please, while spirituality and elegant formulations soon tire the ear, the most jaded of our senses.If one uses these figures frequently, one gives the impression of being fond of a childish style of speech, but if one uses them sparingly, varies their design, and spreads them throughout the speech, these eye-catching ornaments lend an appealing luster to the presentation.

33 亚甲藻[subiectio] 意味着我们要么询问对方，要么询问我们自己，有什么话可以支持他的立场，或者损害我们的立场。然后，我们指出哪些结论是可能的，哪些是不可能的，哪些结论对我们有利，或者通过同样的论证，哪些结论对对方不利，例如：“所以我问，这个人是如何变得如此富有的？他继承了一大笔财产吗？但父亲的财产被卖掉了。他有得到什么遗产吗？无法提出索赔；然而，他的所有亲属都剥夺了他的继承权。他通过起诉获得什么利益了吗？不，远非如此；然而，他自己却在一场赌博中损失了一大笔钱。45。如果正如你们所见，他没有通过任何一种方式致富，那么要么他家里长了金子，要么他的钱是从某种非法渠道获得的。”或者：“法庭上的先生们，我经常注意到，许多人试图通过提及一些光荣的行为来为自己辩护，甚至他们的敌人也无法质疑。但我的对手却不能做这样的事。他应该依靠他父亲的功绩吗？但你却在宣誓后判了他死刑。还是他会回归自己的​​生活？那是什么样的人生，他在什么样的背景下过着光荣的人生？因为你们都知道，在你们的眼中，他在这里是如何生活的。但也许他会列出他的亲戚，以便给你留下深刻的印象？但没有。那他还会依赖他的朋友吗？但没有人会认为被称为他的朋友是不光彩的。”同样：“你认为你的敌人有罪，你当然会将他绳之以法，不是吗？根本不是，因为你没有经过审判或调查就谋杀了他。难道你不害怕禁止这种行为的法律吗？远非如此；在您看来，它们甚至没有被写下来。当他向你提起你们昔日的友谊时，你有什么印象吗？不，你无论如何都杀了他，甚至并表现出更大的热情。当他的孩子们跪倒在您的脚下时，您是否心生怜悯？不，你残忍至极，甚至拒绝为他们的父亲举行葬礼。”

33 Hypophora[subiectio] means that we ask either the other party or ourselves what can be stated in support of his position or to the detriment of ours.We then point out which conclusions are possible or which are not, things that benefit us or, through the same argument, disadvantage the other party, according to the following example: “So I ask, how could this man have become so rich.Has he inherited a large fortune?But the father's property was sold.Has he received any legacy?It is not possible to claim; however, he has been disinherited by all his relatives.Has he made any profit by suing?No, far from it; however, he himself has lost a large sum of money on a betting deal.45. If, as you all see, he has not become rich in any of these ways, then either gold must grow in his house, or he must have obtained his money from some illicit source.” Or: “Your Honors, I have often noticed that many people try to defend themselves by referring to some honorable act, which even their enemies cannot question.But my counterpart can't do anything like that.For shall he take refuge in his father's merits?But you have condemned him to death after taking an oath.Or will he return to his own life?What kind of life is that, and in what context has he lived an honorable life?For you all know how he lived here in your sight.But perhaps he will list his relatives, so that they will impress you?But there aren't any.Then he will rely on his friends?But there is no one who would not consider it dishonorable to be called his friend.” Likewise: “Your enemy, whom you considered guilty, you brought to justice, of course?Not at all, for you murdered him without trial or investigation.Didn't you fear the laws that forbid this?Far from it; in your opinion, they weren't even written down.When he reminded you of your old friendship, did this make an impression on you?No, you murdered him anyway, evenwith even greater zeal.And how was it, when his children threw themselves at your feet, were you seized with pity?No, in your bottomless cruelty you also denied their father burial.”

三十四这种修辞手法具有很大的力量和分量，因为它通过说这件事还没有做来回答应该做什么的问题。这是一种凸显行为卑鄙本质的非常简单的方法。

34This rhetorical figure possesses a great deal of power and weight, since it answers the question of what should have been done by saying that this has not been done.This is thus a very simple method of highlighting the despicable nature of an action.

在这个图的一个变体中46我们也可以让副词指代我们自己吗，例如：“当我被这么多酒吧包围时，我会做什么呢？斗争？但那样的话，我们出去的部队就会很少了；此外，地形条件对我们非常不利。我应该留在营地吗？但我们既没有期待增援，也没有给养。我该离开营地吗？但我们被锁在里面了。我会牺牲士兵的生命吗？但我认为，我接收他们的条件是，我要尽我所能，为了他们的祖国和父母，保护他们不受伤害。我会拒绝敌人的条件吗？但士兵的福祉高于信任。”四十七这种假设的积累导致一个显而易见的结果：所有可能的替代方案中没有一个比实际选择的方案更可取。

In a variation of this figure46can we also let the hypophora refer to our own person, e.g.: “For what would I have done, when I was surrounded by so many bars?Fight?But then we would have gone out with a very small troop; moreover, the terrain conditions were very unfavorable for us.Should I stay in the camp?But we had no reinforcements to expect, nor did we have provisions for our sustenance.Should I leave the camp?But we were locked in.Would I sacrifice the lives of the soldiers?But I considered myself to have received them on condition that I would, to the best of my ability, preserve them unharmed for their homeland and their parents.Would I reject the enemy's terms?But the well-being of the soldiers takes precedence over the trust.”47An accumulation of such hypophores results in it seeming obvious that none of all possible alternatives should have been preferred to the one that was actually chosen.

高潮[gradatio] 是一种修辞手法，说话者要先重复前一个词，然后再说后面的词，如下例所示：“这些人给了我们什么自由的希望？他们想要什么就得到什么，他们能得到什么，他们敢于做什么，他们敢于做什么，而且他们所做的似乎并不会让你不高兴。”或者：“我没有考虑过这件事，也没有批准；我没有批准过这件事，也没有立即开始行动；我没有开始行动过这件事，也没有完成这件事；我没有批准过这件事，也没有完成这件事。”同样：“Africanus四十八勤能补拙，能干出名堂，名声显赫。”或者：“希腊帝国由雅典人统治；雅典人被斯巴达人击败；斯巴达人被底比斯人征服；底比斯人被马其顿人击败，马其顿人在短时间内通过战争征服了亚洲，并将其并入希腊帝国。

Climax[gradatio] is a figure of speech in which the speaker does not move on to a subsequent word until he has first repeated a previous one, as in the following example: “For what hope of freedom do these men give us?What they want they get, what they get they can, what they can they dare, what they dare they do and what they do does not seem to displease you.” Or: “I did not consider this without approving, I did not approve without immediately starting to act myself, I did not start to act without completing it and I did not complete it without approving it.” Similarly: “Africanus48acquired ability through diligence, honor through ability, envious people through honor.” Or: “The Greek empire was dominated by the Athenians; the Athenians were defeated by the Spartans; the Spartans were subdued by the Thebans; the Thebans were conquered by the Macedonians, who in a short time subdued Asia in war and added it to the Greek empire.”

三十五不断重复前一个单词有一定的复杂性，这是这个图形的特点。

35There is a certain sophistication in the constant repetition of the previous word, which is characteristic of this figure.

定义[definitio] 是用来描述某种事物特征的术语，例如：“国家至上是国家尊严和伟大的缩影。”49或者：“对某人的不公正包括攻击、侮辱或对某人行为的羞辱性质疑。”同样：“你们表现的不是节俭，而是贪婪，因为节俭意味着小心地保管自己拥有的东西，而贪婪则是不公正地攫取他人的财产。”此外：“你表现的不是勇敢，而是鲁莽，因为勇敢是为了经过计算的利益而无视辛劳和危险，从而使经过计算的优势显得更加重要，而鲁莽则是像角斗士一样，不假思索地将自己暴露在危险之中，忍受痛苦。”这种比喻之所以被认为是有效的，是因为它以如此清晰和简洁的方式强调了某件事的全部含义和内涵，以至于似乎没有必要使用更多的词语，而用更少的词语又被认为不可能做到这一点。

Definition[definitio] is the term used to describe a figure that briefly and completely states the characteristic properties of something, e.g.: “The supremacy of the state is the epitome of the dignity and greatness that characterizes the state.”49Or: “An injustice to someone means assault, insult, or shamefully casting suspicion on someone’s conduct.” Similarly: “You are not showing thrift but greed, since thrift means carefully preserving what one owns, while greed is an unjust encroachment on the property of others.” Furthermore: “You are not showing bravery but foolishness, since bravery is to disregard toil and danger for the sake of a calculated benefit, whereby calculated benefits seem to outweigh, while foolishness means, like a gladiator, exposing oneself to dangers and enduring pain without any thought.” This figure is considered effective for the reason that it emphasizes the full meaning and significance of something in such a clear and concise way that it both seems unnecessary to use more words and is perceived as impossible to do so with fewer.

过渡[transitio] 是一种修辞手法的名称，它首先对所说的内容进行简要总结，然后同样简要地说明接下来的内容，如下例所示：“现在你知道他是如何对待他父亲的；现在考虑一下他自己作为父亲的表现。”或者：“你知道我为这个人做了多少善事。现在听听他是如何向我表达感激之情的。”通过这种修辞手法，演讲者达到了两个目的：第一，他提醒听众他已经说过的话；第二，他让听众为接下来要说的话做好准备。

Transition[transitio] is the name of the figure that first gives a brief summary of what has been said and then just as briefly tells about the continuation, according to the following example: “You now know how he has behaved towards his father; now consider how he himself has been as a father.” Or: “You know the good deeds I have done towards this man.Now hear how he has chosen to show me gratitude.” With this figure of speech, the speaker achieves two purposes: first, he reminds the listener of what he has already said, and second, he prepares him for what is to come.

三十六 修正案[correctio] 取消刚才所说的内容，并用看起来更正确的内容代替，例如：“但如果被告询问了他的主人，或者只是暗示一下，这件事就可以毫无困难地进行下去。”或者：“因为在这些人征服之后，或者更确切地说是被击败之后——我该如何称呼这种给胜利者带来的痛苦多于好处的胜利呢？”同样：“嫉妒是美德的伴侣，它大多陪伴着好人，而不是迫害他们！”这个数字给听众留下了深刻的印象。因为当用普通的词语来表达某件事时，人们会觉得它只是被注意到了，但当说话者纠正自己时，它就会呈现出更恰当的表达方式。但有人可能会反对，从一开始就决定最好、最精致的词语不是更好吗，尤其是在写作的时候？在某些情况下，这并不可取，即改变措辞是为了表明，如果使用常用词汇，所讨论的想法似乎用不清楚的语言表达出来，而如果找到更恰当的词语，则表达形式会更清晰。但如果从一开始就找到这个词，人们就不会注意到思想或词语选择中的愉悦感。

36 Amendment[correctio] cancels what has just been said and puts in its place something that seems more correct, e.g.: “But if the accused had asked his host, or rather just made a hint, the matter could have been carried out without difficulty.” Or: “For after these men had won, or rather been defeated – for what shall I name the victory that brought more misery than good to the victors?” Likewise: “O envy, companion of virtue, which for the most part accompanies good men, nay pursues them!” This figure makes a strong impression on the listener.For when a thing is presented with an ordinary word, one gets the impression that it has only been noted, but as the speaker corrects himself, it takes on a more apt expression.But wouldn't it be better, someone might object, to decide on the best and most exquisite word from the very beginning, especially when writing?There are occasions when this is not preferable, namely when the changed choice of words is intended to show that the thought in question seems to be expressed in an unclear language if one uses common vocabulary, while it takes on a clearer form when one finds a more apt word.But if one had found that word from the beginning, one would not have noticed the pleasantness in either the thought or the choice of words.

三十七 瞬态[occultatio] 存在于我们说我们正在忽略、没有意识到或不想说我们将要说的事情时，例如：“如果我觉得这个场合合适，我肯定会说几句关于你童年的事，那时你沉迷于各种放荡的行为；现在我故意忽略这件事。此外，我不会深入讨论军事保民官举报你在军事服役中玩忽职守的事实。你已经向 Lucius Labeo 支付了赔偿金50我也不认为侮辱与此有任何关系。我不会提及这些，而是​​回到这次审判的核心问题上。”同样：“我不想提你从我们的盟友那里得到了钱；我并不急于指出你们掠夺了城市、王国和每个人的家园；我对你的所有偷窃和抢劫行为置之不理。”这种比喻适用于以下情况：没有理由让别人注意到所讨论的问题；或者对某事进行偷偷暗示更为有效，而这种暗示通常需要冗长或不恰当的解释；或者这种解释无法足够清晰或容易反驳。这样的次引起阴险的怀疑比明确地陈述可以反驳的事情更有利。
