37 Passing by[occultatio] exists when we say that we are passing over, are not aware of, or do not want to say the very thing we are about to say, e.g.: “For I would certainly say a few words about your childhood, which you devoted to all kinds of licentiousness, if I found this occasion suitable; now I am passing over the matter intentionally.Furthermore, I am not going to go into the fact that the military tribunes reported you as negligent in military service.That you have paid damages to Lucius Labeo50I don't think insult has anything to do with it either.I will not mention any of this, but will return to the main issue of this trial.” Similarly: “I refrain from mentioning that you have received money from our allies; I am not anxious to emphasize that you have plundered cities, kingdoms, and everyone’s homes; I disregard all your thefts and robberies.” This figure is used when there is no reason to draw the attention of others to the matter in question, or when it is more effective to make a furtive hint about something that would otherwise require a lengthy or inappropriate explanation, or when such an explanation cannot be made with sufficient clarity or is easy to refute.SuchtimesIt is more advantageous to arouse insidious suspicions than to explicitly state something that can be refuted.

分离[disiunctum] 是当我们让两个或多个子句以其各自的谓语结尾时使用的格，例如：“罗马人民看到努曼西亚被摧毁，迦太基被消灭，科林斯被夷为平地，弗雷杰莱被消灭。”51努曼廷人不需要依靠自己的体力，迦太基人不需要依靠自己的战略知识，科林斯人的智慧和狡猾也无法为他们提供支持，而弗雷格兰人则不需要依靠与我们进行文化和语言交流。”同样：“身体美要么因疾病而枯萎，要么随着时间的流逝而消失。”如您所见，后一个示例中的两个子句以及前一个示例中的所有子句都以其自己的特定谓语结尾。

Disjunction[disiunctum] is the figure called when we let two or more clauses end with their own separate predicate, e.g.: “The Roman people saw to it that Numantia was destroyed, Carthage was wiped out, Corinth was razed to the ground, and Fregellae was annihilated.”51The Numantines had no use for their physical strength, the Carthaginians had no joy in their strategic knowledge, the Corinthians' wisdom and cunning gave them no support, and the Fregellians had no joy in their cultural and linguistic community with us.” Similarly: “With bodily beauty it is the case that it either withers through illness or is erased with the passage of time.” As can be seen, both clauses in the latter and all clauses in the former example end with their own separate predicate.

三十八 连词[coniunctio] 表示句子的前后部分由置于其间的谓语连接在一起，例如：“身体美要么因疾病而枯萎，要么随着时间的流逝而消逝。”

38 Conjunction[coniunctio] means that the earlier and later parts of the sentence are held together by the predicate placed between them, e.g.: “It is either through illness that bodily beauty withers, or with the passage of time.”

附件[adiunctio] 是谓语不放在句子中间，而是放在句首或句末的一种结构。开头的例子：“枯萎使身体变得美丽，无论是由于疾病还是随着时间的流逝。”结尾示例：“身体之美，要么因疾病，要么随着时间的流逝而枯萎。”

Adjunct[adiunctio] is the figure where the predicate of the sentence is not placed in the middle but either at the beginning or at the end.Example of the beginning: “Wither makes bodily beauty, either through illness or with the passage of time.” Example of the end: “With bodily beauty, it is so that it either through illness or with the passage of time fades.”

分离属于光面风格，这就是为什么应谨慎使用这种图形以避免过度饱和。连词适合简洁的表达风格，因此应该更多地使用。这三个图形都属于同一基本类型。

Disjunction belongs in the glossy style, which is why this figure should be used sparingly to avoid oversaturation.Conjunction suits the concise presentation style and should therefore be used more often.All three of these figures belong to the same basic type.

复制[conduplicatio] 意思是重复一个或多个词，目的是夸大或引起怜悯，如下例所示：“你惹麻烦了，盖乌斯·格拉古52，我们的国家和社会陷入动荡！”或者：“当你的母亲跪倒在你脚下时，你难道不感动吗？“你不感动吗？”同样：“现在你竟敢出现在这些人面前，叛徒？叛徒们，我说你们竟敢出现在他们面前？”当同样的话被重复时，这会给听者留下非常强烈的印象，并给对方造成更大的伤害，就像一把武器一次又一次地击中身体的同一个部位一样。

Duplication[conduplicatio] means repeating one or more words with the intention of exaggerating or arousing pity, as in the following example: “You are causing trouble, Gaius Gracchus52, unrest in our nation and our society!” Or: “Were you not moved when your mother fell at your feet?Were you not moved?” Likewise: “Now you dare even appear before these people, traitors?Traitors to the fatherland, I say, do you dare to appear before their eyes?” When the same words are repeated, this makes a very strong impression on the listener and inflicts a greater wound on the opponent, as if a weapon were to strike the same part of the body again and again.

同义词[interpretatio] 是一种修辞手法，它不是重复相同的词语，而是用具有相同含义的其他词语来代替已经说过的话，如下例所示：“你已经从根本上摧毁了我们的国家，你已经从根本上摧毁了我们的社会。”或者：“你可耻地殴打了你的父亲，你犯罪地对赋予你生命的人下手。”当第一个话语的力量被后面的同义短语所重申时，听众必然会受到强烈的影响。

Synonymous[interpretatio] is the figure of speech which, instead of repeating the same words, replaces what has already been said with some other word with the same meaning, as in the following example: “You have torn the state up by the roots, you have destroyed our society to its foundations.” Or: “You have shamefully beaten your father, you have criminally laid hands on the one who gave you life.” The listener is necessarily strongly affected when the force of the first utterance is renewed by the following synonymous phrase.

三十九 逆转[commutatio] 意思是将两个互不相容的观念通过逆转来表达，后者以前者为出发点，但含义相反，例如：“人必须吃饭才能活着，而不是活着才能吃饭。”或者：“我不写诗，因为我写不出我想写的诗，也不想写我能写的诗。”同样：“关于这个人，人们所说的一切都不宜说；人们所说的一切都不宜说。”或者：“一首诗应该是一幅会说话的画，一幅画应该是一首无声的诗。”同样：“如果你愚蠢而保持沉默，那么你就是聪明的；但如果你聪明而保持沉默，那么你就是愚蠢的。”不可否认，其结果非常有效，因为相反观点的陈述也与言语的逆转相匹配。由于这种修辞手法很难理解，我给出了几个例子来阐明它的性质；一旦你理解了它，作为演讲者你就更容易找到自己的例子。

39 Reversal[commutatio] means that two mutually incompatible ideas are expressed by a reversal in such a way that the latter takes its starting point from the former but with the opposite meaning, according to the following example: “One must eat to live, not live to eat.” Or: “I refrain from writing poems, because I cannot write the poems I want and do not want to write the poems I can.” Likewise: “What one says about this man is not fitting to be said; what is fitting to be said is not said.” Or: “A poem should be a painting that speaks, a painting should be a mute poem.” Likewise: “If you are stupid and therefore silent, you are wise; but if you are wise and nevertheless silent, you are stupid.” Undeniably, the result is very effective in that the statement of the opposite idea is also corresponded to the reversal in words.Since this rhetorical figure is difficult to conceive, I have given several examples of it to clarify its nature; once you understand it, it will be easier for you as a speaker to find your own examples.

放弃[permission] 是一种修辞手法，我们用它来表示在某些事情上我们完全服从于别人的意志，如下例所示：“既然身体和灵魂是我唯一剩下的东西，在被剥夺了其他一切之后，我把这些东西，唯一剩下的东西，留给你和你的判断。”你可以随心所欲地利用我、虐待我；你可以肆无忌惮地决定如何对待我；只要你说话，只要你发出信号，我就会服从！”

Giving up[permissio] is the figure of speech in which we say that in some matter we completely subordinate ourselves to the will of someone else, according to the following example: “Since body and soul are the only things I have left, after having been deprived of everything else, I leave to you and your discretion these very things, the only thing that remains of much.”You are permitted to use and abuse me as you please; you can decide what you want about me with impunity; speak, give a sign, and I will obey!”

这个比喻当然也在其他一些场合被使用，但在唤起同情心方面尤其有效。

This figure is certainly used on several other occasions, but it is particularly effective when it comes to evoking compassion.

40 阿波里[dubitatio] 表示说话者似乎在询问他应该使用两个或多个词中的哪一个，例如：“在那种情况下，国家遭受了领事的巨大伤害——我应该说，愚蠢还是卑鄙，或者两者兼而有之？”或者：“你竟敢这么说，你这个——好吧，我该怎么称呼你才能符合你的性格呢？”

40 Apori[dubitatio] denotes the situation where the speaker seems to ask which of two or more words he should rather use, e.g.: “On that occasion the state suffered great harm from the consuls’ – shall I say the stupidity or the meanness, or both?” Or: “You dare to say this, you of all people the – well, what shall I call you to do justice to your character?”

消除[expeditio] 意味着在列举了几种可能的行动方案之后，一个人拒绝了所有方案，只留下一个，并根据以下例子决定采用哪一个：“既然你所声称的土地确实属于我，你必须证明它是在你占有它时被遗弃的，或者它是根据习俗成为你的，或者你买的，或者你继承的。因为我在那里，所以排除了你占有废弃土地的可能性。该财产也不可能通过继承成为您的。尚未知晓购买情况。我从活着的时候起，我的财产就没能通过继承落到你们手里。所以，事实是，你们强行将我从我的财产中驱逐出去了。”

Elimination[expeditio] means that after enumerating several possible courses of action, one rejects all but one, which one decides on, according to the following example: “Since it is a fact that the land you claim belonged to me, you must prove either that it was abandoned when you took possession of it, or that it became yours by custom, or that you bought it, or that you inherited it.Since I was there, it rules out your taking possession of abandoned land.It is also impossible for the property to become yours through inheritance.No purchase is known.Since I am alive, my property has not been able to come into your hands through inheritance.So it remains that you have forcibly expelled me from my property.”

41这个图形在事实问题的论证中特别有用，但与大多数其他图形不同，它并不是可以随时使用的；仅当所讨论问题的性质证明其合理时才可使用。

41This figure is particularly useful in arguments within the factual question, but unlike most other figures, it is not the case that you can use it whenever you want; you can only use it if the nature of the issue being discussed justifies it.

不连词结构[dissolutum] 表示一种不使用并列连词来呈现各个部分的表达方式，例如：“遵从父亲的意愿，顺从亲戚，做朋友的意愿，尊重法律。”或者：“把一切都花在辩护上，不要提出异议，审问你的奴隶，努力寻找真相。”这个数字包含能量和功率，有助于简洁的演示。

Asyndeton[dissolutum] denotes a way of presenting in which the separate lines are presented without coordinating conjunctions, e.g.: “Follow the will of your father, obey your relatives, do your friends’ will, respect the laws.” Or: “Spend everything on your defense, make no objections, have your slaves interrogated, strive to find the truth.” This figure contains energy and force and is useful for a concise way of presenting.

帕索皮西斯[praecisio] 意思是说，一句话的剩余部分没有说完，例如：“我和你们并不平等地作战，因为罗马人民认为我——是的，我没有这么说，以免有人觉得我自命不凡——但罗马人民常常认为你们应该受到羞辱。”同样：“你敢这么说，你刚刚还在别人家里——不，我不敢这么说，以免有人认为我在说一些对我来说不合适的事情，而我正在谈论一些对你来说合适的事情。”这里未说出口的怀疑比详细的解释更能引起人们的不满。

Aposiopesis[praecisio] means that the remainder of a statement that has been begun is left unsaid, e.g.: “I do not fight with you on equal terms, for the Roman people have regarding me – yes, I refrain from saying it, lest perhaps anyone should find me pretentious – but the Roman people have often considered you deserving of dishonor.” Likewise: “You dare to say this, you who were just in another’s house – no, I dare not say it, lest anyone should think that I am saying something that is not fitting for me, when I am telling you about things that are fitting for you.” The unspoken suspicion here arouses greater displeasure than a detailed explanation would have done.

结论[conclusio] 是一种用简短的论证来证明从前面所说或所做的事情必然得出什么结论的修辞手法，例如：“但是，如果希腊人从神谕中得知，没有菲罗克忒忒斯的箭的帮助，特洛伊城就无法攻下，而这些箭只能见面。帕里斯，那么杀死他就等于攻占了特洛伊。”53

Conclusion[conclusio] is the figure that, with a short argument, establishes what necessarily follows from what was previously said or done, according to the following example: “But if the Greeks had learned from the oracle that Troy could not be taken without the help of Philoctetes' arrows, and if these could onlymeet.Paris, then killing him was certainly tantamount to taking Troy.”53

四十二还有十种修辞手法需要处理。我没有在演讲的不同地方漫无目的地展示这些内容，而是选择在上述数字之后对它们进行单独的回顾。原因是他们都属于同一类。因为它们共同的特点是，它们脱离了通常的词义，并通过一种语言提炼，赋予词语新的内容。

42There are still ten figures of speech to be dealt with.Instead of presenting these aimlessly in different places in my presentation, I have chosen to devote a separate review to them after the aforementioned figures.The reason is that they all belong to the same class.For what is characteristic of all of them is that they depart from the usual word meaning and, through a kind of linguistic refinement, give the words a new content.

拟声词[nominatio] 是这些修辞手法中的第一个。当谈到缺乏名称或名称不恰当的事物时，这个比喻提醒我们，我们可以自己发明一些合适的词，这些词要么是拟声词，就像我们的祖先创造的词“bräka”、“rårna”、“mumble”、“ssla”，要么是为了表达，例如：“这个人对国家的攻击引起了可怕的骚动54跻身社会前列。”应谨慎使用这个数字，以避免频繁使用新表达方式而产生厌倦感。但是，如果明智地使用比喻，并且不要过于频繁，那么表达的新颖性就不会冒犯任何人，相反，它还能美化语言。

Onomatopoeia[nominatio] is the first of these rhetorical figures.When it comes to things that either lack or have an inappropriate name, this figure draws our attention to the possibility of inventing some apt word ourselves, either onomatopoeic like the words created by our ancestors “bräka”, “rårna”, “mumble”, “ssla”, or to achieve expressiveness, e.g.: “This man’s attack on the state caused a terrible uproar54among the foremost in society.” This figure of speech should be used sparingly to avoid the boredom that can arise when a new expression is used frequently.But if one uses the figure judiciously and not too often, the novelty of the expression does not offend at all, but on the contrary adorns the language.

拟人化[pronominatio] 意思是说使用别名来阐明无法通过通用名称表达的内容。例如：有人能提到格拉古兄弟吗55说：“但这不是阿非利加努斯”56孙子。”同样，当有人谈到他们的对手时说：“法庭上的先生们，现在看看这位剑齿响尾蛇先生是如何对待我的。”这样，人们就不能不优雅地赞扬和批评身体和道德品质以及外部环境，57使用昵称代替真实姓名。

Antonomasia[pronominatio] means that one saysuses a byname to clarify the content of something that cannot be expressed through the common name.So for example:can someone with an allusion to the Gracchi55say: “But such was not Africanus'56grandchildren.” Likewise, when someone, speaking of his opponent, says: “Look now, gentlemen of the court, how this Mr. Saber Rattlesnake has treated me.” In this way, one cannot without elegance both praise and blame both physical and moral qualities, as well as external circumstances,57by using the nickname instead of the actual name.

43 转喻[denominatio] 是一种从相关和相邻的事物中衍生出来的表达形式，通过这种表达方式，无需用通常的词语来命名某事物就可以理解它。要么让较大的代表较小的，就像有人谈论塔尔佩亚岩石时58称之为“卡比托利欧山”，<...>59或者为发明者发明，例如有人说“酒”而不是“巴克斯”，或说“面粉”而不是“谷神星”，60 <…>61或者工具主人的身份，就像有人这样称呼马其顿人：“长矛并没有那么快就占领希腊”，或者以同样的方式提到高卢人：“阿尔卑斯山外的标枪也没有那么容易地从意大利赶走。”您还可以根据事件的原因来命名事件，例如如果一个演讲者想强调某人在战争中取得了成就，然后说：“火星62强迫你这样做”，或者根据原因解释原因，例如我们称某个职业为懒惰，是因为它使从业者变得懒惰；我们称寒冷为迟钝，是因为它使我们变得迟钝。凡是包含某种内容的东西，都可以给其内容命名，例如：“意大利在战争中不能被打败，希腊在学习中不能被打败”；这里列出的不是希腊人和意大利人，而是包含这些国家的国家。内容为其包含的内容命名，例如当有人谈论黄金、白银或象牙时，其意思是“财富”。这些转喻在教学时很难分类，但在寻找时却很难找到，因为这种转喻的使用不仅在诗人和演讲者中很普遍，而且在日常语言中也很普遍。

43 Metonymy[denominatio] is a figure that derives from related and adjacent things the expression by which something can be understood without naming it with its usual word.One either lets the larger stand for the smaller, as when someone speaking of the Tarpeian rock58calls it “the Capitoline”, <…>59or the invented for the inventor, as when someone says “the wine” instead of Bacchus, or “the flour” instead of Ceres,60 <…>61or the tool of the owner, as when someone names the Macedonians in the following way: “The lances did not so quickly come into possession of Greece”, or in the same way with reference to the Gauls: “Nor was the transalpine javelin driven away from Italy so easily.” One can also name an event after its cause, e.g.if a speaker wants to emphasize that someone has accomplished something in war and then says: “Mars62forced you to do this”, or the cause according to what causes it, e.g.when we call a profession lazy because it produces laziness in its practitioners, or the cold sluggish because it makes us sluggish.That which contains something can give a name to the content in the following way: “Italy cannot be defeated in war, Greece not in learning”; instead of Greeks and Italians, the countries that contain these are stated here.The content gives a name to what it contains, e.g.when someone talks about gold, silver or ivory but means “wealth”.These metonymies are more difficult to categorize when teaching than to find when searching for them, since the use of such metonymies is widespread not only among poets and speakers but also in everyday language.

迂回说法[circumitio] 是一种修辞手法，通过限制来表达简单的想法，例如：“西庇阿的远见摧毁了迦太基的力量。”因为在这里人们可以简单地说“西庇阿”和“迦太基”，63如果不是为了修饰语言的话。

Periphrase[circumitio] denotes a phrase that expresses a simple idea by means of a circumscription, e.g.: “Scipio’s foresight crushed the power of Carthage.” For here one could simply have said “Scipio” and “Carthage,”63if it had not been for a desire to embellish the language.

四十四 超级巴顿64[transgressio] 通过倒置或转置来颠倒正常的词序。反转示例：Hoc vobis deos deos immortales arbitror dedisse美德赞成维斯特拉（“我相信这是不朽的诸神赐予你的，作为对你的奖励你的美德”）。搬迁示例：Instabilis就在这个地方财富货币。普遍性令人厌恶的埃里普伊维旺迪借口学院（“不稳定的命运对这个人产生了非常大的影响。一切手段因为命运剥夺了他的美好生活”。）这种不掩盖内容的转移在前面讨论的时期被广泛使用。65。对于句号，应力求语序接近诗歌的节奏，以达到完美而动听的圆润效果。

44 Hyperbaton64[transgressio] reverses the normal word order, either by inversion or by transposition.Example of inversion:Hoc vobis deos immortales arbitror dedissevirtueprovestra (“This I believe the immortal gods have bestowed upon you as a reward foryour virtue”).Example of relocation: Instabilisin this very placefortunecurrency.Omnesinvidious eripuit bene vivendi casusfaculties (“TheUnstable Fortunehas had a very great influence on this man.All meansfor chance has deprived him of a good life”).A transfer of this kind, which does not obscure the content, is widely used in the periods previously discussed.65When it comes to periods, one should strive for a word order that in a way comes close to the rhythm of poetry, so that they can achieve a perfect and appealing rounding.

夸张[superiatio] 是一种通过放大或缩小某事物来破坏事实的比喻。它既可以单独使用，也可以比较使用。独立夸张的例子：“但如果保持统一，我们将以太阳的升起和落下来衡量帝国的疆域。”比较中的夸张用于表达相似性或优越性。相似的例子：“他的身体像雪一样白。”优先顺序示例：“从他口中流出的话语比蜂蜜还甜。”以下情况属于同一类型：“他的盔甲光泽如此强烈，以至于太阳的光芒显得更弱了。”

Hyperbole[superiatio] is a figure that does violence to the truth by either magnifying or diminishing something.It is used either independently or in a comparison.Example of free-standing hyperbole: “But with unity preserved, we will measure the extent of the empire by the rising and setting of the sun.” Hyperbole in comparison is used to express either similarity or superiority.Example of similarity: “His body was white as snow.” Example of superiority: “From his mouth flowed speech sweeter than honey.” The following cases belong to the same type: “The shine of his armor was so strong that the light of the sun appeared weaker.”

提喻[intellectio] 意思是用一小部分来表示整体，或者用整体来表示部分。可以通过部分来理解整体，方式如下：“婚礼笛声没有让你想起他的婚礼吗？”在这里，整个婚礼仪式都通过一个符号——笛子来理解。部分由整体指定，例如当有人对穿着特别昂贵衣服的人说以下的话时：“你向我展示了你的财富并吹嘘你的丰富宝藏。”

Synecdoche[intellectio] means that the whole is designated by a small part or the part by the whole.The whole is understood through the part in the following way: “Did you not remember his marriage by the wedding flutes?” Here, the entire wedding ceremony is understood through a single sign, the flutes.The part is designated by the whole, e.g.when someone says the following to a person who appears in particularly lavish attire: “You show me your wealth and boast of your abundant treasures.”

45通过使用单数，可以指复数，例如：“西班牙人来援助迦太基人，阿尔卑斯山外的野蛮人也来援助迦太基人；在意大利，也有许多人穿着同样含义的托加长袍。”在下列情况下，复数表示单数：“这场可怕的灾难使他的心因深深的悲痛而麻木；因此，他从肺深处吸了一口气，悲痛地叹了口气。”前一种情况指的是几个西班牙人、高卢人和罗马公民，而后一种情况指的是一颗心脏和一个肺。66。前者减少数字以增强表达的优雅，后者增加数字以使语言更具表现力。

45By using the singular, one can refer to the plural, e.g.: “The Spaniard came to the aid of the Carthaginians, as did the Transalpine savage; also in Italy many were clad in toga of the same meaning.” In the following case, the plural denotes the singular: “The terrible catastrophe paralyzed his heart with deep sorrow; therefore he drew breath from the depths of his lungs and sighed with grief.” For in the former case several Spaniards, Gauls and Roman citizens are referred to, in the latter one heart and one lung66In the former case, the number is reduced to enhance the elegance of the expression, in the latter it is increased to make the language more expressive.

卡塔克雷斯[abusio] 是一种修辞手法，用一个类似的、密切相关的词来代替一个常见的词，例如：“人类的力量是短”、“小”体长”，“长的人类的能动性”，“大的演讲”或“参加小的称呼”。因为这里很容易理解，虽然含义不尽相同，但含义相关，但通过压缩其含义，词语的用法得到了扩大。

Catachres[abusio] is the figure by which, instead of a certain common word, one presses the meaning onto a similar and closely related one, e.g.: “The powers of man areshort”, “smallbody length”, “thelongthe agency of man”, “alargespeech” or “participate in asmallCall".For it is easy to understand here that words with related, though not identical, meanings have gained an expanded use by compressing their meaning.

隐喻[translatio] 是指当一个词的含义从一个事物转移到另一个事物时，如果它们之间的相似性似乎可以证明这种转移是合理的。在下列情况下用它来说明某事：“这场起义使意大利在突然的恐惧中醒来”；缩短表达，如这里：“军队的到来瞬间摧毁了这个国家”；避免冒犯，例如：“他的母亲每天都庆祝婚礼”；给予额外的强调，例如：“任何悲伤或不幸都无法平息这个人的敌意并满足他可怕的残忍”；贬低某事，例如：“他夸口说他提供了很大的帮助，因为当我们处于最危险的时候，他轻轻地向我们吹了一口气”；为了语言的修饰，例如：“有一天，由于腐败者的卑鄙而枯萎的国家事务将通过保守派的效率而繁荣。”据说隐喻应该有节制和得体，以便它能够以可以理解的理由过渡到类似的事物，而不会给人留下不加区分、漫无目的地、急切地跳到完全不同的东西的印象。

Metaphor[translatio] means that the meaning of a word is transferred from denoting one thing to another, when the similarity between them seems to justify the transfer.It is used to illustrate something in the following cases: “This rebellion caused Italy to wake up in sudden terror”; to shorten the expression, as here: “The recent arrival of the army extinguished the state in an instant”; to avoid offensiveness, e.g.: “His mother celebrates a wedding every day”; to give extra emphasis, e.g.: “No sorrow or misfortune could have quenched this man’s enmity and satisfied his hideous cruelty”; to belittle something, e.g.: “He boasts that he has been of great help, for he blew gently on us when we were in the greatest danger”; for the sake of linguistic embellishment, e.g.: “One day the affairs of the state, which have withered due to the meanness of corrupt men, will flourish through the efficiency of conservatives.” It is said that there should be moderation and decency in a metaphor, so that it transitions to a similar thing on understandable grounds and does not give the impression of jumping indiscriminately, aimlessly, and eagerly to something completely different.

46 寓言[permutatio] 是一种说一套、但意指另一套的格法。它有三个部分：相似性、论证性或对比性。它基于相似性，当几个相关的隐喻相互衔接时，例如：“当狗接管狼的角色时，我们应该把我们的牛托付给谁来保护？”它以论证的形式出现，即以夸大或缩小的意图建立与人、地点或物体的相似性，例如如果有人称德鲁苏斯为“格拉古兄弟的苍白形象”。67这个寓言使用了对比，例如有人为了取笑一个浪费、放荡的人，称呼他为“节俭、孝顺”。无论是从对立面出发的后一种情况，还是从相似点出发的前一种情况，都可以通过比喻来提出论点。基于相似性的论证示例：“我们的国王阿伽门农现在说了什么，或者更确切地说——尽管他很残忍——我们的阿特柔斯说了什么？”68基于矛盾的论证是存在的，例如，如果我们称打他父亲的恶棍为“埃涅阿斯”69以及猖獗的通奸者“希波吕托斯”。

46 Allegory[permutatio] is the figure where one says one thing but means something else.It has three parts: similarity, argument or contrast.It is based on similarity, when several related metaphors follow one another, e.g.: “For when the dogs take over the role of wolves, to whose protection shall we entrust our cattle?” It takes the form of an argument, when a similarity is established with a person, a place, or some object with the intention of magnifying or diminishing, as e.g.if someone were to call Drusus “a pale image of the Gracchi”.67The allegory uses contrast, e.g.when someone, with the intention of making fun, calls a wasteful and dissolute person “thrifty and dutiful”.Both in the latter case, where one starts from opposites, and in the former, which starts from similarities, one can create arguments through a metaphor.Examples of arguments based on similarity: “What does our king Agamemnon say now, or rather – as cruel as he is – our Atreus?”68Arguments based on contradiction exist, for example, if wecalls the scoundrel who struck his father “Aeneas”69and the rampant adulterer “Hippolytus”.

在我看来，这大致对应于关于修辞手法应该说的内容。现在，主题本身促使我转向修辞手法。

This roughly corresponds to what, in my opinion, should be said about the figures of speech.Now the subject itself urges me to move on to the figures of speech.

四十七 分配[distributio] 意味着将多个指定的角色分配给几个事物或人，如下例所示：“法官先生们，你们当中任何一位尊敬参议院的人都必须憎恨这个人，因为他总是以极大的厚颜无耻攻击参议院。渴望获得骑士称号的人70将在国家中闪耀光芒，必然也希望这个人受到最严厉的惩罚，这样他就不会因为自己的卑鄙行为给这个如此辉煌的庄园带来污秽和耻辱。你有父母，就通过惩罚这个人来表明，不信神的人从你身上得不到任何好处。“你们这些有孩子的，就当做一个表率，让大家看看我们国家对这种人的惩罚有多么严厉。”或者：“参议院的职责是向国家提供建议；官员的职责是认真执行参议院的意愿；人民的任务是用选票选择和批准最明智的政策和最合适的人选。”同样：“检察官的任务是提出指控，辩护律师的任务是反驳和驳斥，证人的任务是陈述他所知道或听到的内容，法官的任务是确保每个人都遵守自己的任务。如果您，卢修斯·卡西乌斯，允许证人进行辩论并做出超出他所知或所闻的假设，那么您将会混淆检察官和证人的权利，助长不诚实证人的偏见，并导致被告两次为自己辩护。”71这种修辞手法非常丰富，因为它能够用一句话表达很多意思。通过在图中为每个事物分配特定的任务，它将一大堆事物区分开来。

47 Distribution[distributio] means that a number of specified roles are distributed among several things or people, as in the following example: “Gentlemen judges, whoever of you holds the name of the Senate dear must hate this man, since he has always attacked the Senate with the greatest impudence.He who desires that the knighthood70shall shine with brilliance in the state, must of necessity also wish that this man undergo the most severe punishment, so that he may not, through his meanness, bring filth and disgrace upon this so glorious estate.You who have parents, show by punishing this man that godless men have nothing to gain from you.You who have children, set an example to show what severe punishments our state has determined for such people.” Or: “It is the duty of the Senate to assist the state with advice; it is the duty of the officials to conscientiously carry out the will of the Senate; it is the duty of the people to choose and approve with their votes the wisest policies and the best-disposed men.” Similarly: “It is the duty of the prosecutor to bring charges, of the defender to refute and refute, of the witness to say what he knows or has heard, and of the judge to see that each of these adheres to his duty.If you, Lucius Cassius, allow a witness to argue and make assumptions beyond what he knows or has heard, you will consequently confuse the rights of the prosecutor with those of the witness, encourage the bias of a dishonest witness, and cause the accused to defend himself twice.”71This rhetorical figure possesses great richness in that it is able to express so much in a nutshell.By assigning each one its specific task in the figure, it keeps a whole host of things apart.

四十八 直言不讳[licentia] 用于当一个人在那些不应该被尊重或害怕的人面前行使自由言论的权利，因为他认为自己有充分的理由将某些错误归咎于他们或他同情的人，如下例所示：“公民们，你们感到惊讶吗？每个人都忽视了你们的利益。因为没人愿意代表你？没人为你辩护吗？你们都怪自己，别再胡思乱想了！什么说不是每个人都应该谨慎地对你的事务发表立场？想想那些曾经捍卫过你的事业的人，试着想象他们的承诺，然后想想他们都发生了什么！那么你必须意识到，说实话，是你的冷漠，或者更确切地说是懦弱，导致这些人全部在你面前被杀害，而且正是由于你的选票，他们的敌人才登上了权力的最高位置。”或者：“法官先生们，你们为什么不愿意给这个恶人定罪，为什么要给他重新审判？对他的指控不是很明显吗？这一切难道还没有得到目击者的证实吗？另一方面，防守能力不足不是毫无用处吗？您当时是否担心，如果第一次开庭就判刑，会被认为太残忍？但当你避免了那种你实际上不必害怕的责备时，你却将自己暴露在了另一种责备之下，那就是被认为胆小和懦弱。最大的灾难已经降临到个人和国家头上，而当更大的灾难似乎即将来临时，你却坐着打哈欠。白天你等待夜晚，夜晚你等待白天。每一天，都会有至少一些悲伤或不愉快的消息被报道出来——但是，对于造成这种痛苦的人，你是否想给他更多的喘息机会，让他在你的怀抱中走向国家的毁灭，你是否想让他尽可能长时间地留在我们的社会里？

48 Outspokenness[licentia] is used when one nevertheless exercises one's right to speak freely before those who should not be respected or feared, because one believes one has good reason to blame them or the people they sympathize with for some error, as in the following example: “Are you surprised, citizens, that everyone disregards your interests?Because no one wants to represent you?About no one coming to your defense?You have yourselves to blame, stop wondering!For what is it that says that not everyone should be careful about taking a position on your affairs?Consider the men who once defended your cause, try to visualize their commitment, and then consider what happened to them all!Then you must realize, to tell the truth, that it was your indifference, or rather cowardice, that led to all these being murdered before your eyes, and that it was thanks to your votes that their enemies reached the highest position of power.” Or: “For what reason did you, gentlemen of the judges, hesitate to condemn this godless man, and why did you give him a new trial?Wasn't what was accused of him quite obvious?Hadn't all this been confirmed by witnesses?On the other hand, wasn't the defense useless in its poverty?Were you afraid at that time that you would be considered cruel if you sentenced him at the first hearing?But while you avoided that reproach, which in fact you had no need to fear, you have exposed yourself to another, namely, to being considered timid and cowardly.The greatest calamities have befallen both individuals and the state, and while even greater ones seem imminent, you sit and yawn.During the day you await the night, and during the night you await the day.Not a day goes by without at least some sad or unpleasant news being reported – but the one who is the cause of this misery, do you want to give him further respite and keep him under your arms to the state's destruction, do you want to keep him in our society as long as you can?

49如果这种直言不讳给人留下了太深刻的印象，有几种方法可以抵消它。可以立即添加诸如“我在此呼吁您的功绩”、“我想看看对您的智慧的考验”或“我呼吁您证明行动的力量”之类的话，以便直言不讳所激起的感情被赞扬所抑制。因此，这种方法意味着赞美可以平息听众的愤怒和烦躁，而开放可以阻止他误入歧途。如果使用得当，这种方法对于修辞和友谊都大有裨益，这样听众就不会犯罪，而我们说话的人就会显得是他们的朋友和真理的朋友。

49If such outspokenness makes too sharp an impression, there are several ways to counteract it.It is possible to immediately add something like “I appeal here to your merits”, “I want to see a test of your wisdom”, or “I call for your proven power of action”, so that the feelings stirred up by the outspokenness are dampened by the praise.The method thus means that praise calms the anger and irritation of the listener, while openness deters him from going astray.Used in the right place, this method is of great benefit both in rhetoric and in friendship, so that those who listen may not sin and so that we who speak may appear to be their friends and friends of the truth.

但有一种直言不讳是基于更微妙的算计，也就是说，我们要么按照观众希望我们谴责他们的方式进行谴责，要么说我们担心观众会如何看待我们实际上知道每个人都会毫不费力接受的事情——“但事实迫使我们不得不说出来。”我将对这两种类型进行说明。前者的例子：“公民们，你们太容易相信别人，太温顺了；你们对每个人都太信任了。你想象每个人都在努力履行对你的承诺。您错了。你毫无根据的希望和你自己的愚蠢早已成为你脸上的污点，你宁愿向别人索取你拥有的权力，也不愿亲手夺取。”下面的话可以作为后一种坦率的一个例子：“法庭上的先生们，我一直是这个人的朋友，但是这份友谊——虽然我担心你们会如何看待，但我还是要说——是你们夺走了我的友谊。那么怎么办呢？“好吧，为了获得你的认可，我宁愿把袭击你的人视为敌人，而不是朋友。”

But there is a type of outspokenness which is based on a more subtle calculation, namely, when we either rebuke the audience as they themselves want us to rebuke them, or say that we are anxious about how the audience will take what we know in fact that everyone will accept without difficulty – “but the truth compels us to speak nevertheless.” I will illustrate both of these types.Example of the former: “Citizens, you are too trusting and meek; you trust too much in everyone and everyone.You imagine that everyone is making an effort to fulfill their promises to you.You are wrong.Your baseless hopes and your own foolishness have long been a black eye on your face, you who have preferred to demand from others what you had power over, rather than seize it with your own hands.” The following may serve as an example of the latter kind of outspokenness: “I have been this man’s friend, gentlemen of the jury, but that friendship – although I fear how you will take it, I must nevertheless say it – it is you who have robbed me.How then?"Well, to gain your approval, I would rather consider the one who attacked you as my enemy than as my friend."

50因此，根据我所展示的，这种被称为“直言不讳”的形象可以用两种方式来使用。一是提出尖锐的批评，但如果措辞过于严厉，则可能产生轻重缓和的效果。第二个涉及伪装，我接下来会讨论。掩饰中，批评无需软化，它只是模仿直言，但内心却契合听者的心态。

50This figure, called “outspokenness,” can therefore, according to what I have shown, be used in two ways.One is to express sharp criticism, which can, however, be mitigated if it is formulated too harshly.The second concerns pretense, which I discussed next.In dissimulation, there is no need to soften criticism, since it only imitates outspokenness but at heart corresponds to the listener's mindset.

利托特斯[deminutio] 用于当一个人首先声称自己或所辩护的人由于天赋、有利环境或自身努力而拥有一些明显的优势，然后为了不给人留下傲慢或自夸的印象而淡化或贬低这种优势时，例如以下方式：“为此，法官先生们，我相信我有权说，通过工作和勤奋，我确保我在军事科学方面并不是最差的。”如果演讲者说“确保我是最好的”，那么即使这是事实，听起来也会显得妄自尊大。他的话刚好能避免恶意并确保获得赞赏。再如：“那么是贪婪还是贫穷促使他犯罪呢？贪婪？但他对朋友却极其慷慨，这表明他宽宏大量。贪婪的反面。贫困？但他的父亲留给他——我不想夸大——一笔不小的遗产。”这里也避免使用“大”或“非常大”这样的词。当谈论您自己或客户的优点时，您应该记住使用这个数字。因为在实际生活中，轻率地谈论这些事情会引起嫉妒，而在公开演讲时会引起厌恶。就像在生活中人们可以通过提前思考来避免嫉妒一样，作为演讲者人们可以通过智慧来避免厌恶。

Litotes[deminutio] is used when one first claims that one, or the person one is defending, possesses some clear advantage either by nature or through favorable circumstances or one's own efforts, and then tones down or belittles this in order not to give the impression of arrogance or boasting, for example in the following way: “For this, gentlemen of the jury, I believe I have the right to say, namely that through work and diligence I have ensured that I am not directly among the worst when it comes to military science.” If the speaker had said “ensured that I am the best,” it would have sounded arrogant, even if it were true.As the words fell, he said just enough to avoid ill will and ensure appreciation.Another example: “So was it greed or poverty that drove him to commit the crime?Greed?But he has been extremely generous to his friends, which indicates liberality, i.e.the opposite of greed.Poverty?But his father left him – I do not want to exaggerate – a not inconsiderable fortune as an inheritance.” Here too, words like “large” or “very large” are avoided.When talking about your own or your clients' merits, you should remember to use this figure.For thoughtless talk about such things arouses envy in practical life and dislike when one appears as a public speaker.In the same way that in life one avoids envy by thinking ahead, as a speaker one can ward off dislike through wisdom.

51 描述72[description] 是清楚、明确和着重指出某一行为后果的比喻，例如：“但是，如果各位法官投票宣告此人无罪，他就会像一头从笼子里放出来的狮子或一头挣脱锁链的猛兽一样，在广场上游荡，磨砺牙齿，攻击每个公民的财产，攻击所有人，朋友和敌人，认识的和不认识的，夺走他们的名誉，夺走他们的生命，还有一些人毁坏房屋和家园：他将动摇国家的根基。因此，各位法官，请将他驱逐出境，让所有人免于恐惧，同时也确保你们自己的安全！因为如果你们让这个人逍遥法外，那么这对你们自己不利——相信我，法官们——你们释放了一只野蛮而可怕的野兽。”同样：“但是，法官先生们，如果你们判处我的当事人严厉的惩罚，那么在同一次判决中，你们也会让很多人陷入毁灭。他年迈的父亲把所有的希望都寄托在这个年轻人身上，但他将失去生存的意志；他的年幼的孩子失去了父亲的支持，将会遭到父亲的敌人的嘲笑和嘲讽；他的整个家族都将因这场不应有的灾难而灭亡。但他的敌人一旦赢得残酷胜利的血腥屠杀，就会嘲笑他们的苦难，并在言语和行动上暴露他们的傲慢。”另一个例子是：“公民们，你们中没有人不知道，城市被攻占后通常会带来什么样的苦难。那些手持武器自卫的人会被立即以最残忍的方式杀害；其余的人，年龄足够、体力足够承受苦役，就被拖去当奴隶，而那些年龄不够、体力足够承受苦役的人，就被剥夺了生命；最后，敌人放火焚烧房屋，房屋也同时起火，那些因自然或自愿而通过亲属关系或友谊关系团结在一起的人，则四散流离。有的孩子被从父母的怀抱中夺走，有的孩子死在父母的怀抱中，还有一些孩子被羞辱在父母的脚下。“法官大人，没有人能够用语言公正地描述此事，也没有人能够用言语表达出这场灾难的恐怖。”这种修辞手法可以用来激起愤慨或怜悯，因为一个行为的所有后果都用简短而清晰的句子一起呈现。

51 Description72[descriptio] is the figure that clearly, distinctly and emphatically points out the consequences of an action, e.g.: “But if you, gentlemen of the judges, vote for the acquittal of this man, he will immediately, like a lion let out of his cage or a terrible beast loosed from his chains, roam the Forum, sharpening his teeth to attack the property of every citizen, attacking everyone, friends and enemies, known and unknown, robbing some of their reputations, others of their lives, and still others ruining houses and homes: he will shake the state to its foundations.Therefore, gentlemen of the court, expel him from the state, free everyone from fear, and not least ensure your own safety!For if you let this man go unpunished, it is against yourselves – believe me, gentlemen of the judges – you have unleashed a wild and horrible beast.” Likewise: “But if you, gentlemen of the judges, sentence my client to a severe punishment, you will at the same time, in one and the same judgment, plunge many into ruin.His aged father, who in his old age has placed all his hope in this young man, will lose the will to live; his little children, deprived of their father's support, will be exposed to the scorn and ridicule of their father's enemies; his whole house will perish through this undeserved misfortune.But his enemies, as soon as they have brought home the bloody palm of cruel victory, will mock their misery, and they will reveal their arrogance in deed as well as in word.” Another example: “For none of you, citizens, is ignorant of the sufferings that usually follow when a city is taken.Those who have defended themselves with weapons in hand are killed immediately with the utmost cruelty; of the rest, those who are old enough and strong enough to endure hard labor are dragged away into slavery, while those who are not are deprived of their lives; finally, the houses are simultaneously set ablaze by the enemy, and those who by nature or by their own free will were united by ties of kinship or friendship are scattered; of the children, some are torn from the arms of their parents, others are killed in their arms, others are again disgraced at their feet.There is no one, gentlemen of the jury, who is able to do justice to the matter in words or to convey in speech the horror of such a catastrophe.” With the help of this kind of rhetorical figure, one can evoke indignation or pity, since all the consequences of an action are presented together in short and clear turns.

52 分配73[divisio] 意味着将问题分成两个选项，并对每个选项给出一个理由来回答，如下例所示：“我为什么要责备你？如果你是正直的，你就不应该受到责备；如果你不诚实，你就不会在意它。”或者：“我现在有什么理由强调我的优点呢？如果你记住它们，你就会感到厌烦；如果你忘记了它们，那么我的行动就没有任何影响力，我的言语又能做什么呢？”同样：“有两件事可以诱惑人去获取利益，那就是贫穷和贪婪。我们知道你贪婪，而你本应该和你的兄弟平等分享；我们现在看到你很贫穷，需要帮助。那么你怎么能让人觉得你没有犯罪动机呢？”这种分配和分配（“立场澄清”）指的是演讲的第三部分——我在第一本书中讨论过74紧接在事实陈述部分之后——在于后者通过列举或总结来完整地解决演讲中要讨论的要点，而现在所讨论的数字意味着直接处理一个问题。对图中涵盖的两个或多个步骤中的每一个步骤的原因进行简要说明是一种修饰风格的方式。

52 Division73[divisio] means breaking a question into two alternatives and answering each alternative by giving a reason, as in the following example: “Why should I reproach you at all?If you are upright, you have not deserved blame; if you are dishonest, you will not care about it.” Or: “What reason would I have now to emphasize my merits?If you remember them, I will bore you; if you have forgotten them, I have consequently made no impression in action, and what could I then accomplish in words?” Similarly: “There are two things that can tempt man to gain, poverty and greed.We know that you showed greed when you should have shared equally with your brother; that you are poor and needy we see now.How can you then make it appear that you had no motive for the crime?” The difference between this kind ofdivisionand thedivision(“position clarification”) which denotes the third section of a speech – which I discussed in the first book74immediately after the section on factual presentation – lies in the fact that the latter, by enumerating or summarizing, addresses the points to be discussed in the speech in its entirety, while the figure in question now means that a question is dealt with directly.The brief statement of reasons for each of the two or more steps the figure encompasses is a way of embellishing the style.

积累[frequentatio] 意味着将整个案件中不同部分的观点集中到一起，从而使陈述更具强调性、更尖锐或更深刻，如下例所示：“这个人真的有什么问题吗？你有什么理由宣告他无罪？他背叛了自己的荣誉，并等待着别人；他鬼鬼祟祟、肆无忌惮、厚颜无耻、傲慢自大；不敬父母，不知感恩朋友，敌视亲人；对上级固执己见，对同事、同志居高临下，对下属残忍无情；总之，他是所有人都无法忍受的。”

Accumulation[frequentatio] means bringing together points of view that belong in widely different parts of the whole case into a single place in order to thereby make the presentation more emphatic, sharper, or more incisive, as in the following example: “Is there really anything wrong with this man?What reason do you have to acquit him?He has betrayed his own honor and lies in wait for others; he is sly, unbridled, impudent, and arrogant; he is disrespectful to his parents, ungrateful to his friends, and hostile to his relatives; he is stubborn toward his superiors, condescending to his peers and comrades, and cruel to his subordinates; in short, he is unbearable to everyone.”

53同类的积累在属于事实认定问题的案件中非常有用。如果单独表达这些怀疑，则会发现它们微不足道且薄弱，但如果将它们集中在演讲中的一个地方，事情就不再显得可疑，而是变得显而易见，例如如下：“因此，法庭上的先生们，不要孤立地考虑我的论点，而是对它们进行集体评估，就好像它们构成一个整体一样。如果被告因该男子的死亡而受益；如果他的行为不道德，性格阴险，财产极少，而且这种罪行除了他自己以外没有给任何人带来好处；如果没有其他人能够如此巧妙地实施犯罪，或者他自己不能以其他更具启发性的方式实施犯罪；如果他没有忽略采取任何必要的行动；如果选择的地点是最佳的，那么采取行动的机会就非常有利，攻击的时间也非常合适；如果花费了很长时间来实施计划，那么就不无希望能够掩盖恶行；此外，如果该男子被谋杀之前，有人看见他独自一人出现在谋杀案发生的地点；如果在犯罪发生后不久听到了受害者的声音；如果很明显犯罪嫌疑人在谋杀案发生后半夜回到家，并在第二天结结巴巴、语无伦次地谈论谋杀案；如果这一切部分得到了证人的证实，部分得到了酷刑下的供词的证实，并且也得到了普遍意见的支持，而这种意见在有证据支持的情况下必然是正确的——那么，法官先生们，在全面评估这些论点之后，你们有责任对所涉罪行不抱怀疑，而是确信它。因为，可能纯粹是偶然地，上述某个情节会使被告显得像个嫌疑人，但是，从第一个情节到最后一个情节，所有情节都适用于他，这一事实必然预示着他是犯罪的同谋。这不可能是巧合。”75这个数字具有很大的影响力，在事实调查问题中几乎总是必要的。但它也可以不时用于其他问题和任何类型的演讲中。

53Of the same kind is the accumulation that is so useful in cases that belong to the fact-finding question.Suspicions that, when expressed individually, turned out to be insignificant and weak, make a thing no longer seem suspicious but appear obvious if you gather them in a single place in the speech, e.g.as follows: “Therefore, gentlemen of the court, refrain from considering my arguments in isolation from each other, but make a collective assessment of them, as if they constituted a single whole.If the accused had an advantage from the man's death; if his conduct is immoral, his character is insidious and his fortune is extremely small and this crime has benefited no one but himself; if no one else could have committed the crime as skillfully or if he himself could not have done it in some other more cunning way; if he did not neglect to take any necessary measures; if the chosen place was the best imaginable, the opportunity to act favorable and the time of attack particularly suitable; if a very long time was spent in putting the plan into action, not without good hope of being able to conceal the evil deed; if, moreover, before the man was murdered he had been visible alone at the place where the murder took place; if shortly afterwards during the crime itself the voice of the victim was heard; if it is clear that the suspect after the murder returned home in the middle of the night and the next day spoke stammeringly and incoherently about the murder; If all this has been confirmed partly by witnesses and partly by confessions made under torture, and is also supported by the general opinion, which is inevitably correct when it is based on evidence – then, gentlemen of the judges, it is incumbent upon you, after a comprehensive assessment of these arguments, not to entertain suspicions about the crime in question, but to be convinced of it.For it may be by pure chance that one or another of the circumstances cited will make the accused appear as a suspect, but the fact that all the circumstances, from the first to the last, apply to him necessarily presupposes that he is complicit in the crime.It can't be a coincidence.”75This figure holds a lot of power and is almost always necessary in the fact-finding question.But it can also be used from time to time in other questions and in any kind of speech.

54 装饰[expolitio] 的意思是反复强调同一个论点，但给人的印象是不断地说出新的东西。这个图形可以用两种方式设计：你可以重复完全相同的想法，也可以围绕它画一圈。重复同一个想法时，不能以完全相同的方式进行——这只会让听众感到厌倦，而又不修饰风格——而要有所变化。这可以通过三种方式实现：言语、表演以及对待该物质。

54 Decoration[expolitio] means dwelling on the same argument but giving the impression of constantly saying something new.This figure can be designed in two ways: you can either repeat exactly the same idea or you can also circle around it.When repeating the same idea, it must not be done in exactly the same way – this would only tire the listener without embellishing the style – but with variation.This happens in three ways: throughthe words, the performanceand the way totreatthe substance.

(1) 词语选择的变化意味着一个人首先形成一个想法，然后用不同的词语一次或多次表达同一个想法，但这些词语的含义相同，如下例：“如果社会的安全受到威胁，那么无论多么大的危险，智者都相信他有权避免它。当讨论到国家生存的保障时，一个理智的人无疑会认为自己有义务为了国家的利益而冒着生命危险；他始终坚信，祖国需要他为之奋斗，无论他冒着多大的生命危险。”

(1) Variation in word choice means that one first formulates a thought and then expresses the same idea one or more times in different words, which however have the same meaning, as in the following example: “There is no danger so great that the wise man believes he has the right to avoid it, if the safety of the community is at stake.When discussing the safeguarding of the existence of the state, the sensible man will undoubtedly consider himself obliged to risk his own life for the good of the state; he will always maintain the opinion that the fatherland demands his dedicated struggle, however great the danger to his life he thereby exposes himself to.”

（2）传递方式的变化是通过在对话的语气、有力的声音以及不断变化着的语调和手势之间交替实现的，而同一想法的不同表述方式也通过传递方式的强调变化而相匹配。不可能以书面形式给出该过程的准确描述，但另一方面，这似乎足够清楚；因此不需要举例。

(2) Variation in delivery is achieved by alternating between a conversational tone, a powerful voice, and constantly new intonations and gestures, whereby the different formulations of the same idea are also matched by emphatic shifts in the way they are delivered.It is impossible to give in writing a precise description of the procedure, which on the other hand seems clear enough; therefore no example is needed.

55（3）第三种变化在于处理材料的方式，包括将思路设计成血清素或者以某种方式虔诚以激发强烈的情感。塞莫西尼奥我打算稍后在适当的地方更详细地讨论这个问题。76，现在我只会简要提及在这种情况下似乎足够的内容。形象的意思是把话放在别人嘴里，同时又要使之适合对方的立场。为了继续上一个主题并从而促进学习，我给出以下例子：“智者认为，为了国家的利益，他必须将自己暴露在各种危险之中。他常自言自语：我不仅为自己而生，更是为了国家而生。感谢命运，愿我的生命主要用于祖国的福祉。这个国家给了我食物，直到今天，它一直让我过着安全而有尊严的生活，它通过良好的法律和给予我光荣的成长环境来维护我的利益。我怎样才能回报这个国家给予我的一切呢？’明智的人越是经常对自己说这样的话，他就越是坚定决心，在国家陷入危险时，自己绝不会回避危险。”

55(3) The third type of variation, which lies in the way the material is treated, involves designing the line of thought either as asermocinatioor in a way that isdevotedto evoke strong emotions.SermocinatioI intend to discuss this in more detail later in the appropriate place.76, and right now I will only briefly mention what seems sufficient in this context.The figure means putting the words in someone else's mouth and at the same time adapting them to the person's position.To continue on the previous theme and thereby facilitate learning, I give the following example: “The wise man believes that he must expose himself to all kinds of dangers for the good of the state.He often says to himself: 'I was born not only for my own sake but also, and even more so, for the state's.May my life, for which I have fate to thank, be spent primarily for the welfare of my homeland.This country has given me food, it has always, to this day, allowed me to live in security and honor, it has safeguarded my interests through its good laws and by giving me an honorable upbringing.How can I repay all that this country has bestowed upon me?' The more often the wise man says this to himself, the more determined he becomes to never shy away from danger himself, when the state is in danger.”

通过选择一种能激发强烈情感的呈现方式，可以进一步实现处理事物方式的变化。虽然我们自己应该给人一种情感投入的印象，但我们可以通过以下方式影响听众，例如：“是否有人如此缺乏想象力和如此心胸狭窄，以至于他不把这个人捧上天，认为他是最聪明的人，他热切地接受并愉快地应对每一个危险，无论多么巨大和可怕，为了拯救祖国，为了社区的安全和国家的福祉？

Variation in the way a thing is treated is further achieved by choosing a presentation method that arouses strong emotions.While we should give the impression of being emotionally involved ourselves, we influence the listener in the following way, for example: “Is there anyone so unimaginative and so narrow-minded in his jealousy that he does not exalt this man to the skies and consider him the wisest of men, he who eagerly accepts and joyfully meets every danger, however great and terrible, for the salvation of the fatherland, for the security of the community and for the well-being of the state?

56就我而言，我对这个人的赞扬无法达到我想要的程度，而且我相信你们所有人也都一样。”

56For my part, I cannot praise this man as much as I would like, and I am convinced that the same is true of all of you.”

因此，当演讲者想要改变主题时，可以使用这三种方法：通过词语、表达方式和处理方式，将主题分解为血清素并激发强烈的情感。但谈论同一件事时，应该用多种不同的表达方式。因为当一个人（1）用简单的术语表达了这个想法时，他可以（2）给出一个理由，然后（3）用两种方式再次表述这个想法，即有理由或无理由，然后（4）提出相反的观点（所有这些我都在修辞手法部分讨论过）。77）。在此之后，人们可以（5）举一个明喻和（6）一个例子（我打算在专门为此目的而设的地方更详细地讨论这一点）。78)，之后是(7)结论（我在第二本书中已经进行了必要的讨论79，我展示了结束争论的正确方法；我在本书中阐明了“结论”这一修辞手法的含义。80）。这样，大量使用修辞手法和思维比喻的装饰，就能以极其有效的方式美化风格。

Thus, one has these three methods at one's disposal when one, as a speaker, wants to vary one's theme: through the words, the presentation, and the manner of treatment, whereby the latter breaks down intosermocinatioand arousing strong emotions.But when talking about the same thing, you should vary the expressions in many ways.For when one (1) has presented the idea in simple terms, one can (2) give a reason, then (3) formulate the idea again in two ways, namely with or without reason, and then (4) present the opposite (all of this I have dealt with in the section on figures of speech).77).After this, one can (5) cite a simile and (6) an example (I intend to treat this in more detail in the place intended for this purpose).78), after which follows (7) the conclusion (which I have discussed to the necessary extent in the second book79, where I showed the correct method of concluding arguments; the meaning of the figure of speech called conclusion I have clarified in the present book80).An ornamentation that makes extensive use of figures of speech and thought in this way can thus embellish the style in an extraordinarily effective way.

下面将对这种七段处理进行说明。我将举一个与前面主题相同的例子，以便您理解如何运用修辞规则轻松地以各种方式发展一个简单的想法：81

In the following, such a seven-section treatment will be illustrated.I will give an example with the same theme as before, so that you can understand how easily one can develop a simple idea in a variety of ways using the rules of rhetoric:81

57（1）“明智的人不会为了国家而回避任何危险。(2) 因为经常发生这样的情况：那些不想为国家牺牲的人却被迫与国家一起牺牲，而且，由于我们生命中一切美好的东西都来自祖国，所以我们不应该认为为祖国忍受任何苦难是一种负担。(3) 因此，那些为了国家利益而回避自己面临的危险的人的行为是不明智的。因为一方面他们无法摆脱邪恶，另一方面他们对国家忘恩负义。但另一方面，那些为了祖国的危险而牺牲自己的人，应该被认为是明智的，因为他们既尊重国家，又选择为广大公民而死，而不是与他们同归于尽。（4）这是最大的不公正复制当大自然迫使你为自然献出生命时，你却不肯为祖国献出生命，因为祖国赋予了你生命，而你的生命却由祖国保全了；宁愿选择不光彩和懦弱的生活，也不愿为祖国英勇而光荣地死去，这是最大的不公正，一方面为了朋友、父母和其他亲戚而将自己置于危险之中，另一方面却不愿为国家（包含这一切以及祖国的圣名）冒任何风险。（5）在航行中，如果有人将自己的安全置于船舶的安全之上，是应该受到鄙视的；同样，如果有人在国家面临危险的情况下，只考虑自己的安全而不考虑全体人民的共同得救，也是应该受到谴责的。因为船失事后，许多人可以毫发无损地上岸；但当祖国遭遇海难时，没有人能够游走自救。（6）在我看来，德西乌斯看到了82据说，他为了拯救自己的军团，将自己的一生奉献给了死亡，并投入到敌人之中。他失去了生命，但他没有浪费生命。他用极其不值钱的东西换来了珍贵的东西，用很少的钱得到了最高的利益。他牺牲了自己的生命，换来了祖国；他放弃了一切，赢得了一份不断受到赞扬、日益闪耀光辉的荣誉。（7）如果我已经部分地通过理性，部分地通过历史的例子表明，为了国家而不必回避危险是正确的，那么，那些为了拯救祖国而不回避任何危险的人就应该被视为明智的人。

57(1) “The wise man will not shy away from any danger for the sake of the state.(2) For it often happens that he who does not want to die for the state is nevertheless forced to die with the state, and since it is from the fatherland that we have received all the good things in life, we must not consider it a burden to endure any evil for the fatherland.(3) Those who shun the danger they face for the sake of the state, therefore, act unwisely.For on the one hand they cannot escape evil, and on the other hand they show themselves ungrateful to the state.But those who, on the other hand, face the dangers of their fatherland at the risk of themselves, should be considered wise, since they both pay due respect to the state and choose to die for the multitude of citizens rather than die with them.(4) For it is the greatest injustice toreproducelife to nature, when it forces you to do so, but refuse to give your life for your fatherland, when it asks you to, the life that you were given by nature but preserved thanks to your fatherland; it is the highest injustice to prefer a life of dishonor and cowardice to a brave and honorable death for your fatherland and to, on the one hand, expose yourself to danger for the sake of friends, parents and other relatives, but on the other hand, not want to risk anything for the state, which contains all this and, in addition, the holy name of the fatherland.(5) He who, during a voyage, prefers to look after his own safety more than that of the ship is worthy of contempt, and in the same way he is blameworthy who, in a situation dangerous to the state, thinks more of his own than of the common salvation of all.For after a shipwreck many can get ashore unharmed; but when the fatherland suffers shipwreck, no one can save himself by swimming away.(6) This, in my opinion, Decius saw82clear, who is said to have dedicated his life to death and thrown himself into the midst of the enemies to save his legions.He lost his life, but he did not waste it.At the price of something very worthless he won something precious, for a small sum he acquired the highest good.He sacrificed his life and received in exchange his fatherland; he gave up his spirit and won an honor that is constantly praised and shines with ever greater brilliance every day.(7) Now if I have shown, partly by reason, and partly by historical examples, that it is right not to avoid dangers for the sake of the state, then those must be considered wise who do not shun any danger for the sake of the salvation of their fatherland.”

58因此，人物的装饰就采用了这些手段。我之所以要花较长的篇幅来讨论这个比喻，是因为它不仅在人们在真实案例中辩论时赋予语言力量和美感，而且最重要的是，当人们希望改进自己的风格时，它是一种非常有用的练习。因此，建议在与真实案例无关的练习中实践修饰原则，并在真实演讲中使用它们来修饰论点，这是我在第二本书中讨论过的内容。83。

58It is thus these means that the figure's decoration uses.I have come to discuss this figure at comparatively great length, because it not only lends power and beauty to language when one argues in a real case, but above all is such a useful exercise when one wishes to improve one's style.It is therefore advisable to practice the principles of embellishment in exercises separate from authentic cases and to make use of them in real speech in the embellishment of an argument, something I have treated in the second book.83.

通信[commoratio] 意味着一个人在最有力的论点上停留很长时间，即支持整个演讲的论点，并一次又一次地回到这个论点上。这个数字极其有用，并且非常典型地代表了优秀的演讲者；它不给听众任何机会将注意力从最重要的证据上移开。我一直没能找到任何真正好的例子，因为所讨论的论点并不是像身体的一部分一样脱离整个演讲而孤立的，而是像血液一样流经整个演讲。

Commomtio[commoratio] means that one lingers for quite a long time on the strongest argument, the one that supports the entire speech, and returns to it again and again.This figure is extremely useful and very typical of the good speaker; it does not give the listener any opportunity to divert his attention from the most weighty evidence.I haven't been able to find any really good examples, because the argument in question is not isolated from the speech as a whole like a body part, but like blood flows through the entire body of the speech.

对立[contentio] 是一种可以表达对立面的修辞手法。正如我之前所说84，它是修辞手法之一，例如：“对你的敌人，你表现得和解，对你的朋友，你则毫不留情。”但它也可以是一种修辞手法，例如：“你为这个人的不幸而悲伤，而他却为国家的不幸而高兴。”你对自己的财产感到绝望，而只有这个人对自己的财产有更大的信心。”这两种对立的区别在于，前者是由快速形成的词语对立面组成，而后一种情况则应该是比较相反的想法。

Antithesis[contentio] is a figure that allows opposites to be expressed.As I said before84, it is one of the figures of speech according to the following example: “To your enemies you show yourself conciliatory, to your friends relentless.” But it can also be a figure of speech, e.g.: “You grieve over this man's misfortunes, while he rejoices over the state's misfortunes.You despair of your possessions, while this man alone has so much greater confidence in his own.” The difference between these two types of antithesis is that the former consists of quickly formulated verbal opposites, while in the latter case it should be opposing ideas that are compared.

59 寓言[similitudo] 是一种表示方法，其中将一个事物转移到另一个事物，使它们彼此相似。该图用于装饰风格，为了证据还有一件事清除或者说明性的。正如它有四种用途一样，它也以四种不同的方式表述：分别通过对比、否定、详细比较和简要比较。寓言的每个目的都应与特定的设计方法相结合。

59 Parable[similitudo] is a method of representation in which one transfers from one thing to another something in which they are similar to each other.This figure is used toadorn the style,forevidenceand to do one more thingclearorillustrative.Just as it is used for four purposes, it is also formulated in four different ways: through contrast, negation, detailed and abbreviated comparison, respectively.Each purpose for a parable should be combined with a specific design method.

（1）如果要修饰风格，可以按照这个例子将人物设计成反面：“因为与赛道上的情况不同，接过燃烧的火炬的接力赛跑者比交接火炬的人跑得更快，而接过军队指挥权的新指挥官并不比交接火炬的人更好。因为在前一种情况下，疲惫的信使将火炬交给休息好的信使，而在后一种情况下，经验丰富的将军将军队交给缺乏经验的将军。”不用寓言，也可以非常简单、清楚、可信地表达这一点，例如例如“常言道，能将善将接替能将统帅军队的往往是能力较弱的将领”，但刚才这个比喻，是为了修饰文体，增加语言美感，在形式上是一种对比。因为类比是以对比的形式出现的，用来反驳人们想要证明的事物与其他事物的相似性。

(1) If you want to embellish the style, you can design the figure as an opposite according to this example: “For unlike what is the case on the racetrack, where the relay runner who takes over the burning torch runs faster than the one who hands it over, the new commander who takes over the command of an army is no better than the one who hands it over.For while in the former case it is a weary runner who hands over the torch to a rested one, in the latter it is a question of an experienced general handing over the army to an inexperienced one.” Without a simile, this could have been said very simply, clearly and believably, e.g.in the following way: “It is said that it is usually less capable generals who take over the command of armies from more capable ones”, but the simile just now serves the purpose of embellishing the style, of increasing the linguistic beauty, and in terms of form it was presented as a contrast.For analogy in the form of contrast is used to dispute that what one wants to prove is similar to something else.

（2）否定句可用于证明某事，如以下例子：“一匹未驯服的马，无论生性多么好，都不适合做人们希望马做的事情；同样，一个未受过教育的人，无论多么有天赋，也不能拥有美德。” “不经过训练就无法获得美德”这一说法似乎更有说服力，因为即使是马，如果不被驯服，也不会有任何用处。因此，明喻的目的是为了证明，而其形式则是否定。从寓言中的第一个词就可以看出这一事实。

(2) A negation can be used to prove something, as in the following example: “An untamed horse, however well-built by nature, is not fit for the services one wants a horse to perform; in the same way, an unlearned man, however gifted, cannot come into possession of virtue.” The claim that virtue cannot be acquired without training appears all the more convincing, since even a horse cannot be of any use until it has been tamed.The purpose of the parable is thus proof, and its form is negation; that fact is already evident from the first word in the parable.

60(3) 明喻也可用于使意思更清楚，下面的例子显示了如何将其表述为一个简短的比较：“在友谊中，就像在比赛中一样，一个人不能将自己的努力局限于达到规定的目标：一个人必须竭尽全力，才能轻松地跑得更远。”因为这个寓言的意义在于，人们应该更加清楚地认识到，责怪那些人是多么不公平，例如，在朋友死后，把他的孩子置于他们的保护之下：跑步者必须跑得非常快，而朋友必须怀有极大的善意，他们才能凭借速度跑过终点线。明喻的形式是比较的简化形式，因为被比较的事物并不像其他情况下那样彼此分离，而是在呈现过程中统一和融合在一起。

60(3) The simile can also be used to make something clearer, and the following example shows how it can be formulated as a shortened comparison: “In a friendship, as in a race, one must not let one’s efforts be limited to reaching the prescribed goal: one must strain one’s will and strength so much that one can easily run further than that.” For the meaning of this simile is that one should realize more clearly how unjustified it is to blame those who, for example, after the death of a friend, take his children under their protection: a runner must run so fast and a friend must feel such great goodwill that they simply run past the goal.The form of the simile is the abbreviated form of comparison, for the things being compared are not, as in other cases, separate from each other, but both have been united and fused together in the presentation.

(4) 为了使事情更清楚，可以按照下面的例子，将明喻作为详细的比较：“想象一位琴手走上前来，他衣着精美，身穿金色绣花长袍，紫色长袍上绣有各种颜色的花，头上戴着一个大王冠，上面装饰着闪闪发光的大宝石。他手里拿着一把罕见而美丽的七弦琴，琴上装饰着黄金和象牙。他本人也非常英俊，体格也更加凸显了他的美貌。如果他现在在观众中引起了很大的期望之后，突然用可怕的尖锐声音打破沉默，并伴有令人厌恶的身体动作，那么他就会遭到嘲笑和蔑视，而这种蔑视与他美丽的装扮和对他的期望成正比。同样，对于那些拥有崇高社会地位、拥有巨大物质财富、拥有命运和自然赋予人类的一切天赋的人来说，如果他缺乏美德，他就会被排除在正直人士之外，他越富有、越有名、人们对他的期望越高，他受到的嘲笑和鄙视也就越大。”在这个寓言中，双方都被渲染了，通过对比一方的无能和另一方在相似方面的愚蠢，达到了一种人人皆知的描述效果。这里的形式是详细比较，因为一旦建立了相似性，每个元素就会与其他元素相关。

(4) To make a thing more clear, one can formulate a simile as a detailed comparison according to the following example: “Imagine a lyre player who comes forward exquisitely dressed, with a gold-embroidered robe, a purple robe with embroidery in various colors, and a large crown on his head adorned with large, shining precious stones.In his hand he holds a rare and beautiful lyre adorned with gold and ivory.He is also very handsome himself and has a physique that emphasizes his beauty.If he now, after having thus created great expectations in the audience, suddenly breaks the silence with a hideously shrill voice, accompanied by repulsive body movements, he is thrown out amid mockery and with a contempt that is directly proportional to his beautiful attire and to the expectations placed upon him.The same is true of the one who has a high social position, possesses great material wealth, and is abundantly endowed with all the gifts that fate and nature can bestow on a human being: if he lacks virtue, he is excluded from all association with men of integrity, and he is mocked and despised all the more intensely, the richer and more famous he is, and the greater the expectations he has.” In this simile, both sides have been embellished, and by comparing the incompetence of the one with the folly of the other under a similar aspect, the result is a depiction that is clear to all.The form here is that of detailed comparison, as each element is related to something else, once the similarity has been established.

61使用明喻时，必须密切注意确保词语的选择强调与构成明喻基础的其他事物的相似性。以下可以作为一个例子：“就像燕子在夏天陪伴我们，但被寒冷赶走了……”从同一个明喻中，我们现在可以得出一个比喻的素材：“同样，虚假的朋友在我们生命中阳光明媚的日子里陪伴着我们，但一旦他们看到我们的幸福受到冬天的威胁，他们就会飞走。”然而，如果人们能够养成在内心想象各种事物的习惯，这些事物有的有生命的，有的无生命的，有哑巴的，有话的，有野生的，有驯服的，有属于地球的、在天空的或是在海洋中的，由人类创造的，偶然的或自然的，常见的或不寻常的，并在这些事物中寻找一些可以修饰、证明或使某事变得清晰明显的明喻，那么找到明喻就会变得更容易。并不是说事物之间在所有细节上都需要有相似性，但是作为比较的对象必须具有相似性。

61When using similes, one must pay close attention to ensuring that the choice of words emphasizes the similarity to something else that forms the basis of the simile.The following can serve as an example: “Just as the swallows keep us company in summer but are driven away by the cold…” From the same simile we now draw material for a metaphor: “In the same way false friends keep us company during the sunny days of our lives, but as soon as they see that our happiness is threatened by winter, they all fly away.” However, it becomes easier to find similes if one can get into the habit of imagining before one’s inner gaze all kinds of things, living and inanimate, mute and speaking, wild and tame, belonging to the earth, in the sky or in the sea, created by human hands, chance or nature, ordinary and unusual, and go in search of some simile among these things that can embellish, prove or make something clear and evident.Not that there needs to be similarity between things in all particulars, but that which is the subject of comparison must have similarity.

62 例子[exemplum] 意思是重现过去的行为或陈述，并明确提及作者。这个数字与寓言的用途相同。它使某物光彩夺目，而其目的仅仅是为了美观；它通过阐明那些看起来有些模糊的事物来创造清晰度；它通过使某事更有可能发生来增加可信度；它把某种东西生动地呈现在我们眼前，让人感觉仿佛可以用手抓住它。如果我没有展示与图形装饰相关的例子，我就会给出每个用途的例子。85并解释了为什么在明喻部分使用例子86。因此，我既不想让我的演讲太短而无法被理解，也不想让我的演讲太长而无法被理解。

62 Example[exemplum] means reproducing an action or statement from the past with explicit mention of the author.This figure is used for the same purposes as the parable.It gives something shine, when the purpose is nothing more than the beautiful formulation itself; it creates clarity by shedding light on what seems somewhat obscure; it increases credibility by making something more probable; it places something before our eyes by expressing it so vividly that one almost feels like one can grasp it with one's hand.I would have given examples of each of these uses, if I had not shown what examples are in connection with figure ornamentation.85and explained why examples are used in the section on simile86I have therefore neither wanted to make my presentation too short to be understood nor unnecessarily long, once it has been understood.

图像[imago] 表示将一幅图像与另一幅图像放在一起，因为有某种相似性。它既可以用来赞扬，也可以用来责备。赞美的例子：“他以最强壮的公牛般的体魄和最野蛮的狮子般的凶猛投入战斗。”旨在煽动仇恨的指控示例：“这个恶棍，每天像一条背上有冠的蛇一样在广场中央爬行，长着歪斜的牙齿，目光毒辣，气喘吁吁，四处张望，寻找可以向其吐露邪恶的人，用嘴唇涂抹，用牙齿接种，用舌头撒播。”下面的例子展示了这个比喻是如何引起嫉妒的：“这个人，身上带着沉重的黄金，夸耀着他的财富，像库柏勒的弗里吉亚祭司一样大喊大叫。”87或者作为某种算命先生。”引起蔑视：“这个人就像蜗牛一样静静地躲在壳里，被带走，连房子一起被吞噬。”

Image[imago] means that an image is put together with another image, because there is some similarity.It is used either to praise or to blame.Example of praise: “He entered the battle with a body like the strongest bull and with a ferocity like the wildest lion.” Example of blame with the intention of provoking hatred: “This wretch, who daily creeps about the middle of the Forum like a serpent with a crest on his back, with crooked teeth, a poisonous look, panting wildly, looking in all directions to find someone on whom he can breathe his evil, smear it with his lips, inoculate it with his teeth and sprinkle it around with his tongue.” The following example shows how the figure is used to arouse envy: “This man, who, weighed down and overloaded with gold, boasts of his wealth, shouts and raves like a Phrygian priest of Cybele87or as some kind of fortune teller.” To evoke contempt: “This man, who like a snail quietly keeps hidden in his shell, is carried away to be devoured with house and all.”

63 肖像[effictio] 是指用语言非常详细地呈现和描述某人的外貌，让人一目了然地知道他指的是谁，例如：“这位先生，法庭上的先生们，我指的是那个面色红润、身材矮小、驼背、有着白色略微卷曲的头发、蓝灰色眼睛、下巴上有一道大疤痕的男子，如果你们还记得的话。”当您想要单独突出某人时，这个数字非常有用，并且如果它简短而清晰，还可以为风格增添魅力。

63 Portrait[effictio] means that one presents and depicts someone's appearance in words in such detail that it is clear who is being referred to, according to the following example: "This man, gentlemen of the court, I mean the reddish, short and stooped man with white and slightly curly hair, blue-gray eyes and a large scar on his chin, if you can possibly remember him." This figure is very useful when you want to point out someone, and also adds charm to the style if it is short and clear.

词源[notatio] 用某些特定符号来描述某人的性格，这些符号构成了该人的特征。如果你想描述一个并不富有但却想给人留下富有印象的人，你可以这样说：

Etymology[notatio] consists of describing someone's personality by using certain specific signs, which constitute characteristic traits of the person in question.If you want to describe a person who is not rich but wants to give the impression of being so, you could say something like this:

“陪审团的先生们，这个人认为自己被称为富人是件非常了不起的事，现在请首先观察他给我们的眼神。你难道没有感觉到他在说：“我很乐意给你一分钱88，如果你不让我这么无聊的话？当他用左手托着下巴坐着时，他认为他闪亮的宝石和闪耀的金子让每个人都眼花缭乱。当他在这里称呼他的奴隶时——他是他唯一的奴隶，因为我认识他，而我假设你不认识——他用不断变化的名字来称呼他。“你好”，他说，“过来，桑尼奥，确保那些野蛮人不会做任何恶作剧”，以免不知情的听众认为他在向众多奴隶中的一个说话。他悄悄地告诉他，要整理一下家里的餐厅，或者向叔叔借一只埃塞俄比亚马去澡堂当看门人，或者把他的阿斯图里亚斯纯种马放在他家门口，或者安排一些其他无意义的事情用具：因为他的自负。然后他大声喊道：“一定要仔细清点钱，如果可能的话，争取在天黑前完成！”奴隶现在已经很了解主人的性格了，他回答说：“如果你想让我们今天完成清点，你必须派几个奴隶来做这项任务。” – “放手吧，”他说道，“带上黎巴嫩和索西亚。” – “是的，先生。”这时，这名男子碰巧遇到了一些外国人，他们是他在国外旅行时认识的，于是他邀请了他们，并承诺会给他们一个盛大的招待会。这种情况自然让他非常困惑，但他还是按照自己撒谎的本性说道：“你能来拜访真是太好了！”但如果你直接去我家就更好了。” – “如果我们有地址，我们也会这么做的，”他们回答道。 –“那又怎么样？”您可能很容易从任何人那里得到它！但现在跟我来吧。’他们跟着他。与此同时，该男子还在不停地吹嘘。他询问田里的庄稼长势如何，他解释说他自己的农场被烧毁了，因此他无法去看望他们；他仍然不敢重建它们。“但在我位于塔斯库卢姆的庄园里89我已经开始做一些完全疯狂的事情——我打算在同样的基础上继续发展！’

“This man, gentlemen of the jury, who thinks it is particularly remarkable to be called rich, now observe first of all the look he gives us.Don't you get the impression that he's saying: 'I'd be happy to give you a penny88, if you didn't bore me so much?And when he sits with his chin propped on his left hand, he thinks he's blinding everyone with his shiny gems and glittering gold.When he addresses his slave here – his only one, because I know him, which I assume you don't – he addresses him with ever-changing names.'Hello there', he says, 'come here, Sannio, make sure those barbarians don't do any mischief', lest unknowing listeners think he is addressing one of many slaves.He whispers to him to tidy up the dining room at home, or to ask to borrow an Ethiopian from his uncle to be a caretaker in the bathhouse, or to place his Asturian thoroughbred in front of the entrance to his house, or to arrange some other pointlessparaphernalia:for his conceit.Then he shouts for everyone to hear: 'Make sure the money is counted carefully, and if possible try to finish before night!' The slave, who is by now well acquainted with his master's character, replies: 'You must assign several slaves to that task, if you want us to finish counting today.' - 'Let go,' he says, 'take Libanus and Sosia with you.' - 'Yes, master.' Then the man happens to come across some foreigners, whom he had met during a foreign trip and then invited, promising them a grand reception.The situation naturally makes him extremely confused, but true to his lying nature, he says: 'So nice of you to come visit!But it would have been better if you had gone straight to my house.' – 'We would have done that too,' they reply, 'if we had only had the address.' – 'So what?You could have easily gotten it from anyone!But come with me now.' They follow him.Meanwhile, the man boasts incessantly.He asks how the crops are in the fields, he explains that his own farms have burned down and that he cannot visit them; he does not yet dare to rebuild them.'But on my estate in Tusculum89I've started something completely crazy – I intend to build on the same foundations!'

64正说着，他突然站在一户人家门前，当天，这户人家正在举办宴会。由于他碰巧认识这所房子的主人，所以他和客人一起进去了。“我住在这里，”他说。他检查了拿出的银器，检查了准备好的桌子沙发并表示赞同。一名奴隶男孩出现了。这只狗大声而清晰地告诉那名男子，他的主人很快就要回家了，并请他离开。'真的吗？'然后他回答。“走吧，我的朋友们，我哥哥从法勒尼亚庄园回来了90，我打算见见他。四点钟回来！’客人离去；男人飞速地冲回家。但四点钟其他人就到达了指定地点。他们询问主人，被告知房子的主人是谁，遭到嘲笑，然后住进了一家客栈。第二天，他们见到了那个男人，告诉他发生的事情，道歉，并追究他的责任。他回答说，他们被这些地方的相似性所误导，走错了整条街；他自己虽然身体不太舒服，但还是“熬夜”了。事实上，他已经指示他的奴隶桑尼奥去借用器皿、桌布和奴隶，这个敏捷的奴隶男孩敏捷而心甘情愿地完成了这项任务。男人把客人带到他家；他宣布将自己最大的房子借给了一位正在举办婚礼的朋友。奴隶报告说要求归还银子；主人开始怀疑有什么不对劲。'离开！'他的主人回答道。“你把你的房子和奴隶借给他——他也想要我的银子吗？不过不管怎样，就算我家里有客人，他也可以借银子。我们可以选择来自萨摩斯岛的船只91'。'是的，我告诉你他的其他奇思妙想还有什么意义吗？这个人的性格就是这样，如果我要描述他一天之内​​说的那些废话和吹牛，那么一年也不够。”

64During all this talking, he suddenly stands in front of a house, where a party is holding a banquet that same day.Since he happens to know the owner of the house, he goes in with his guests.'I live here,' he says.He examines the silverware that has been brought out, he inspects the prepared table sofas and expresses his approval.A slave boy appears.This one tells the man loudly and clearly that his master will soon be home and asks him to leave.'Really?' he then replies.'Let us go, my friends, my brother has come home from his Falernian estate90, and I intend to meet him.Come back here at four o'clock!' The guests leave; the man rushes home at full speed.But at four o'clock the others arrive at the designated place.They ask for their host, are told who owns the house, are laughed at, and take in an inn.The next day they meet the man, tell him what happened, apologize, and hold him accountable.He replies that they were fooled by the similarity between the places and took the wrong turn on a whole street; he himself, despite not feeling very well, had 'waited up until late into the night'.In fact, he had instructed his slave Sannio to borrow vessels, tablecloths, and slaves, a task that the nimble slave boy had completed nimbly and willingly.The man takes his guests to his home; he announces that he has lent his largest house to a friend who is holding a wedding.The slave reports that the silver is being demanded back; the owner has begun to suspect mischief.‘Go away!’ his master replies.'Here you lend him your house and your slaves – does he want my silver too?But by all means, even if I have guests at home, he can borrow the silver then.We can settle for vessels from Samos91.' Well, is there any point in me telling you about his other whims?The man's character is such that a whole year wouldn't be enough if I wanted to describe all the blabbering and boasting he manages to do in a single day."

65通过这个形象，我们可以描述出每个人的性格特征，它给演示带来了极大的乐趣，因为它展示了一个人的全部性格，无论是自夸者（我刚刚开始举例说明），嫉妒者，膨胀者，贪婪者，野心家，情人，性感者，小偷还是告密者。简单来说，通过这个人物形象，可以体现出每个人最突出的性格特征。

65This figure, with the help of which one can describe what is typical of each individual personality, gives the presentation great pleasure, since it illustrates the entire character of an individual, whether it concerns the boaster, as I have just begun to exemplify, the envious, the inflated, the greedy, the ambitious, the lover, the voluptuous, the thief or the informer.In short, one can bring out each person's most prominent character traits through this figure.

塞莫西尼奥92[sermocinatio] 意味着将一段话放到某人的口中，并选择能体现其性格的话，如下例所示：“当城市里挤满了士兵，每个人都惊恐万分，都待在家里的时候，这个人来了，他穿着野战斗篷，手里拿着剑和长矛；陪同他的还有三个装备相同的年轻人。突然，他冲进屋子，大声喊道：“我们好房东呢？他为什么不来接我？你为什么保持沉默？’在场的所有人都惊恐得说不出话来。这个不幸男人的妻子突然泪流满面，扑倒在这个可怜人的脚下。“我恳求您，以您生命中最珍贵的东西的名义，可怜可怜我们吧！不要去毁灭那些已经被毁灭的人，温柔地利用你的地位！我们也曾被幸运眷顾；记住你是人！’ – “立刻把他带过来，别再哭得我耳朵难受了！”他不会逃跑的！’与此同时，房主得知该男子已经到来，大声尖叫，威胁要杀死他。得知这个消息后，他立即对负责照看孩子的奴隶说：“戈尔吉亚，听着，把孩子们藏起来，保护他们，确保这些年轻人安全！”他话音未落，恶棍就站在那里说道：“好吧，你竟然厚着脸皮留在这里？”我的声音难道没有把你吓坏吗？现在你将用你的血来满足我的仇恨并平息我的愤怒！’但房子的主人保持冷静，回答道：“我担心我彻底被打败了。现在我明白了。你不会想在法庭上与我较量实力吧，在那里失败是一种耻辱，胜利是一种荣誉；你想杀人。让我被杀吧；我不会输而死！’ –‘想象一下，在你生命的最后一刻，你也在说格言！现在你的生命掌握在我手中，你难道不向我求饶吗？’这时妻子插话道：“是的，他在向你乞求，但请你饶恕我吧，我打扰到你了！”而你，以众神的名义，跪倒在他的脚下，拥抱他！他是你的霸主，他打败了你，现在你必须打败你自己！’ – “老婆，别说了，别说那些有损我尊严的话！”男人回答道。闭嘴，然后拍摄你自己的。但是你，你却迟迟不肯通过我的死亡剥夺我的生命，剥夺你自己过上好日子的希望？’入侵者推开了哭泣的女人，正当男人要说出一些符合男子气概的话时，恶棍将剑刺入了他的胸膛。

Sermocinatio92[sermocinatio] means that a speech is put into the mouth of a certain person and chosen so that it shows his character, according to the following example: “When the city was flooded with soldiers and everyone, struck with fear, stayed at home, this man came, wearing a field cloak, armed with a sword and with a spear in his hand; he was accompanied by three young men equipped in the same way.Suddenly he burst into the house, after which he shouted loudly: 'Where is our fine landlord?Why didn't he come and receive me?Why are you silent?' Everyone present was speechless with horror.The wife of the unfortunate man burst into tears and threw herself at the wretch's feet.'I beg you, by the dearest thing you have in life, to have mercy on us!Do not destroy those who have already been destroyed, use your position with gentleness!We too have once been favored by fortune; remember that you are human!' – 'Get him at once and stop tormenting my ears with your crying!He won't get away!' Meanwhile, the owner of the house learns that the man has arrived and, shouting loudly, threatens to kill him.Immediately after receiving this news, he says to the slave who is in charge of the children: ‘Gorgias, listen, hide the children, defend them and see that the young people get to safety!’ He has hardly had time to say this before the villain stands there and says: ‘Well, you are insolent enough to stay here?Didn't my voice scare the life out of you?Now you will satisfy my hatred and quench my anger with your blood!' But with preserved calm the master of the house replies: 'I feared that I was completely defeated.Now I see how it is.You do not want to measure your strength with me in court, where defeat is a shame and victory an honor; you want to kill.Let me not be killed; I will not die defeated!' – 'Imagine that in your last moments you too speak in maxims!Won't you ask me for mercy, now that I have your life in my hands?' Here the wife intervenes: 'Yes, he is begging and pleading with you, but please show me mercy, I am bothering you!And you, by all the gods, fall at his feet and embrace him!He is your superior, he has defeated you, now you must defeat yourself!' – 'Stop, wife,' the man replies, 'saying things that are beneath my dignity!Shut up and shoot yours.But you, you delay in depriving me of life and yourself, through my death, of all hope of a good life?’ The intruder pushed the weeping woman away, and just as the man was about to utter something that was certainly worthy of his manhood, the villain buried the sword in his chest.”

我的意思是，这个例子为每个人提供了一种表达自我的方式，反映了他们的心态，这就是人们必须在这个图中观察到的。变体血清素是以下类型的虚假答案：“如果这是你的判断，我们认为这些人会说什么？他们不是都会说下面这句话吗？”然后你就说出你认为他们想说的话。

I mean, this example gives each person a way of expressing themselves that reflects their mentality, which is what one has to observe in this figure.A variant ofsermocinatiois the feigned answer of the following type: “For what shall we think these men will say, if this be your judgment?Won't they all say the following?", after which you say what you think they want to say.

66 拟人诗[conformatio] 是将一个不存在的人呈现为存在的形象，或者让一个哑巴或无形的物体说话，从而赋予它一种形式、一种语言和一种适合其声誉的行为方式，例如如下：“但是，如果这座坚不可摧的城市本身会说话，它难道不会说以下的话吗？“我曾被无数的胜利标志所装饰，通过最令人信服的胜利获得了财富，在辉煌的胜利之后我的国库充满了财富，但是现在，公民们啊，我却因你们的不和而受到伤害。这座城市既不能被狡猾邪恶的迦太基人、久经考验的努曼西亚人、也不能被在艺术和科学方面处于领先地位的科林斯人所动摇，93你是否发现这座城市正被最坏的人践踏和摧毁？”或者：“但如果伟大的卢修斯·布鲁图斯94如果他再次复活并出现在你们面前，他会不会说出下面的话？“我赶走了国王，你们面对的是暴君。我创造了一种不存在的自由，你们却不想维护所创造的自由。我冒着生命危险解放了祖国，你们即使没有危险也不在乎自由。”这个比喻可以适用于各种各样的东西，无论是沉默的还是无生命的。与刺绣和恳求同情相结合尤其有效。95。

66 Prosopoeia[conformatio] is the figure in which a non-present person is presented as present, or when a mute or formless object is made to speak, thereby giving it a form, a language and a way of behaving that are adapted to its reputation, e.g.as follows: “But if this invincible city itself were to speak, would it not say the following?'I, who have been adorned with countless signs of victory, who have obtained riches through the most convincing triumphs, and who have had my treasuries filled after brilliant victories, I am now wounded, O citizens, by your discord.The city that could not be shaken by either the cunning and wicked Carthage, the well-tried Numantia, or the high-ranking Corinth in arts and sciences,93Do you now find that city being trampled and crushed by the worst kind of people imaginable?” Or: “But if the great Lucius Brutus94were to rise again and appear before you here, would he not utter the following words?'I drove out kings, you faced tyrants.I created a freedom that did not exist, you do not want to maintain the freedom that was created.I liberated the fatherland at the risk of my own life, you don't care about being free even without danger.'” This figure can be applied to a variety of things, both mute and inanimate.It is especially effective in conjunction with embroideries and pleas for compassion.95.

67 强调[significatio] 是一种修辞手法，它所暗示的意思比话语中实际表达的内容更多。该图形的形状为夸张[优势]，歧义[模糊的]，后果的迹象[结果]，隐匿性[脱落]和类比[相似]。

67 Emphasis[significatio] is a figure of speech that suggests more than what is actually stated in an utterance.The figure has the shape ofhyperbole[superiority],ambiguity[ambiguous],indication of consequence[consequences],aposiopesis[abscission]and analogy[similarity].

（1）夸张是指说出比事实更多的内容，以引起怀疑，例如：“他继承了这么大的遗产，却在这么短的时间内连一个陶器都没有留下。”96把火带进来。”

(1) Hyperbole is the act of saying more than the truth allows, with the intention of inciting suspicion, e.g.: “Of such a large inheritance, after such a short time he does not even have a clay vessel left.”96to fetch fire in.”

（2）歧义性是指一个词可以有两种或两种以上的方式解释，但最终只能按照说话者希望的方式来理解。例如，一个继承了几份遗产的人说：“你平时照顾自己，过得还算不错！”我们应该避免模糊风格的歧义，并努力创造这种强调。如果您了解并注意单词的双重或多重含义，您就可以轻松地想出它们。

(2) Ambiguity means that a word that can be interpreted in two or more ways is nevertheless only perceived in the way the speaker wishes, as when one says of someone who has received several inheritances: “Watch out, you who usually provide for yourself so well!” One should both avoid such ambiguities that obscure the style, and strive for those that create this kind of emphasis.You can easily come up with them if you know and pay attention to the double or multiple meanings of words.

（3）通过陈述后果来强调某一特定情况的后果，以便推断出整个上下文，例如如果有人对一个鱼贩的儿子说：“闭嘴，你这个曾经用胳膊肘擤鼻涕的人的儿子！”

(3) Emphasis through the statement of consequence occurs when one mentions the consequences of a certain circumstance that allows one to infer the entire context, e.g.if one were to say to a fishmonger's son: "Shut up, you son of someone who used to pick your nose in your elbow!"

（4）通过省略来强调97意思是某人刚开始说某事，然后突然停下来，而之前说过的话足以引起怀疑，例如：“他凭借他的美貌和青春刚刚进入别人的家——我不想再多说了。”

(4) Emphasis through aposiopesis97means that one first starts to say something but then abruptly stops, whereby what has already been said is enough to arouse suspicion, e.g.: “He who with his beauty and his youth has just been in another's house – I don't want to say more.”

（5）通过类比，如果一个人满足于陈述类似的事情，但由此阐明了自己的意思，那么他就可以强调地表达自己，例如：“不要太相信，萨图尔尼努斯98，在人群中——格拉古兄弟未受报复的谎言99杀。”

(5) By analogy one expresses oneself emphatically, if one is content with stating something similar but thereby clarifies what one means, e.g.: “Do not trust too much, Saturninus98, on the crowd – unavenged lie the Gracchi99kill."

这种形象往往蕴含着丰富的风格优雅和美感。它允许听众在说话者保持沉默的情况下自己得出某些结论。

This figure often contains a great deal of stylistic elegance and beauty.It allows the listener to draw certain conclusions themselves while the speaker remains silent.

68 简洁[brevitas] 意味着只使用必要的最少的词语来表达一个想法，例如：“在途中，他占领了利姆诺斯岛，然后在萨索斯岛留下了驻军，然后摧毁了维米纳西姆城，从那里返回赫勒斯滂海峡并立即占领了阿拜多斯。”或者：“在此之前，他担任过执政官，然后是国家最重要的人物；然后他去了亚洲，然后被宣布为敌人；然后他成为总司令，最后第七次担任执政官。”100”这种修辞手法能够在简短的短语框架内表达很多内容，因此应该经常使用，无论是当事情不需要长篇大论解释或时间不允许详细讨论时。

68 Brevity[brevitas] means expressing a thought using only the necessary minimum of words, e.g.: “On the way he captured Lemnos, then he left a garrison on Thasos, then he destroyed the city of Viminacium, returned from there to the Hellespont and immediately captured Abydos.” Or: “Just before that he was consul, then he was the foremost in the state; then he went to Asia, then he was declared an enemy; then he became commander-in-chief and finally consul for the seventh time.”100.” This figure of speech is able to express a multitude of things within the framework of a short phrase and should therefore be used often, either when the matter does not require a long explanation or when time does not allow for dwelling on it.

证据[demonstratio] 是一种用语言表达某事物的修辞手法，让人仿佛看到动作的展开和事物呈现在眼前。如果把事件发生之前、之后和期间的情况都包括进去，或者按照以下例子详细论述后果或情况，就可以做到这一点：“格拉古一看到人民因为害怕参议院的决定会让他改变主意而动摇，他就召集了人民议会。与此同时，这个恶棍怀着邪恶和犯罪的计划匆匆逃离了朱庇特神庙。他大汗淋漓，眼睛火辣辣的，头发竖起，长袍凌乱不堪，他加快了脚步，身边还有几个人跟着他。当传令官要求格拉古保持沉默时，这个疯子用脚踢了一张长凳，打断了一条腿，并命令其他人也这样做。当格拉古开始向神祈祷时，这些恶棍就发起了攻击。他们从四面八方跑来。这时，其中一人大喊：“快逃，提比略，快逃！”你没看见吗？转过身来，你没听到吗！’然后，原本不稳定的人群突然感到恐惧，四处逃窜。但这个疯子，嘴里邪恶地吐着白沫，从肺腑深处发出残忍的气息，举起手臂，在圣殿里击打格拉古，格拉古不知道发生了什么事，但仍然站在原地。他毫无保留地展现出他与生俱来的男子气概，静静地倒下了。杀害他的凶手身上洒满了英雄可怜的鲜血，环顾四周，仿佛完成了一项辉煌的壮举，高兴地向那些祝贺他的人伸出沾满罪行的手，走向朱庇特的神庙。101
